201 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. State


No. 78,337


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 648; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1145; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 347



July 13, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 22, 1995. Released for Publication September 22, 1995.
Writ of certiorari denied Johnson v. Florida, 517 U.S. 1159, 116 S. Ct. 1550, 134 L. Ed. 2d 653, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 2740 (1996)
Post-conviction relief denied at Johnson v. State, 104 So. 3d 1032, 2012 Fla. LEXIS 2275 (Fla., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Sarasota County, Andrew Owens, Judge - Case Nos. 88-3200-CF-A-N1 88-3438-CF-A-N1.
Johnson v. State, 660 So. 2d 637, 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1144 (Fla., 1995)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment and sentence of the Circuit Court in and for Sarasota County (Florida), which imposed the death penalty after trial on charges of first-degree murder and armed burglary.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his convictions for first-degree murder and armed burglary, and he also challenged the imposition of the death penalty. Appellant raised numerous errors, including that the arrest warrant was defective and his confessions should have been suppressed. The court held that the omissions from the affidavit in question were not material because they could not possibly have altered the probable cause finding. All of the omissions were de minimis at best and in no sense vitiated probable cause. The court found that the arrest, at a minimum, was supported by probable cause under the fellow-officer rule and that appellant's statements and confession were lawful. The court held that appellant's statement that he would rather receive a shot than die in the electric chair was made voluntarily and spontaneously, not as part of custodial interrogation. Accordingly, there was no error in the failure to suppress it. Further, the court found that appellant's confession elaborating details of the murder and identifying the location of a murder weapon was properly admitted because appellant had fully waived his right to be represented by counsel at the time of the confession.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's first-degree murder and armed burglary convictions, as well as the sentences imposed. The court held that omissions from the probable cause affidavit for the arrest warrant were immaterial and did not vitiate probable cause. Further, there was no suggestion of reckless or intentional disregard of the truth. The court also held that all the confessions made by appellant were lawful and not subject to suppression.

 

202 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Pangburn v. State


No. 81,650


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


661 So. 2d 1182; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1122; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 323



July 6, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 25, 1995. Released for Publication October 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Paul L. Backman, Judge - Case No. 90-14442CF10-B.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Raising five issues regarding the guilt phase and 12 issues regarding the penalty phase, appellant sought review of his convictions and sentences for robbery and two counts of first-degree murder, including his sentence of death for one murder convictions, from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his brother were charged with the murders of two women. The jury found appellant guilty of the first-degree murder and robbery. A penalty phase proceeding was conducted, and the jury returned a recommendation for the death penalty. Subsequent to the penalty phase proceeding, the trial judge discovered that the jury had not been given separate jury forms to enable it to make separate recommendations as to each of the murders. The parties stipulated that the jury's recommendation would be accepted as one of death for one murder and one of life imprisonment for the other. Before appellant was sentenced, however, he attempted to withdraw his consent to the stipulation, but the trial judge refused to allow him to do so. On appeal, appellant raised five issues regarding the guilt phase and 12 issues regarding the penalty phase. However, the court affirmed the convictions for robbery and murder, but reversed his sentences for the murder convictions. In reversing the sentences, the court found that the trial judge should have granted appellant's request to withdraw under the liberal standard used.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions and his sentence of life imprisonment for the robbery conviction were affirmed, but his sentences for the murder convictions were reversed and remanded for a new penalty phase because the trial judge should have granted appellant's request to withdraw his consent to a stipulation that the jury's recommendation would be accepted.

 

203 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


B.B. v. State


No. 83,712


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


659 So. 2d 256; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1063



June 29, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 24, 1995. Released for Publication August 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case No. 93-02903 (Pinellas County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a minor, sought review of the decision from the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) that reversed the order of the trial court granting petitioner's motion to dismiss the petition charging him with unlawful carnal intercourse with a minor in violation of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 794.05 (1991), and that certified the question of whether that statute violated the privacy provision of Fla. Const. art. I, § 23.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a 16-year-old minor, was charged with unlawful carnal intercourse with a 16-year-old minor in violation of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 794.05 (1991). The trial court found that the statute violated petitioner's state constitutional privacy rights and granted petitioner's motion to dismiss the delinquency petition. The appellate court reversed the dismissal. Upon certification on the question of the constitutionality of the statute, the court held that petitioner's status as a minor did not deprive him of his privacy rights under Fla. Const. art. I, § 23. The court held that because the purpose of § 794.05 was to further the state's compelling interest in protecting minors from sexual exploitation by adults, it was not facially unconstitutional. However because the state's interest in a minor-minor sexual situation was to protect the health and quality of life of the minors, and because § 794.05 was not the least intrusive means of furthering that interest, the statute was unconstitutional as applied to petitioner. Therefore, the court quashed the decision and remanded the case for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision reversing the trial court's order granting petitioner, a minor's, motion to dismiss the delinquency petition, and answered the certified question by finding that the statute prohibiting sex with a minor violated the state constitution's privacy provisions as applied to petitioner, because the purpose of the statute was to protect minors from the sexual acts of adults, and a minor could not be prosecuted under it.

 

204 of 1586 DOCUMENTS



Hayes v. State


No. 79,997


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 257; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1040; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 296



June 22, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 13, 1995. Released for Publication September 13, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Stanton S. Kaplan, Judge - Case No. 90-3993-CF10.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged conviction for first degree murder and the imposition of the death sentence by the Broward County Circuit Court (Florida). Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in admitting collateral crime evidence, unreliable DNA evidence, and hearsay testimony and in misplacing a burden of proof.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for first degree murder and the imposition of the death sentence. The trial court denied appellant's motion in limine to exclude evidence of a collateral similar crime under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.404(2)(a) (1993), which the state introduced at trial. The court held that this error was not harmless because the facts were dissimilar. The trial court, despite appellant's objection, admitted DNA evidence. The court held that the evidence should be excluded, because the testing laboratory had admitted unreliable procedures. The trial court allowed, over appellant's objection, the state's witness to testify about the victim's statement and to assert that appellant committed the crime. The court decided that this was an error. Appellant claimed that the trial court improperly allowed, contrary to his objection, the state to attempt to transfer the burden of proof for testing evidence. The court determined that this was error. The court reversed the first degree murder conviction, vacated the death sentence, and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for first degree murder, vacated his death sentence, and remanded for a new trial, because the trial court erred by admitting collateral crime evidence, unreliable DNA evidence, and hearsay testimony and by misplacing a burden of proof.


 

205 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Sinclair v. State


No. 82,499


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


657 So. 2d 1138; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1041; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 293



June 22, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Edward Richardson, Judge - Case No. 93-01085-CFA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(1), defendant appealed both his conviction for first degree murder and his sentence of death from the Circuit Court for Brevard County (Florida). In giving the death sentence, the trial court found one aggravator and no statutory mitigators, and gave little or no weight to three nonstatutory mitigators.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried and convicted of first degree murder from a premeditated design and was sentenced to death by the trial court when it found one aggravator and no statutory mitigators and gave little or no weight to three nonstatutory mitigators. The appellate court affirmed the conviction because the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting testimony, after it properly made an adequate inquiry into whether there was a violation of the discovery rules. In addition, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying a continuance when defendant's trial counsel resigned from the public defender's office a month before the trial began. As to the sentencing phase, the appellate court concluded that the death sentence had to be reversed because the imposition of such a sentence was not proportionate. The aggravator and mitigators in the instant case were similar to those in another case reviewed by the court where the death penalty was vacated, and it have been disproportionate to rule otherwise in this case. The death penalty sentence was vacated and reduced to life in prison.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree murder, but vacated the death penalty and reduced it to life in prison without possibility of parole for 25 years. The imposition of the death penalty was disproportionate when the aggravators and mitigators were compared with another case previously reviewed by this court.

 

206 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Kearse v. State


No. 79,037


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


662 So. 2d 677; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 1039; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 300



June 22, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing November 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County, Marc A. Cianca, Judge - Case No. 91-136 CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County (Florida) which imposed the death penalty after he was convicted of robbery with a firearm and first-degree murder in the death of a police officer.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery with a firearm and first-degree murder in the death of a police officer. After the trial court imposed the death penalty, defendant appealed. On appeal, the court did not find that the court abused its discretion in admitting testimony which was relevant to the issue of premeditation. The court affirmed defendant's convictions but vacated his death sentence and remanded for a new penalty phase proceeding because a jury instruction on aggravating circumstances was unconstitutionally vague, the court could not say beyond a reasonable doubt that errors were harmless, and the court could not find beyond a reasonable doubt that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel. The court agreed with defendant that the aggravating factors of avoiding arrest/hindering enforcement of laws and murder of a law enforcement officer were duplicative because both factors were based on a single aspect of the offense, that the victim was a law enforcement officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but vacated his death sentence and remanded for a new penalty phase proceeding because the jury instruction on aggravating circumstances was unconstitutionally vague and the court could not say beyond a reasonable doubt that the errors were harmless or that the murder was heinous, atrocious, or cruel.

 

207 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. T.B.D.


No. 84,013


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


656 So. 2d 479; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 980; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 274



June 15, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 27, 1995. Released for Publication July 27, 1995. Certiorari Denied February 26, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1401.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case No. 93-3895.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the state of Florida, challenged a decision of the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) that affirmed a trial court's decision that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 876.18 (1993), which prohibited erecting a flaming cross on the property of another, violated U.S. Const. amend. I. Appellant claimed that the statute was constitutional because the prohibited activity was a threat of violence.


OVERVIEW: Appellee, a minor, was charged with erecting a flaming cross on the property of another in violation of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 876.18 (1993). Appellee claimed that the statute on its face violated U.S. Const. amend. I because it was a content-based statute prohibiting expressive conduct. The trial court held the statute unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed. Appellant, the state of Florida, challenged the ruling on the ground that the statute was constitutional. The state supreme court reversed the lower courts' rulings and held the statute constitutional as proscribing threats of violence. An unauthorized cross-burning by intruders in one's own yard constituted a direct threat to one's security, inflicted injury in the form of fear and intimidation, and tended to incite an immediate breach of the peace. Threats of violence were not protected by the first amendment and the state of Florida had a compelling interest in protecting the right of its citizens to be free from violence or the threat of violence, so the statute was constitutional. Because the full range of conduct that the statute addressed was proscribable as a threat of violence, the statute was not overbroad.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court reversed an appellate court decision that affirmed the trial court's decision that a statute that banned erecting a flaming cross on the property of another violated U.S. Const. amend I. The supreme court held that the statute was constitutional because erecting a flaming cross on the property of another amounted to a threat of violence, and threats of violence were not protected speech under the first amendment.

 

208 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Advisory Opinion to the Atty. Gen. Re Casino Authorization


No. 84,064


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


656 So. 2d 466; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 953; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 258



June 8, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Advisory Opinion to the Attorney General.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Presenter, the Florida Attorney General, requested an advisory opinion from the Supreme Court of Florida about a ballot initiative petition circulated by supporters, a gaming organization, to amend the Florida Constitution by authorizing casino gaming. Opposition, an anti-gaming organization and Florida's governor and cabinet, raised issues of compliance with Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161(1) (1993) and Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3.


OVERVIEW: Presenter, Florida Attorney General, requested an advisory opinion from the court on the ballot initiative petition circulated by supporters, a gaming organization, to amend Florida's Constitution to allow casinos. Opposition, an anti-gaming organization, Florida governor and cabinet, challenged the petition and proposed amendment's compliance. Opposition argued that the ballot's title and summary was unclear and misleading contrary to Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161(1) (1993). Opposition questioned whether the amendment contained just one subject under Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3. The court found the ballot's title and summary misleading in three respects. Although the petition led voters to believe casinos will be operated only in hotels, the amendment permitted casinos in a variety of facilities. While the petition led voters to believe that casinos would exist on functioning ships, the amendment allowed casinos on stationary vessels. The petition's initial language led voters to believe the amendment would prohibit casinos and misled by not stating gaming was already prohibited. The court held fatal defects prohibited the ballot initiative and did not reach the constitutional issue.


OUTCOME: The court issued an advisory opinion as requested by presenter Florida Attorney General, which agreed with opposition anti-gaming organization and Florida governor and cabinet, because the ballot initiative petition circulated by supporters, a gaming organization, was misleading. Therefore, the court ruled that supporters' proposed amendment to allow casino gaming would not be placed on the ballot.

 

209 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Miele v. Prudential-Bache Sec., Inc.


No. 81,467


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


656 So. 2d 470; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 954; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 260



June 8, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Certified Question of Law from the United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit - Case No. 92-2334.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The United States Court of Appeals for the Eleventh Circuit certified a question for review concerning the applicability of Fla. Stat. ch. 768.73 to an arbitration award granted in favor of plaintiff investors in their action against defendant investment company.


OVERVIEW: When defendant investment company refused to reimburse plaintiff investors for substantial losses incurred on an investment account, plaintiffs filed a demand for arbitration pursuant to the parties' contract. Plaintiffs were awarded both compensatory and punitive damages. Plaintiffs filed a petition in district court seeking to have the award confirmed. Defendant forwarded two checks to plaintiffs, including one made out to a state general revenue fund for a percentage of the punitive damage award pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 768.73. After plaintiffs moved again for an order confirming the award, the district court held that the statute applied to arbitration awards. Plaintiffs appealed, but the appellate court reserved consideration of issues until a state court determined whether the statute applied. The court held that a civil action, as referred to in Fla. Stat. ch. 768.73, clearly referred to an action filed in a court within the state and did not include an arbitration proceeding. Therefore, the statute did not apply to plaintiffs' arbitration award of punitive damages. The case was returned to the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The state statute that required payment of a percentage of punitive damages to a general revenue fund applied to civil actions filed with a court and, thus, was inapplicable to plaintiff investors' arbitration award of punitive damages from defendant investment company.

Hunter v. State


No. 82,312


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 244; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 932; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 251



June 1, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 13, 1995. Released for Publication September 13, 1995. Certiorari Denied February 20, 1996, Reported at 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1187.
Writ of certiorari denied Hunter v. Florida, 516 U.S. 1128, 116 S. Ct. 946, 133 L. Ed. 2d 871, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1187 (1996)
Post-conviction proceeding at Gaskin v. State, 798 So. 2d 721, 2001 Fla. LEXIS 2080 (Fla., 2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Post-conviction relief denied at Hunter v. State, 817 So. 2d 786, 2002 Fla. LEXIS 548 (Fla., 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hunter v. State, 29 So. 3d 256, 2008 Fla. LEXIS 1636 (Fla., 2008)

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, Gayle S. Graziano, Judge - Case No. 92-34170.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder, three counts of attempted first-degree murder, one count of attempted armed robbery, and three counts of armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of one count of first-degree murder, three counts of attempted first-degree murder, one count of attempted armed robbery, and three counts of armed robbery. He was sentenced to death. On appeal, defendant raised fourteen points of alleged error, including an allegation that the trial court erred in finding him competent to stand trial, that the prosecution improperly withheld exculpatory evidence, allegations that Florida's death penalty statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141, was unconstitutional, and allegations that the trial court gave the jury incorrect instructions. The appellate court found no merit to defendant's allegations. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in finding defendant competent to stand trial, that the prosecution's misconduct during discovery did not prejudice defendant, and that Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141 was not unconstitutional. The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentencing in full.


OUTCOME: The court rejected all fourteen of defendant's contentions of error and affirmed his conviction and sentencing. The court found defendant's claim that Florida's death penalty statute was unconstitutional to be meritless.

 

211 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Gamble v. State


No. 82,334


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


659 So. 2d 242; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 796; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 242



May 25, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 23, 1995. Released for Publication August 23, 1995. Certiorari Denied February 20, 1996, Reported at 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1100.
Writ of certiorari denied Gamble v. Florida, 516 U.S. 1122, 133 L. Ed. 2d 860, 116 S. Ct. 933, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 1100 (1996)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Gamble v. State, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 660 (Fla., May 6, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, G. Richard Singletary, Judge - Case No. 91-1676-CF-B-DS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court for Lake County (Florida) that sentenced appellant to death for first-degree murder. Appellee state sought review of trial court's evidentiary rulings and contended that the court erred in prohibiting appellee from introducing in the penalty phase certain evidence and testimony.


OVERVIEW: Appellant murdered his landlord by striking him several times in the head with a claw hammer and choking him with a cord. The jury found appellant guilty of first-degree murder, and the trial court found, as an aggravating factor, that the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated. The court sentenced appellant to death. Appellant sought review of the decision and alleged that the lower court erroneously found that the crime was cold, calculated, and premeditated and that his death sentence was disproportionate and excessive. Appellee state asserted that the lower court erred in prohibiting appellee from introducing in the penalty phase certain testimony and evidence. The supreme court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence. The court found that the trial court's decision was completely supported by the evidence, and testimony showed the murder was cold, calculated, and premeditated. The court concluded that appellant was procedurally barred from making the argument that the jury recommendation of death was unreliable due to an inadequate jury instruction.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the appellant's conviction and sentence for first-degree murder and held that the cold, calculated, and premeditated aggravating factor was applicable. The court also found that appellant's argument that the lower court's cold, calculated, and premeditated jury instruction was unreliable was procedurally barred because he failed to raise the argument on appeal.

Rogers v. State


No. 76,456


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


660 So. 2d 237; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 725; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 233



May 11, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 11, 1995. Released for Publication September 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Martin County, Carl Harper, Judge (Retired) - Case No. 89-437CF A02.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Martin County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, and one count of attempted sexual battery, and sentenced him to death, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(a), (b), (d).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his convictions of first-degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, and one count of attempted sexual battery, and the death penalty imposed, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(a), (b), (d). In reviewing the record, the court found that the state failed to meet its burden. The circumstances surrounding the death of the victim did not support premeditation. Without sufficient evidence to support premeditated murder or felony murder, the court had to reverse appellant's conviction of first-degree murder. Instead, the court found the evidence supported a conviction of second-degree murder. The court also reversed the convictions and sentences for attempted sexual battery and kidnapping because it found the trial court erred in denying appellant's motions for judgment of acquittal for kidnapping because there was insufficient evidence to support the crime. The evidence did not rise to the level of an overt act under Fla. Stat. ch. 794.011(1)(h) toward the commission of a sexual battery. The court remanded with directions that the trial court enter a judgment of guilty of second-degree murder and resentence appellant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment that convicted appellant of first-degree murder, two counts of kidnapping, and one count of attempted sexual battery, and sentenced him to death, because there was no proof of premeditation and the evidence was not sufficient to sustain the crimes. The court remanded for entry of a judgment of guilty of second-degree murder and for resentencing.

215 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Besaraba v. State


No. 80,016


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


656 So. 2d 441; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 675; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 212



May 4, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 29, 1995. Released for Publication June 29, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Stanton S. Kaplan, Judge - Case No. 89-17748 CF10 A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment convicting him of first-degree murder, attempted murder, and robbery, and sentencing him to death, from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was a homeless man who was convicted of first-degree murder, attempted murder, and robbery and sentenced to death. Appellant left a bus after a confrontation with the driver. He later returned to the bus and shot the driver and two other people who posed no threat to him. Appellant challenged his convictions and sentences, raising 28 issues on appeal. The court affirmed the convictions and life sentences for robbery and attempted murder, but vacated the death sentence as disproportionate under Florida caselaw. The court struck the cold, calculated and premeditated circumstance, because there was insufficient evidence in the record to prove this factor beyond a reasonable doubt. This left a single aggravating factor--the commission of another capital offense or felony involving use or threat of violence. The death penalty was reserved for the least mitigated and most aggravated of murders. Appellant's case involved vast mitigation including no significant history of criminal activity, the crimes were committed while he was under great mental or emotional disturbance, a badly deprived and unstable childhood, good character, and a history of alcohol and drug abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed all of appellant's convictions and his life sentences on the robbery and attempted murder charges, but vacated his death sentences as disproportionate, and remanded for imposition of life sentences without the possibility of parole for 25 years on the murder counts.

Koshel v. State


No. 83,765


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


659 So. 2d 232; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 623; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 203



April 27, 1995, Decided

218 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Bouters v. State


No. 83,558


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


659 So. 2d 235; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 624; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 186



April 27, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Fifth District - Case No. 93-504 (Orange County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision from the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida), challenging the constitutionality of the stalking statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 784.048, as overbroad and vague.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with aggravated stalking in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 784.048(4). He unsuccessfully moved to dismiss the charge, claiming the statute was unconstitutionally overbroad and vague, and then pled nolo contendere. The district court upheld the statute and petitioner appealed, asking that the district court opinion be quashed. The court found that stalking, whether by word or deed, fell outside the U. S. Const. amend. I's purview. The statute proscribed a particular type of criminal conduct which was defined at length in the statute and expressly provided that constitutionally protected activity was not included within the meaning of "course of conduct." The statute provided that the perpetrator had to made a credible threat with the intent to place the victim in reasonable fear of death or bodily harm. Since statute created a reasonable person standard, it was not unconstitutionally vague. Thus, the statute was found to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the stalking statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad or vague as it clearly defined the proscribed activity and established a reasonable person standard.

220 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Varney v. State


No. 84,172


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA

221 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. State Dep't of Health & Rehabilitative Servs.


No. 82,967


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


656 So. 2d 902; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 628; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 192



April 27, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 5, 1995. Released for Publication July 5, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity Second District - Case No. 93-01138 (Sarasota County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a homosexual, applied for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Statutory Validity, Second District (Florida), which expressly declared valid Fla. Stat. ch. 63.042(3) (1991), and expressly construed several provisions of the Florida Declaration of Rights, Fla. Const. art. I.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a gay male who sought to adopt a special needs child. Respondent agency informed petitioner that any application could not be considered due to his sexual orientation based on the homosexual exclusion contained in Fla. Stat. ch. 63.042(3). Petitioner sought declaratory and injunctive relief, and argued that the statute violated equal protection, due process, and the right to privacy as guaranteed by the Florida Constitution. The trial court concluded that the statute was unconstitutional, and respondent appealed. The intermediate court reversed. The appellate court affirmed and held that the record was insufficient to determine that the statute was unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. I, § 2 based on the rational-basis standard of review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the validity of an adoption statute that contained a homosexual exclusion because the court found that the trial court did not have a sufficient record to support a summary judgment in favor of petitioner, a homosexual, on any issue. The court further found that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

Windom v. State


No. 80,830


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


656 So. 2d 432; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 632; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 200



April 27, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 29, 1995. Released for Publication June 29, 1995.
Writ of certiorari denied Windom v. Florida, 516 U.S. 1012, 116 S. Ct. 571, 133 L. Ed. 2d 495, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 8376 (Dec. 4, 1995)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Decision reached on appeal by, Post-conviction proceeding at Windom v. State, 886 So. 2d 915, 2004 Fla. LEXIS 664 (Fla., May 6, 2004)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Windom v. Sec'y, Dep't of Corr., 578 F.3d 1227, 2009 U.S. App. LEXIS 18271 (11th Cir. Fla., Aug. 10, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at Windom v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 1588 (Fla., July 28, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Dorothy J. Russell, Judge - Case No. CR92-1305.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court, Orange County (Florida) that convicted him of three counts of first degree murder and one count of attempted first degree murder, and sentenced him to death for each of the murder convictions and imprisonment for the attempted first degree murder charge.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged and convicted of three counts of first degree murder and one count of attempted first degree murder. The trial judge sentenced appellant to death for all three counts of first degree murder and to a consecutive term of twenty-two years' imprisonment for the attempted first degree murder charge. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences. Although the court held that it could not affirm the cold, calculated, and premeditated finding with respect to two of the murders for which appellant was convicted, the existence of the one aggravator of the conviction of two other capital offenses and one violent felony against a person in each instance was sufficient to outweigh the little weight given to the mitigating factors set forth in the sentencing order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions and sentences; although the trial court's finding that the murders were cold, calculated, and premeditated was incorrect with respect to two of the murders, the sentences were supported by the number and nature of appellant's crimes.

 

223 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Laforet


No. 83,537


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


658 So. 2d 55; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 569; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 173



April 20, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 24, 1995. Released for Publication July 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 92-2832 (Indian River County).



DISPOSITION:  The court remanded the judgment of the appellate court because although the legislature expressly stated that the statute applied retroactively, it must be applied prospectively only because in substance it imposed a penalty on petitioner for failing to settle in bad faith.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurer challenged the judgment of the Fourth District Court of Appeal, Indian River County (Florida), which held that the trial court properly granted respondents' motion for additur because Fla. Stat. Ann. § 627.727(10) applied retroactively.


OVERVIEW: Respondents had brought suit against petitioner insurer under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 624.155, contending that petitioner had acted in bad faith in failing to settle an uninsured motorist insurance claim. After trial, the trial judge applied Fla. Stat. Ann. § 627.727(10) and granted respondents excess judgment as a matter of law. On appeal, the appellate court found that the trial court properly granted respondent's motion for additur because § 627.727(10) was to have retroactive application. Petitioner contended that § 627.727(10) could not be applied retroactively and that its motion for directed verdict was incorrectly denied because the basis upon which petitioner denied coverage was fairly debatable. The court held that § 627.727(10) could not be applied retroactively because it was, in substance, a penalty. Even if the legislature had expressly stated that a statute was to have retroactive application, the court would refuse to apply a statute retroactively if the statute impaired vested rights, created new obligations or imposed a penalty. Because the statute exposed petitioners to punitive damages for refusing to settle in bad faith, the statute could not apply retroactively.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the judgment of the appellate court because although the legislature expressly stated that the statute applied retroactively, it must be applied prospectively only because in substance it imposed a penalty on petitioner for failing to settle in bad faith.

 

224 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Manfredonia


No. 82,999


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


649 So. 2d 1388; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 201; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 58



February 9, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Invalidity Second District - Case No. 93-01162.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged judgments from the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which dismissed appellant's challenges from adverse rulings in unrelated prosecutions of appellees for allowing open house parties in which minors consumed or possessed drugs or alcohol in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 856.015 (1991).


OVERVIEW: In unrelated cases, appellees were charged with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 856.015 (1991) by knowingly permitting minors to possess or consume alcohol or drugs on appellees' premises. The appellate court dismissed one appellee's charge and held that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The second appellee's charge was dismissed because appellant's challenge was untimely. Appellant challenged the adverse rulings. The court affirmed and reversed in part. Chapter 856.015 was not a model of clarity because its use of the term "reasonable" rendered it susceptible to varying meanings of what actions adults were required to take to ensure that minors did not possess or consume alcohol or drugs on the adults' property. Nonetheless, the court held that lack of clarity alone did not justify invalidating the statute. The court ruled that the statute was not too vague to be enforceable. The court noted that an adult could avoid liability under the statute by terminating the party or taking some other reasonable action to prevent a minor's consumption or possession after learning of it. The dismissal of the charges against the second appellate was affirmed on untimeliness grounds.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and reversed in part a judgment that dismissed appellant state's challenges to the dismissal of charges against appellees. The court held that the statute under which appellees were prosecuted was not unconstitutionally vague in its attempt to render an adult liable for knowingly permitting a minor to consume or possess alcohol or drugs on the adult's premises. The appeal as to one appellee was properly dismissed as untimely.

 

225 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fla. Dev. Fin. Corp.


No. 84,683


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


650 So. 2d 14; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 205; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 65



February 9, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Leon County - Bond Validations J. Kevin Davey, Judge - Case No. 94-4620.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida) decision that validated revenue bonds, which related to the investment of state transportation fund earnings issued by appellee public body corporation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state appealed a trial court decision that validated revenue bonds issued by appellee public body corporation. The bonds involved the investment of state transportation fund earnings. The appellate court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The appellate court held that the bonds did not violate Fla. Const. art. VII, § 10 because the proposed bonds did not pledge public credit or taxing power. The appellate court found that the bondholders were sufficiently put on notice that appellee's obligation under the bonds was limited to several specifically defined revenue sources, and as such, the bondholders could not compel a levy of taxes to compel payment of bond obligations. Since no public credit was pledged, the fact that the primary beneficiary of the project was a private entity was of no matter. Appellee sufficiently established that a legitimate public purpose would be served by the project financed by the bond proceeds. The Florida Development Finance Corporation Act of 1993, Fla. Stat. ch. 288.9602 et seq. (1993), clearly delineated the public purpose served by the bonds. Such findings were not clearly erroneous and supported the validity of the issued bonds.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's decision that validated the revenue bonds issued by appellee public body corporation that involved investment of state transportation fund earnings. The appellate court ruled that the bonds were constitutional because no public credit was pledged and because the project to be financed by the bond proceeds served a legitimate public purpose.

 

226 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Gilbreath v. State


No. 83,090


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


650 So. 2d 10; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 44; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 51



February 2, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Second District - Case No. 93-03330 (Highlands County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) that affirmed the lower court's decision that convicted petitioner of making obscene or harassing telephone calls to a postal service management employee in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 365.16(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with making obscene or harassing telephone calls to a postal service management employee's home. The employee filed a complaint against petitioner and, in a bench trial, the employee testified that over a period of two years he had received approximately 30 similar calls from petitioner. The trial court found petitioner guilty of making obscene or harassing telephone calls in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 365.16(1)(a). The court of appeals affirmed the conviction and sustained the statute against the attack that it was an unconstitutional infringement of the right to free speech. Petitioner sought review of the lower court's decision, and the supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision. The court restricted ch. 365.16 to telephone calls or language that intended to abuse, threaten, or harass. With the restrictions, the court held that ch. 365.16(1)(a) was valid because the statutory provision was not directed at the communication of opinions or ideas but at the conduct of making a telephone call without disclosing the caller's identity, with the intent to annoy, abuse, threaten, or harass the recipient of the call.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision that entered a conviction against petitioner for making obscene or harassing telephone calls and held that the statute on which the conviction was based was constitutional. The court limited the statute's scope by limiting it to telephone calls in which the caller possessed an intent to abuse, threaten, or harass.

Hildwin v. Dugger


No. 76,145, No. 82,321


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


654 So. 2d 107; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 23; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 39



January 19, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 11, 1995. Released for Publication May 11, 1995.
Writ of certiorari denied Hildwin v. Florida, 516 U.S. 965, 116 S. Ct. 420, 133 L. Ed. 2d 337, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 7452 (1995)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus, and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hernando County, Richard Tombrink, Jr., Judge - Case No. 85-499-CF.
Hildwin v. Florida, 490 U.S. 638, 109 S. Ct. 2055, 104 L. Ed. 2d 728, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 2698 (1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, convicted of strangulation murder and sentenced to death, appealed the decision from the Circuit Court in and for Hernando County (Florida), which denied his motion pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, and petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a prisoner under sentence of death, appealed the trial court's denial of his motion pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner was convicted of strangulation murder, which the court affirmed. Petitioner claimed error in the guilt phase of his trial because no evidence was presented at the 3.850 hearing, that any evidence defense counsel claimed he did not receive and did not otherwise have access to, would have with "reasonable probability" changed the result. Petitioner also argued that the trial court erred in concluding that he was not prejudiced by his counsel's failure to investigate and present additional mitigating evidence at sentencing. The court agreed. It concluded that, in view of the substantial mitigating evidence presented at the 3.850 hearing, including the testimony of two mental health experts, the court found that counsel's errors deprived petitioner of a reliable penalty phase. The court affirmed the denial of petitioner's rule 3.850 motion with respect to his conviction, vacated and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding before a jury, and denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of petitioner's rule 3.850 motion with respect to his conviction for strangulation murder, denied the petition for writ of habeas corpus, but vacated and remanded for new sentencing proceeding before a jury because counsel's errors deprived petitioner of a reliable penalty phase.

Reed v. State


No. 82,217


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


649 So. 2d 227; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 26; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 34



January 19, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Third District - Case No. 92-1972 (Dade County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which upheld his convictions for robbery and several traffic offenses.


OVERVIEW: Defendant robbed a convenience store and was involved in an automobile accident while fleeing the scene. He was arrested and charged with traffic offenses, but armed robbery charges were not filed until much later in order to allow the state to gather information. His trial took place hundreds of days after his arrest. The reviewing court overturned his convictions. Defendant's right to a speedy trial was violated. The speedy trial time commenced when he was arrested. Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.191(a), (d). Because defendant was arrested for the conduct or criminal episode that gave rise to both the charges of robbery and kidnapping, the speedy trial time on those charges began to run from the date of his arrest.


OUTCOME: A decision that upheld defendant's convictions for robbery and several traffic offenses was quashed and remanded because governmental delay violated his right to a speedy trial.

Dep't of Health & Rehabilitative Servs. v. A.S.


No. 81,814


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


648 So. 2d 128; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 17; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 23



January 12, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Second District - Case No. 92-01901.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Department of Health and Rehabilitative Services, sought review of a decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which found that Fla. Stat. ch. 415.503(9)(e) was unconstitutionally vague in a child welfare action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee father left his six year old boy at home to conduct his duties as a fish and wildlife officer. Neighbors notified law enforcement and appellant, the Department of Health and Rehabilitative Services. Appellee sought to have a neglect report expunged. The hearing officer determined that appellee's act or omission was not serious enough for appellant's involvement. Appellant adopted the hearing officer's findings of fact, but refused to expunge the record. The lower court reversed, finding the central abuse registry statute unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the result but reversed on the unconstitutionality finding, holding that the statute provided sufficient standards to be followed by appellant in carrying out the statutory child protection program. Appellee's conduct did not rise to the level where he should be classified as the perpetrator of child neglect or abuse.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the result because appellee's conduct did not rise to the level where he should have been classified as a child neglector or abuser. However, the court reversed on the unconstitutionality finding because the statute provided sufficient standards in carrying out the statutory child protection program.

Jones v. State


No. 81,482


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


652 So. 2d 346; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 18; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 29



January 12, 1995, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 31, 1995. Released for Publication March 31, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Rodolfo Sorondo, Jr., Judge - Case No. 90-50143.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which upheld a jury verdict that found appellant guilty of first-degree murder and armed robbery and sentenced appellant to death. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in upholding the armed robbery counts and in rejecting appellant's mental or emotional disturbance at the time of the offense as a mitigating factor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was employed by victims, husband and wife business owners. After victims were killed, the police found appellant locked inside victim's building with possessions of victims on his person. Appellant had been shot in the forehead by the husband and he told a nurse that he had to kill victims because they owed him money. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and armed robbery by a jury and sentenced to death. Appellant sought review and contended that the trial court erred in upholding the armed robbery counts and in rejecting appellant's mental or emotional disturbance at the time of the offense as a statutory mitigating factor, along with other claims. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that for robbery, the victim did not have to perceive the force or violence. The decision as to whether a mitigating circumstance had been established was within the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for murder and armed robbery. The court held that a decision as to whether a mitigating circumstance had been established was within the trial court's discretion. For robbery, a victim did not have to perceive the force or violence.

Moreau v. Lewis


No. 84,019


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


648 So. 2d 124; 1995 Fla. LEXIS 3; 20 Fla. L. Weekly S 8



January 5, 1995, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Mandamus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus to require respondent Secretary of State to expunge allegedly unconstitutional enactments in the 1994-1995 General Appropriations Act and the Implementing Bill to the 1994-95 General Appropriations Act from state records, and to require respondent Comptroller and respondent Secretary of the Agency for Health Care Administration to ensure that the expunctions were reflected in state financial operations.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a Medicaid recipient, sought a writ of mandamus. Petitioner asserted that the 1994-1995 General Appropriations Act (Act), 1994 Fla. Laws ch. 94-357, § 1A(63), at 2916, and the Implementing Bill, 1994 Fla. Laws ch. 94-358, § 2(18), at 3282, which purported to establish co-payments for medical services, violated the single-subject requirements of Fla. Const. art. III, §§ 6, 12. The supreme court noted that it could issue writs of mandamus ordering the expunction of unconstitutional provisions in the Act. The court agreed that the implementing bill could not change or amend existing law on subjects other than the implementation of appropriations acts. The court concluded that the legislation worked a substantive change to the law and violated the single-subject requirement of the state constitution. The court directed respondent Secretary of State to expunge the unconstitutional provision from the Act and the official records of the state. Additionally, the court directed respondent Comptroller and respondent Secretary of the Agency for Health Care Administration to ensure that the expunction was reflected in the state's financial operations.


OUTCOME: The court directed respondent Secretary of State to expunge an unconstitutional provision from the General Appropriations Act and the official records of the state because the proposed legislation worked a substantive change to the law and violated the single-subject requirement of the state constitution. The court directed that the expunction be reflected in the financial operations of the state as well.

State v. Globe Communs. Corp.


No. 82,377


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


648 So. 2d 110; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1871; 40 A.L.R.5th 917; 23 Media L. Rep. 1116; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 645



December 8, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Fourth District - Case No. 91-3112.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) for appellee newspaper which declared Fla. Stat. ch. 794.03 (1989), which mandated criminal sanctions for identifying a victim of a sexual offense in any instrument of mass communication, facially unconstitutional under both the U.S. Const. amend. I, and Fla. Const. art I, § 4.


OVERVIEW: Appellee newspaper twice published the name of an alleged rape victim and was charged therefor by appellant state of violating Fla. Stat. ch. 794.03 (1989), which mandated criminal sanctions for identifying a victim of a sexual offense in any instrument of mass communication. The trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss on the grounds that ch. 794.03 was both facially, and as applied, unconstitutional under both the U.S. Const. amend. I, and Fla. Const. art I, § 4. Appellant state challenged that decision to the district court, which affirmed the dismissal. The court agreed with the district court's opinion that ch. 794.03 failed to pass the strict scrutiny test of constitutional jurisprudence because the statute was not narrowly tailored and did not further a state interest of the highest order. The court found that because the law was overinclusive in scope, it would improperly impose criminal sanctions. The court rejected appellee's arguments to remedy those defects by rewriting the law to include affirmative defenses and adopt curative jury instructions. The district court's ruling to invalidate the law was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed for appellee newspaper, and against appellant state, the district court's decision to invalidate the Florida statute which criminalized publication of a sex crime victim's identity because it was unconstitutional under the free speech and free press provisions of both the United States' and Florida's constitutions.

Barrett v. State


No. 78,743


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


649 So. 2d 219; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1832; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 627



November 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 6, 1995. Released for Publication February 6, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Notice and Cross-Notice of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Citrus County, John Thurman, Judge - Case No. 90-490-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From the Circuit Court in and for Citrus County (Florida), defendant appealed his convictions for first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit murder and the attendant death sentences. His appeal asserted several contentions, including that reversal was required because the trial court failed to conduct a Richardson hearing and because the trial court improperly overrode the jury's recommendation of life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for first-degree murder and conspiracy to commit murder and the attendant death sentences. In the penalty phase, the trial judge found five aggravating circumstances and several mitigating circumstances. The court reversed defendant's convictions, vacated the death sentences, and remanded for further proceedings because the state failed to conduct a Richardson hearing for a discovery violation. The court held that the state committed the discovery violation when it failed to provide the defense with a copy of defendant's palm prints. It explained that the trial court should have conducted a Richardson hearing to determine if the violation prejudiced defendant. The trial court, however, did not conduct such a hearing, finding that defendant's challenge to this discovery violation was untimely. Without the hearing, the court ruled that it was required to reverse the convictions. Even though this guilt phase issue required reversal, the court added that the trial court erred when it overrode the jury's life recommendation because of the presence of reasonable mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions, vacated the death sentences, and remanded for further proceedings because the state failed to conduct a Richardson hearing to determine if the state's violation of discovery rules prejudiced defendant. The court also ruled that the trial court impermissibly overrode the jury's recommendation of life in prison to impose the death penalty because reasonable mitigating factors were present.

Wike v. State


No. 81,117


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


648 So. 2d 683; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1839; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 617



November 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 25, 1995. Released for Publication January 25, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County, Paul Rasmussen, Judge - Case No. 88CF-547.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the imposition of the death sentence by the Circuit Court in and for Santa Rosa County (Florida), following a remand. Defendant claimed that the sentence was imposed in violation of Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.780.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and other felonies and sentenced to death. The death sentence was reversed and during the remanded sentencing phase, defendant requested the right to make closing arguments, citing Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.250. The state informed the trial court that Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.250 governed the right to close in the guilt phase and there was no such right in the penalty phase, and the trial court denied defendant's request. The court reversed defendant's death sentence because Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.780 provided for the right of a defendant to close in the penalty phase. The court rejected the state's argument that the failure to grant defendant's request to close was harmless error because it was well established that the right to close in the guilt phase was reversible error and the policy considerations for protecting the right in the guilt phase were the same. The court also rejected the state's contention that defendant waived this issue because defendant requested his rights under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.780, which were denied only after the state advised the trial court that no such right existed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's death sentence and remanded for resentencing because the trial court erred in refusing to provide defendant with the opportunity to make closing arguments before the jury where defendant was on trial for his life.

 

236 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


B.H. v. State


No. 82,361


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


645 So. 2d 987; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1842; 46 A.L.R.5th 877; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 610



November 23, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Fifth District - Case No. 92-1856 (Volusia County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juvenile appealed the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida), affirming the adjudication of petitioner as delinquent on the ground that Fla. Stat. ch. 39.061, the statute under which he was charged with escape, was unconstitutional in that the statute improperly delegated legislative authority to the Department of Health and Rehabilitative Services to determine what the crime of juvenile escape was.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner juvenile was charged with escape from a juvenile commitment facility in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 39.061. Petitioner pleaded no contest to the charge, reserving the right to appeal the constitutionality of the statute. Petitioner was adjudicated delinquent and committed to the Department of Health and Rehabilitative Services (HRS). Petitioner appealed, and the adjudication of delinquency was affirmed. Petitioner again appealed. The supreme court held that ch. 39.061, under which petitioner was adjudicated delinquent, was unconstitutional because it improperly delegated to HRS the legislative authority to define the crime of juvenile escape in violation of the separation of powers, and the legislature's vague delegation of open-ended authority to HRS did not allow for proper notice of what was a prohibited act under the law in violation of due process. Moreover, the finding that ch. 39.061 was unconstitutional effected an automatic revival of its immediate predecessor, ch. 39.112. Finally, petitioner's adjudication was sustained under revived ch. 39.112 because the specifications of the charge alleged all elements necessary under section 39.112.


OUTCOME: The court found that the statute under which petitioner was adjudicated delinquent was unconstitutional because the legislature delegated unlimited and open-ended power to define the crime of juvenile escape to an administrative agency in violation of the separation of powers and due process protections. However, once the statute was voided, it revived its predecessor, and petitioner's adjudication was sustained under the revived statute.

Lowe v. State


No. 77,972


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


650 So. 2d 969; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1840; 199 Fla. L. Weekly S 621



November 23, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised on Denial of Rehearing March 9, 1995. Released for Publication March 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County, Joe Wild, Judge - Case No. 90-658.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for a rehearing and appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Indian River County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. After the trial court sentenced him to death, he appealed and moved for a rehearing. On appeal, the court held that the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in finding that a child was competent to testify. The court affirmed the sentence and conviction and denied defendant's motion for a rehearing, because the trial judge properly considered the mitigating evidence presented and the death penalty was justified under the circumstances of the case. The court found that the police did not deploy defendant's girlfriend as an agent to coerce a confession and the trial court did not err in admitting defendant's incriminating statement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence and conviction and denied his motion for rehearing because the trial judge properly considered the mitigating evidence presented and the death penalty was justified under the circumstances of the case.

 

238 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Watson v. State


No. 79,139


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


651 So. 2d 1159; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1578; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 564



November 3, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 21, 1995. Released for Publication March 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Juan Ramirez, Judge - Case No. 88-38759.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of March 24, 1994, Previously Reported at: 1994 Fla. LEXIS 408.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), convicting him of murder and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction of murder and his death sentence on multiple grounds. Defendant's claim that he was denied an impartial jury was unfounded because he failed to demonstrate error in denial of challenges for cause, there was not evidence that a juror had formed an opinion prior to trial, and a juror's statement regarding the heinous crime only referenced the nature of the crime committed. Jurors' questions for witnesses were reviewed by the judge and attorneys and deemed proper prior to the judge presenting them to the witnesses. Appeals to the sympathy of the jury and victim impact statements were objected to by the defense, the court sustained the objections and offered a curative statement, which defendant declined. Defendant was not entitled to a hearing on alleged discovery violations because the expert statements referenced were not written statements and were thus not discoverable. Defendant failed to object to jury instructions, and therefore the issue was not preserved for appeal. Mitigating circumstances were properly weighed, and the court rejected argument regarding the constitutionality of the death sentence. Conviction and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for murder and his sentence of death were affirmed because an impartial jury was impaneled, juror questions to witnesses were appropriate, objections to state arguments were sustained and curative statement was offered, defendant was not entitled to a hearing on alleged discovery violation, defendant failed to object to jury instructions, mitigating circumstances were considered, and the death sentence was constitutional.

 

239 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


King v. Ellison


No. 82,300


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


648 So. 2d 666; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1576; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 557



November 3, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1995. Released for Publication January 26, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 92-2376 (Indian River County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Indian River County (Florida), certified the following question as having great public importance: whether Fla. Stat. ch. 732.401(1) (1991), which vested a remainder interest in homestead property in lineal descendants, was unconstitutional when applied to defeat a testator's intent to devise homestead property equally to adult stepchildren as well as adult lineal descendants.


OVERVIEW: A married couple purchased real property. The couple's will bequeathed their entire estates to each other. The husband's will also provided that if he outlived his wife, his property would pass to his children and stepchildren, share and share alike. Wife died, and husband remarried. Husband established homestead in the real property and then passed away. Pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 732.401(1) (1991), husband's surviving spouse received a life estate in the homestead, and husband's lineal descendants received a vested remainder. Petitioners, husband's stepchildren, brought an action alleging that ch. 732.401(1) was unconstitutional because it conflicted with Fla. Const. art. X, § 4(c). The trial court dismissed the complaint with prejudice, and the district court affirmed. On review, the court stated that the challenged statute was not meant to be a restraint on the right to devise homestead property. The statute prescribed how property was to descend when not devised as permitted under Florida law or the constitution. Because husband died leaving a surviving spouse, his attempt to devise his homestead failed. Thus, the homestead descended pursuant to ch. 732.401(1).


OUTCOME: The court held that a statute, which vested a remainder interest in homestead property in lineal descendants, was constitutional when applied to defeat a testator's intent to devise homestead property equally as to adult stepchildren and adult lineal descendants. The statute prescribed how testator's homestead should descend because the property was not devised as permitted under Florida law.

 

240 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


In re Report of the Comm'n on Family Courts


No. 77,623


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


646 So. 2d 178; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1558; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 542



October 26, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected February 21, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Report of the Commission on Family Courts.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: All circuit courts were previously ordered to submit reports regarding the status of their respective family divisions, together with proposed revisions to local rules and administrative orders, in connection with the recommendations of the Florida Commission on Family Courts to implement family law divisions, as required by 1990 Fla. Laws ch. 90-273.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to 1990 Fla. Laws ch. 90-273, circuit courts were required to establish family law divisions and a commission on family courts made recommendations for implementation of the family divisions. Thereafter, all circuit court were required to submit local rules and administrative orders establishing family divisions and then submit annual reports regarding the status of their respective divisions. Meanwhile, 1994 Fla. Laws ch. 94-134 was enacted, giving criminal courts jurisdiction over violations of domestic violence injunctions, thereby conflicting with the scheme that all family law issues, including domestic violence, be handled by family law divisions, not criminal courts. In submitting their reports, various courts were confused about the effect of Chapter 94-134 and the validity of their local rules and administrative orders. In expressly approving certain local rules and administrative orders, the court ruled that its approval was required. The provision of Fla. R. Judicial Admin. 2.050(b), which allowed issuance of administrative orders without approval, did not apply to the establishment of family divisions.


OUTCOME: The local rules and administrative orders establishing family law divisions in each of the circuits were approved, with circuit judges directed to comment on the issue of assigning domestic violence cases, because the divisions were properly established and their implementation was not affected by other administrative rule allowing implementation without approval.

Heath v. State


No. 77,234


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


648 So. 2d 660; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1552; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 540



October 20, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 25, 1995. Released for Publication January 25, 1995.
Writ of certiorari denied Heath v. Florida, 515 U.S. 1162, 115 S. Ct. 2618, 132 L. Ed. 2d 860, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 4351 (1995)
Post-conviction relief denied at Heath v. State, 3 So. 3d 1017, 2009 Fla. LEXIS 134 (Fla., 2009)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Heath v. McNeil, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 83364 (N.D. Fla., July 9, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Alachua County, Robert P. Cates, Judge - Case No. 89-3026-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Alachua County Circuit Court (Florida), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of first-degree murder and armed robbery and imposing sentences of death and life imprisonment, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his brother were charged with armed robbery and first-degree murder. During opening statements in defendant's trial, the prosecutor said that defendant's brother would be the only one who would tell the jury what happened. His brother testified he shot the victim in the chest and defendant stabbed him in the neck. At defendant's instruction, the brother then shot the victim in the head. The victim's wife testified that he liked to go to bars to talk to people and defendant's cellmate testified defendant said he wanted to escape and kill two witnesses that could tie him to the victim. Defendant was found guilty. While his brother was sentenced to life, defendant was sentenced to death and life imprisonment, after asserting no objections to jury instructions. Defendant appealed. In affirming, the court ruled that, although the prosecutor's opening statement improperly highlighted defendant's right to remain silent, the error was harmless. Also, it was not improper to admit the testimony of the wife or cellmate. The death sentence was justified given defendant's dominating influence and greater culpability. Objections to jury instructions were waived.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed because, inter alia, a prosecutor's comment highlighting defendant's right to remain silent was harmless error; evidence of the victim's character was not improperly admitted; testimony that defendant told cellmate that he wanted to escape to kill prosecution witnesses was admissible; and death sentence was appropriate, despite accomplice receiving life sentence, since defendant was more culpable.

243 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Wuornos v. State


No. 81,059


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


644 So. 2d 1012; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1528; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 503



October 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 21, 1994. Released for Publication November 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Thomas D. Sawaya, Judge - Case No. 91-112-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant contested her death sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County (Florida), following three separate murder convictions.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of three separate murders following no contest pleas. In reviewing her death sentence, the court concluded that appellant's plea was not improper or inconsistent because any colorable claim of self-defense continued to be at issue during the penalty phase. The facts did not support the conclusion that her pleas were improperly accepted. The lower court and her counsel apprised her of, and she understood, the consequences of her plea. Further, appellant's claim that hearsay evidence was improperly admitted during the penalty phase was rejected because the rules of evidence were relaxed during the penalty phase and because it was appellant that opened the door to the evidence by resting on hearsay evidence. The state's theory on cold calculated premeditation prevailed, was consistent with the facts, and was proven beyond a reasonable doubt. Thus, the facts supported the finding of that aggravator. The court found no error in the trial court's holding that the mitigating factors presented by appellant were not supported by evidence and that, in any event, were overwhelmingly outweighed by the aggravating circumstances. The court affirmed the death sentence.


OUTCOME: In affirming appellant's murder convictions and death sentence, the court held that her no contest plea was proper and that the finding of aggravating and mitigating factors were not erroneous.
