Caruso v. State


73,507


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


645 So. 2d 389; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1530; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 508



October 6, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1994. Released for Publication December 2, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Mark A. Speiser, Judge - Case No. 87-21838CF10.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the override by the Broward County Circuit Court (Florida) of the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment after appellant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder. After the jury voted to recommend life sentences on both counts, the trial judge sentenced appellant to life imprisonment on one count and to death on the other. Appellant challenged his convictions and the death sentence. The trial judge found in aggravation the previous conviction of another capital offense based on the contemporaneous convictions. The trial judge concluded that the jury's life sentence recommendation was unreasonable as to one victim and, as a result, sentenced appellant to death for one murder and to life for the other murder. Appellant argued that the trial court erroneously overrode the jury's recommendation and the court agreed, holding that there was a reasonable basis for the jury's recommendation of life because appellant had a long-term drug addiction and because the jury could take into consideration appellant's youthful age.


OUTCOME: The trial court's override of the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment as to one murder was erroneous and appellant was resentenced to life because there was a reasonable basis for the jury's recommendation. The imposition of a life sentence as to the other murder was affirmed.

Dep't of Revenue v. Kuhnlein


Nos. 82,994, 82,995


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


646 So. 2d 717; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1479; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 467



September 29, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 30, 1994. Released for Publication November 30, 1994. Appellees/Cross-Appellants Adams and Crows' Motion for Rehearing or Clarification as to Case No. 82,995 Denied November 30, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Direct Appeals and Cross-Appeals of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Orange County, Lawrence R. Kirkwood, Judge, Case Nos. CI 92-6224 & CI 92-5912 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District, Case Nos. 93-2848 & 93-2849.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state departments and appellee citizens cross-challenged a judgment of the Trial Court in and for Orange County, which the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida) certified, that an impact fee was in violation of the United States Constitution commerce clause and that, while a taxpayer could bring a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action in state court on a tax matter, Fla. Stat. ch. 319.231 did not violate a taxpayer's right to travel.


OVERVIEW: The Florida legislature passed and amended Fla. Stat. ch. 319.231 (1991), which imposed an impact fee on cars purchased or titled in other states that then were registered in Florida by permanent residents. Appellee citizens filed suit arguing that the fee was a tax that violated the commerce clause of the U.S. Const. art. I, § 8 and violated their civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The lower court found ch. 319.231 unconstitutional under the commerce clause but also found that a taxpayer could bring a § 1983 action in state court in a tax matter. The lower court further held that the statute did not violate anyone's right to travel. Appellant state agencies challenged the ruling that the statute violated the commerce clause, but the court rejected the argument. The court held that appellants had standing because they faced penalties for failure to pay the fee. Appellees argued that in state auto dealers were given an advantage. The court agreed and noted that the burden was placed on out-of-state economic interests and therefore violated the commerce clause. The court therefore affirmed the lower court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The holding that a Florida impact fee on cars purchased or titled in other states but then registered in Florida violated the commerce clause of the United States Constitution was affirmed. The court found that the impact fee affected and burdened only out-of-state economic interests in that only autos purchased out-of-state were subject to the fee.

Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Pittman v. State, 90 So. 3d 794, 2011 Fla. LEXIS 1519 (Fla., 2011)

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Raising ten issues, three of which were directed to the guilt phase of his trial, appellant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Polk County (Florida), which convicted him on three counts of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with three counts of first-degree murder and sentenced to death after he stabbed his wife's parents and sister and burned their home in an attempt to cover up the murders. The jury found him guilty of three counts of first-degree murder, two counts of arson, and one count of grand theft, and found him not guilty of burglary. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged her convictions of first-degree murder and armed robbery with a firearm from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner was convicted of first-degree murder and armed robbery with a firearm and was sentenced to death on the murder charge and ten years for the armed robbery. Prisoner contended that certain information and documents were withheld from her during pretrial discovery. The court held the information was furnished to prisoner's original defense team within the time limits of the Richardson rule. Prisoner argued the nature of the similar crimes evidence was so disturbing that its relevance was outweighed by the potential for prejudice. The court stated that the nature of the various crimes was relevant to have established a pattern of similarities among the homicides. The court held that the relevance of the similar crimes evidence clearly outweighed prejudice here. Prisoner contended that trial court erred when it denied her motion for judgment of acquittal because her testimony was uncontroverted. The court held that prisoner's testimony was clearly controverted and the trial court did not err. Judgment and convictions were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant prisoner's convictions and sentences for first-degree murder and armed robbery were affirmed. The relevance of the similar crimes evidence clearly outweighed the prejudice.

OVERVIEW: Appellant brutally murdered his wife in front of their teenage son. The jury convicted him of first-degree murder, and the trial judge followed the jury's recommendation and imposed death. The judge found three aggravating circumstances: previous conviction of another felony involving violence based upon the contemporaneous convictions; that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel (HAC); and that the murder was committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner without any pretense of moral or legal justification (CCP). The court reasoned that although there was evidence that he contemplated the murder in advance, evidence offered in support of mental mitigating circumstances negated the cold component of the CCP aggravator. The court affirmed the conviction, but vacated and remanded his death sentence.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for first-degree murder was affirmed, however because of error in the sentencing order, his sentence of death was vacated and remanded for reconsideration by the judge.

Castro v. State


No. 81,731


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


644 So. 2d 987; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1361; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 435



September 8, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 16, 1994. Released for Publication November 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Thomas Sawaya, Judge - Case No. 87-119CF-A-Z.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the jury recommended death sentence imposed by the Marion County Circuit Court (Florida) upon resentencing after remand from a prior appeal. Appellant alleged that the court erred on several grounds regarding jury selection, aggravating circumstances, and other related concerns.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder in a prior trial brought by the state. Following past penalty phase appeals and remands arising from that conviction, appellant challenged his third resentencing which resulted in a jury recommended death penalty imposed by the trial court. Appellant alleged that the trial court erred in excusing a juror for cause despite his counsel's objection. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excusing for cause the juror who could not set aside his beliefs against the death penalty. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in not striking eight other jurors for cause because they were exposed to prejudicial pretrial publicity which made them predisposed in favor of the death penalty. The court held that the trial court correctly determined those jurors had not formed any opinion before trial based on media coverage. While the court agreed with appellant that the trial court erred in finding that premeditation applied as an aggravating factor, it was harmless error because the trial court correctly found three other aggravating circumstances. Thus, the court affirmed the death penalty sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's imposition of the jury recommended death penalty during resentencing because the trial court committed no reversible error in either denying appellant's requests to keep and strike jurors or in incorrectly finding an aggravating circumstance among three other valid ones.

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, R. Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. 82-1658-CF Div. "S".


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After finding in federal habeas corpus proceedings that appellant was denied meaningful review in his direct appeal of his first-degree murder convictions and the death sentence imposed, the United States Supreme Court remanded the action for initiation of appropriate proceedings for state court reconsideration of appellant's death sentence.


OVERVIEW: The United States Supreme Court, after finding that appellant was denied meaningful review on direct appeal of his first-degree murder convictions and death sentence, remanded the case for appropriate state court reconsideration of appellant's death sentence. The state supreme court vacated the death sentence imposed by the trial court judge after he overrode the jury's life sentence recommendation and remanded the action for imposition of the life imprisonment sentence. The jury's life imprisonment recommendation was supported by nonstatutory mitigating circumstances, including that an accomplice actually killed the victims, that appellant was intoxicated when the murders were committed, and testimony concerning appellant's background and testimony. The trial court's override of the recommendation was improper because the jury's recommended sentence was not clearly erroneous or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The state supreme court, upon remand from the United States Supreme Court, held that the trial court judge improperly overrode the jury's life imprisonment recommendation after convicting appellant of two courts of first-degree murder. The trial court's death sentence was improper because the jury's life sentence recommendation was not unreasonable in light of nonstatutory mitigating factors.

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Thomas M. Coker, Jr., Judge - Case No. 90-5417-CF-10B.

OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions for robbery, attempted first-degree murder, and first-degree murder and sentences of life imprisonment and death were affirmed because victim's recantation was unreliable, defendant did not need additional counsel, and negligible mitigating evidence existed. Defendant robbed a restaurant at which his former girlfriend worked. Police arrived and an officer was killed and another wounded. Defendant was convicted. Defendant brought a motion for a new trial, which was denied. Defendant appealed, claiming a new trial was required where the girlfriend's recantation at the new trial hearing was crucial and placed the murder weapon in defendant's possession. Defendant also claimed, inter alia, that he was entitled to the appointment of co-counsel due to the trial's complexity and the death penalty was unsupported. The death sentence was upheld because negligible mitigating evidence existed and valid aggravators existed.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for a new trial and entry of defendant's convictions for robbery, attempted first-degree murder, and first-degree murder. Defendant's former girlfriend's recantation was unreliable and a new trial unwarranted. Co-counsel was unnecessary because investigators were provided to defendant. The death penalty was upheld because negligible mitigating evidence existed.

X, § 16, complied with Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3, and whether the proposed ballot title and substance complied with Fla. Stat. Ann. § 101.161.

OUTCOME: Briefs were requested and a hearing date was set to consider a proposed amendment to the Florida Constitution because the signature requirements for an initiative petition were met, the required language and length requirements were met for the proposed amendment's title and substance, and proper petition was made to the state attorney general.

 

253 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Abshire v. State


No. 81,326


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


642 So. 2d 542; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 997; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 353



June 30, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 21, 1994. Released for Publication September 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Johns County, Richard Watson, Judge - Case No. 91-2418 A.
Marquard v. State, 641 So. 2d 54, 1994 Fla. LEXIS 863 (Fla., 1994)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for St. Johns County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and armed robbery and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and armed robbery and sentenced to death. Defendant sought reversal of his convictions and challenged the discriminatory use in the jury selection process of gender-based peremptory challenges, claiming his rights under the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, were violated. The supreme court reversed defendant's convictions, vacated his death sentence, and remanded the case for a new trial. The supreme court held that the equal protection clause of the federal constitution prohibited discrimination in jury selection on the basis of gender and prohibited gender-based peremptory challenges. The supreme court found that comments made during jury selection at defendant's trial showed a desire to exclude women solely because they were women. The comments violated the prospective jurors' and defendant's rights to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions for first-degree murder and armed robbery, vacated a sentence of death, and remanded the case for a new trial where defendant's conviction by a jury selected on the basis of gender-based peremptory challenges violated defendant's constitutional right to equal protection.

 

254 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Cuda v. State


No. 82,203


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


639 So. 2d 22; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 998; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 346



June 30, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Fifth District - Case Nos. 92-1950 & 92-2227 (Volusia County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) applied for review of its decision reversing the trial court's dismissal of a charge against defendant for abuse of an aged person by exploitation under Fla. Stat. ch. 415.111(5) (1991). The court of appeal disagreed with the trial court's finding that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged under Fla. Stat. ch. 415.111(5) with one count of abuse of an aged person by exploitation. The trial court dismissed the case, finding that the adjectives "improper or illegal" in the statute were unconstitutionally vague. The court of appeal reversed the order of the trial court and remanded the case for trial, stating that based on the definition of the word "illegal," the statute was constitutional. On an application for review, the supreme court quashed the decision of the court of appeal and remanded the case for further proceedings, holding that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it provided no clear explanation of the proscribed conduct, no explicit definition of the terms used, and no good faith defense. The supreme court found that the statute violated due process because it was too vague to give notice. The determination of the standard of guilt was left to the courts or juries, which was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the court of appeal's decision that reversed the trial court's dismissal of a charge against defendant for abuse of an aged person by exploitation. The court remanded the case for further proceedings, finding that the statute which prohibited the conduct was unconstitutionally vague because it contained no clear explanation of proscribed conduct, no explicit definition of terms, and no good faith defense.

 

255 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Parker v. State


No. 76,172


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


641 So. 2d 369; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 933; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 322



June 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 31, 1994. Released for Publication August 31, 1994.
Writ of certiorari denied Parker v. Florida, 513 U.S. 1131, 130 L. Ed. 2d 888, 115 S. Ct. 944, 1995 U.S. LEXIS 809 (1995)
Post-conviction relief granted at, in part, Remanded by, Writ of habeas corpus denied Parker v. State, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 547 (Fla., Mar. 24, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Leroy Moe, Judge - Case No. 89-8897-CF10.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner who was convicted of murder, armed robbery, and aggravated battery with a firearm challenged his convictions and sentence from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner was sentenced to death upon convictions for murder, armed robbery, and aggravated battery with a firearm. Prisoner also argued that the lower court erred when it failed to grant his motion for continuance because of the state's tardy disclosure of two witnesses. The court noted that the witnesses' names were disclosed two weeks prior to trial, and counsel had declared he was satisfied with discovery after he deposed them and he did not object when they testified. The court held that there was no error in when the lower court denied prisoner's continuance. Prisoner argued that the court erred when it denied his motion for new trial because of a newly discovered witness who would testify that he saw someone else shoot the victim. The court noted that the newly discovered evidence must have been of such nature that it would probably have produced an acquittal on retrial to have been sufficient to have required reversal. The court held that prisoner's new evidence did not meet this standard and the lower court did not abuse its discretion. Prisoner's convictions and sentence were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant prisoner's conviction and sentence for murder, armed robbery, and aggravated battery with a firearm were affirmed. The lower court did not err when it denied prisoner's motion for a new trial because the newly discovered evidence was not of such a nature that it would have probably produced an acquittal on retrial.

Lightbourne v. State


No. 80,366


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


644 So. 2d 54; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 946; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 331



June 16, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied October 26, 1994. Released for Publication October 26, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Carven Angel, Judge - Case No. 81-170-CF-A-01.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court for Marion County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a prisoner under sentence of death, filed a motion for postconviction relief, arguing that two witness who testified at his trial regarding incriminating statements made by appellant while in the county jail, were acting in concert with the prosecution to obtain the statements and that the prosecution withheld information regarding its agency relationship with the two witnesses. Appellant also claimed that the two witnesses lied at the trial and that the prosecution deliberately used the false testimony. The trial court denied appellant's motion for postconviction relief, refusing to admit evidence to show that the witnesses lied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court determined that the statements were not statements against interest under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.804; therefore, they were properly not admitted under the hearsay rule. Moreover, the court rejected appellant's argument that a Brady violation occurred because the prosecution withheld information pertaining to the timing of a payment by the detective to the witness. Court found that the evidence regarding the payment would not have affected the result of the trial and did not constitute a Brady violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying appellant's motion for postconviction relief after holding that the evidence regarding the timing of a payment by the prosecution to a witness did not constitute a Brady violation because it would not have affected the result of the trial.

 

257 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


No. 82,482


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


638 So. 2d 509; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 900; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 305



June 9, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Second District - Case No. 92-03643 (Pasco County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prosecution appealed a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida) declaring Fla. Stat. Ann. § 322.34(3) unconstitutional because an act of simple negligence in operating a motor vehicle could not be combined with the crime of driving a motor vehicle under a canceled, suspended, or revoked license to create a new criminal offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with driving with a suspended license causing death or injury under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 322.34(3). Defendant moved to dismiss the charge on the basis that the statute unconstitutionally criminalized mere negligence. The trial court granted the motion to dismiss, finding that simple negligence could not be used to enhance a criminal act from a misdemeanor to a felony. The appellate court affirmed. The court reversed and remanded the case. The court held that when a person is charged under the statute, a determination already had been made that the person was no longer fit to be driving on Florida's highways. As such, the court held that knowingly driving with a suspended, canceled, or revoked driver's license was indeed a willful act in clear violation of the law. The court reasoned that, although a homicide may have been unintentionally committed through negligence, it was the willful act of committing the underlying felony that criminalized the simple negligence supporting the conviction for felony murder. The court, following this rationale, held, therefore, that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 322.34(3) did not unconstitutionally criminalize simple negligence.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision which declared that the statute involving driving with a suspended license causing death or injury, Fla. Stat. Ann. § 322.34(3), was unconstitutional, holding that the statute did not unconstitutionally criminalize simple negligence.

 

258 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Chiles


No. 82,895


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


638 So. 2d 48; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 903; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 307



June 9, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Mandamus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner compensation claims judge sought a writ of mandamus requiring respondent governor to reappoint him under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.45 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner compensation claims judge sought a writ of mandamus requiring respondent governor to reappoint him under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 440.45 (1991). Petitioner argued under the retention process statute that respondent was required to reappoint him because the nominating commission voted to retain him. Respondent contended the statute impermissibly restricted his gubernatorial power to appoint executive branch members. The court denied petitioner's requested relief, concluding the statute unconstitutionally violated separation of powers to the extent it eliminated respondent's choice in the reappointment of executive branch officers. The court explained workers' compensation claims judges were placed in the executive branch by the state legislature's choice to place them in the department of labor. The court noted that, despite the performance of a quasi-judicial function, compensation claims judges were still a part of the executive branch. As a result, the court found respondent governor had the power to appoint executive branch officials under Fla. Stat. ch. 93-415 § 40.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's requested writ of mandamus requiring respondent to reappoint him as a compensation claims judge, in respondent governor's favor, because workers' compensation claims judges were executive branch members of the state department of labor and statutory appointment procedure was unconstitutionally violative of separation of powers to the extent it restricted respondent's power to appoint executive branch members.

Reed v. State


No. 80,518


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


640 So. 2d 1094; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 827; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 300



June 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 15, 1994. Released for Publication August 15, 1994.
Later proceeding at Reed v. State, 701 So. 2d 868, 1997 Fla. LEXIS 1453 (Fla., 1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, David C. Wiggins, Judge - Case No. 86-6123-CF.
Reed v. Florida, 498 U.S. 882, 112 L. Ed. 2d 184, 111 S. Ct. 230, 1990 U.S. LEXIS 4562, 59 U.S.L.W. 3250 (1990)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Circuit Court, Duval County (Florida), denying his motion for postconviction relief from his sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of robbery, sexual battery, and first-degree murder. He was sentenced to death, and the sentence was affirmed on appeal. Defendant then filed a motion for postconviction relief, and the trial court denied the motion. The court reversed in part and remanded the case. The court held that defendant's allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel, when considered as a whole, were sufficient to require an evidentiary hearing. The court held further that any conversations between defendant and his trial lawyer relevant to the ineffective assistance of counsel claim were not protected by the attorney-client privilege. The court held that defendant could move to exclude from discovery any portion of his file which contained matters unrelated to the crimes for which defendant was convicted, such as evidence of other crimes. In addition, the court held that the trial court should hold a hearing regarding defendant's public records request.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the trial court's order denying defendant's motion for postconviction relief, holding that defendant's allegations of ineffective assistance of counsel, when considered as a whole, were sufficient to require an evidentiary hearing and that the trial court, on remand should also hold a hearing on defendant's public records request.

Morgan v. State


No. 75,676


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


639 So. 2d 6; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 829; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 290



June 2, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Martin County, John D. Ferris, Judge - Case No. 77-326-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of death sentence and murder conviction, in appellee prosecution's favor, in the Circuit Court for Marin County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for murder and death sentence, in appellee prosecution's favor. The court rejected appellant's numerous alleged errors in the penalty phase of his conviction and affirmed. The court explained appellant's attorney-client privilege was not violated by prosecutorial statements referring to a conversation between appellant and a defense expert. The court indicated when appellant opened the inquiry regarding those communications, he waived the protection for such communications. The court next rejected the argument that appellant was subjected to double jeopardy. The court explained that appellant was not previously acquitted of felony murder, as he suggested. Rather, the court noted the judge in the first trial merely opined enough evidence for felony murder was not presented, but nonetheless went on the give the felony murder instruction. The court found appellant's request for additional experts was properly denied when he had already been allowed to retain five experts. The court found the lower court erred in failing to consider mitigating factors for purposes of the death sentence and reversed for imposition of life imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's murder conviction, reversed death sentence, and remanded for life imprisonment because statements were properly admitted at trial, double jeopardy did not occur, denial of additional experts was proper, and evidence was properly admitted. Court found death sentence disproportionate when mitigating factors of age, extreme emotional disturbance, and diminished ability to appreciate conduct were not considered.

 

261 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Palm Beach County v. Wright


No. 81,278


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


641 So. 2d 50; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 832; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 288



June 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 23, 1994. Released for Publication August 23, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance Fourth District - Case No. 92-1912 (Palm Beach County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeals (Florida) certified a question to the court regarding whether a thoroughfare map was unconstitutional. The district court had affirmed a judgment against petitioner county finding that the map was in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V and Fla. Const. art. X, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner county adopted a comprehensive plan which contained a thoroughfare map defining certain corridors for future roadway construction. Respondent property owners attacked the constitutionality of the thoroughfare map, arguing that the map violated U.S. Const. amend. V. and Fla. Const. art. X, § 6 because the map was not a valid police regulation, it failed to substantially advance a legitimate state interest, and it constituted a contemporary taking. The trial court granted summary judgment to respondents. The appellate court affirmed the decision, but certified a question to the state supreme court regarding the map's constitutionality. The court found the map, on its face, was not an unconstitutional taking, and quashed the decision below. The court stated that the adoption of the thoroughfare map was a proper exercise of petitioner's police power because it substantially advanced a legitimate state interest and, without the map, petitioner's ability to plan for future growth would be seriously impeded. The court noted, however, that the map as applied to certain property could result in a taking.


OUTCOME: The court ordered the decision of the lower court upholding a judgment against petitioner county quashed because the court found that petitioner's thoroughfare map was on its face a constitutional exercise of petitioner's police power where it substantially advanced a legitimate state interest.

 

262 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Cardona v. State


No. 79,787


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


641 So. 2d 361; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 835; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 301



June 2, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 31, 1994. Released for Publication August 31, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, David L. Tobin, Judge - Case No. 90-48092-B.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the body of appellant's 3-year-old son was found abandoned in residential bushes, the jury found appellant guilty of aggravated child abuse, Fla. Stat. ch. 827.03(1)(b) (1989), and first degree murder. The Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) followed the jury's recommendation to impose a death sentence, finding the murder especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel. Id. ch. 921.141(5)(h) (1991). Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: After splitting her 3-year-old son's head open with a baseball bat, appellant locked the boy in the closet where he had been confined for the past two months. The next day, appellant and her codefendant girlfriend abandoned the child's battered body in the bushes of a residence. Appellant was convicted of aggravated child abuse and first degree murder, and sentenced to death for the murder. Appellant sought review. Finding most of appellant's claims procedurally barred because they were not raised below, the court affirmed by holding that the evidence was sufficient to support both convictions and that the evidence of child abuse was within the framework of the indictment. With respect to the penalty phase, the defense could not claim as a nonstatutory mitigating circumstance that it would be in the two surviving children's best interest for appellant to be given a life sentence. Furthermore, disparate treatment was justified because appellant was more culpable than the codefendant. Finally, appellant's death sentence was warranted in light of the extended period of time that the child was subjected to the torturous abuse leading to his death.


OUTCOME: Holding that the admissible evidence of child abuse sufficiently supported appellant's convictions for aggravated child abuse and first degree murder, the court affirmed appellant's proportional death sentence because the child was tortured for many months before he was finally beaten to death. Thus, the imposition of the death penalty did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment or violate appellant's due process rights.

Jones v. State


Nos. 81,970, 81,992


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


640 So. 2d 1084; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 816; 63 U.S.L.W. 2031; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 280



May 26, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied August 15, 1994. Released for Publication August 15, 1994. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated. Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fifth District - Case Nos. 91-134 & 92-1876 (Orange & Lake Counties).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified a question to the court regarding the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 800.04, which made it a crime to have sexual relations with a minor under the age of 16. The district court of appeal affirmed one trial court's conviction under the statute and reversed another trial court's ruling that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In two separate actions, petitioners were charged with violating Fla. Stat. ch. 800.04, by engaging in sexual intercourse with minors under the age of 16. In one action, a trial court entered judgment convicting one petitioner under the statute. In another action, a trial court found the statute to be unconstitutional. The district court of appeal affirmed the conviction and reversed the trial court decision that found the statute unconstitutional. The district court of appeal certified the issue of the statute's constitutionality to the state supreme court. The court approved the decisions of the lower court, affirmed petitioner's conviction, and remanded the other petitioners' case for appropriate action. The state supreme court determined that neither the level of intimacy nor the degree of harm was relevant when an adult and a child under the age of 16 engaged in sexual intercourse. Because the state had a compelling interest in protecting minors from sexual harm and exploitation, the statute was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court which upheld the constitutionality of a Florida statute that made sexual intercourse with a minor under the age of 16 a crime was approved. The state supreme court affirmed one petitioner's conviction and remanded the other petitioners' case for appropriate action, given its determination that the statute was constitutional.

Johnson v. Singletary


No. 83,690, No. 83,701


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


647 So. 2d 106; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 826; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 337



May 19, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Original Proceeding - Petition for Writ of Habeas Corpus, and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County, Joseph Q. Tarbuck, Judge - Case No. 78-1869-C


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Escambia County (Florida), which denied his second motion for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Appellant also requested a stay of his execution and made claims based on newly discovered evidence consisting of an alibi witness and affidavits of four persons who stated that another man confessed to killing the victim and told them appellant was innocent.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and robbery. Although the jury recommended a life sentence, the trial court overrode the recommendation and imposed the death penalty, finding five aggravating factors and no mitigating factors. Appellant challenged the trial court's judgment denying his second motion for postconviction relief filed under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 and requested a stay of his execution. Appellant's claims were predicated on newly discovered evidence, which consisted of an alibi witness and the affidavits of four persons who stated that another man told them that he actually killed the victim and that appellant was innocent. The appellate court ruled that the alibi information was not newly discovered because appellant's lawyers submitted the information as part of a clemency petition and because appellant never testified at trial to being with the alibi witness. However, in view of the impending death warrant, the court ruled that appellant was entitled to an evidentiary hearing to allow the affiants to testify and to allow appellant to demonstrate corroborating circumstances sufficient to establish the trustworthiness of the other man's statements.


OUTCOME: In light of the impending death warrant, the appellate court reversed the order denying appellant's motion for new trial and remanded for a prompt evidentiary hearing on the claims surrounding the alleged confessions. The court denied the motion for postconviction relief in all other respects but granted the motion for stay of execution.

Groover v. State


No. 79,199


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


640 So. 2d 1077; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 652; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 249



May 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied August 15, 1994. Released for Publication August 15, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, R. Hudson Olliff, Judge - Case No. 82-1659CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a Circuit Court of Duval County (Florida) judgment, denying his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion to vacate judgment and sentence on his three first-degree murder convictions and multiple death sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of three counts of first-degree murder and sentenced to death on two counts and life imprisonment on the third count. After the sentences and convictions were affirmed, defendant filed a motion to vacate judgment and sentence pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, alleging denial of due process, denial of full and fair hearing, failure to consider nonstatutory mitigating factors, and sentencing errors. Court held that lower court properly considered nonstatutory mitigation in its sentencing, as shown by its overruling of only one of the jury's recommended two life sentences despite no statutory mitigating factors and its instruction of the jury on consideration of such nonstatutory factors. Further, court held no due process problems in denial of defendant's motion, since defendant's counsel had opportunity to argue all issues in its brief and at a hearing prior to signing of the order.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed lower court's judgment, finding that since lower court had instructed the jury on nonstatutory mitigating factors and had not overruled both life sentences recommended by the jury, there was no failure to consider such factors, and further holding that no due process or other claims had any merit.

Keen v. State


No. 71,358


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


639 So. 2d 597; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 653; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 243



May 5, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 14, 1994. Released for Publication July 14, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Patti Englander Henning, Judge. Case No. 84-9474CF-10.



DISPOSITION: We reverse Keen's conviction for first-degree murder of Anita Lopez Keen and his death sentence. We remand for a retrial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Broward County (Florida), convicting defendant of first-degree murder and imposing a sentence of death, after it was found that defendant pushed his wife overboard about 15 to 18 miles offshore in order to collect on two insurance policies.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pushed his wife overboard about 15 to 18 miles offshore. Defendant had intended to collect on two insurance policies that carried double indemnity provisions in case of accidental death. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder. The jury recommended death by a seven-to-five vote. The trial judge followed the jury's recommendation and sentenced defendant to death. The Supreme Court reversed both the conviction and the death sentence. The court could not say beyond a reasonable doubt that the presence of an unauthorized magazine article in the jury room did not prejudice the jurors. The trial judge exacerbated the error by questioning the jurors about their thought processes during the guilt-phase deliberations. In addition, the trial court erred by not disclosing or conducting an in-camera inspection of an essential witness's grand jury testimony.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were reversed because the jurors may have been prejudiced by an unauthorized magazine article in the jury room. The trial judge exacerbated the error by questioning the jurors about their thought process during the guilt-phase deliberations.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After remand for resentencing, defendant appealed from a Circuit Court of Hillsborough County (Florida) judgment, convicting him of first-degree murder and sentencing him to death, arguing numerous grounds, including errors in jury selection and evidence.

OUTCOME: Court affirmed lower court's judgment, holding that defendant's argument regarding sexual battery as an aggravating circumstance was meritless, finding that the juror challenges were proper where race-neutral reasons for exclusion were on record and lower court properly used its discretion, and holding that remaining arguments were without merit.

Vining v. State


No. 75,915


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


637 So. 2d 921; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 620; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 251



April 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 23, 1994. Released for Publication June 23, 1994.
Writ of certiorari denied Vining v. Florida, 513 U.S. 1022, 115 S. Ct. 589, 130 L. Ed. 2d 502, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 8438 (1994)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Vining v. Crosby, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 77028 (M.D. Fla., Oct. 15, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Joseph P. Baker, Judge - Case No. CR 89-2395.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant death row prisoner contested his first-degree murder and armed robbery convictions and his sentence of death from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed both appellant's first-degree murder and armed robbery convictions and his death sentence. It found that even though he filed a number of motions, the original trial date was never changed. Thus, no delay was attributed to his motion practice and the lower court properly denied appellant's motion for discharge. Further, the judge did not abuse his discretion in limiting the scope of questioning during voir dire. The sentencing order included a specific evaluation of nine nonstatutory mitigating factors proposed by appellant and the record supported the court's conclusion that the other proposed factors were not established by evidence or were not of a mitigating nature. Yet, the court found that the murder was not cold, calculated, and premeditated because the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant had a careful plan or prearranged design, and thus, the lower court erred in finding that aggravating circumstance. But where the lower court would have imposed the same sentence even if it had not found the aggravating circumstance, the court held the error harmless.


OUTCOME: In affirming appellant's first-degree murder and armed robbery convictions and attendant sentences, it found that there was no delay attributable to his motion practice, that there was no abuse of discretion in limiting voir dire questioning, that the record supported the mitigating factors found, and that application of one aggravating factor was in error. However, because the sentence would have been imposed regardless, the error was harmless.

 

270 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Republican Party v. Smith


No. 83,249


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


638 So. 2d 26; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 624; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 224



April 28, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 16, 1994. Released for Publication June 16, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, F. E. Steinmeyer, III, Judge, Case No. 93-3449 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 94-403.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Fla. Const. art. V, § 3(b)(5), the First District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified for review the trial court's order that upheld the constitutionality of the Election Campaign Financing Trust Fund statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 106.32(1), which provided a source for matching political campaign funds.


OVERVIEW: A campaign finance act, Fla. Stat. ch. 106.30-106.36 (1991), was created to provide matching public funds to state office candidates. An election trust fund was created, originally funded by legislative appropriation. The election law was amended to provide for the transfer of general revenue monies to the trust fund if necessary. Fla. Stat. ch. 106.32(1) (1991). Appellant political party challenged the statute as unconstitutional. The trial court upheld the statute, and the appellate court certified the issue for review. Affirming the trial court's order, the supreme court found that the statute, which used a formula rather than a set specific dollar amount to fund the trust, was a valid appropriation of public monies, notwithstanding the use of the word "transfer" instead of "appropriation." The statute was general substantive legislation not confined by the appropriation statutes. Fla. Stat. ch. 216.011(1)(b), (c). The statutory scheme served to specify, control, and limit the funds transferred. The statute was not bound by the constitutional itemization requirement, Fla. Const. art. III, § 19(b), where that provision did not take effect until after the statute was enacted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order finding that the Election Campaign Financing Trust Fund statute provided a constitutionally valid appropriation from the general revenue fund where necessary to provide matching funds to state political candidates, and held that the statute upheld the legislature's intent to fund the Election Campaign Financing Act.

 

271 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Gas Transmission Co. v. Public Serv. Comm'n


No. 82,171


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


635 So. 2d 941; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 566; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 207



April 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Public Service Commission.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant gas company challenged an order of the Florida Public Service Commission in which the commission determined that a need existed for a second natural gas transmission pipeline in peninsular Florida and that the pipeline proposed was the appropriate project to fill the need.


OVERVIEW: A natural gas company filed an application for a determination of need with the Florida Public Service Commission (Commission), pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 403.9422, seeking permission to construct a major natural gas transmission system. Appellant, a gas company that controlled the only other natural gas pipeline serving the area, opposed the need determination. After a hearing, the Commission issued its final order in which it found that there was a demand for additional natural gas capacity and that the proposed pipeline was the appropriate project to fill the need. Appellant challenged the order claiming that Fla. Stat. ch. 403.9422 was unconstitutional and that the Commission failed to explain its rejection of certain proposed findings of fact. The court determined that Fla. Stat. ch. 403.9422 was constitutional because it provided sufficient guidelines to overcome a claim that the legislature unconstitutionally delegated its power to the Public Service Commission. Moreover, the court concluded that the Commission's findings of fact were sufficient. Therefore, the court affirmed the order of the Commission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Florida Public Service Commission's (Commission) order. The court found that the authorizing statute was constitutional and that the order of the Commission was proper.

Hendrix v. State


No. 79,048


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


637 So. 2d 916; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 571; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 227



April 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1994. Released for Publication June 21, 1994.
Writ of certiorari denied Hendrix v. Florida, 513 U.S. 1004, 115 S. Ct. 520, 130 L. Ed. 2d 425, 1994 U.S. LEXIS 8091 (1994)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Hendrix v. State, 908 So. 2d 412, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1463 (Fla., 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hendrix v. McDonough, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 32657 (M.D. Fla., May 1, 2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at Hendrix v. State, 2014 Fla. LEXIS 1210 (Fla., Apr. 10, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Notice and Cross-Notice of Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Lake County, Jerry T. Lockett, Judge - Case No. 90-1297 CFA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment and sentence of the Circuit Court in and for Lake County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder, armed burglary, and conspiracy, and which imposed the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Appellant planned with his girlfriend to kill his cousin because the cousin had agreed to testify against appellant in connection with a burglary. Appellant ultimately murdered both his cousin and his cousin's wife. The jury recommended death for each murder and the trial court imposed the death penalty for each. On appeal, appellant challenged his convictions and sentences. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. Appellant first argued that the trial court judge erred in refusing to recuse himself because of conversations he had prior to becoming a judge with the attorney for appellant's girlfriend. The court determined that the judge had violated neither Fla. Stat. ch. 38.02 (1989) nor Fla. Code of Judicial Conduct Canon 3(c) by refusing to recuse himself because the record showed no evidence of the appearance of an improper interest. The court, however, agreed with appellant that there was insufficient evidence to support convictions for two counts of conspiracy. The court noted that there was a single express agreement to commit a criminal act. Moreover, the fact that another person was also killed at the scene did not render the agreement a double conspiracy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, holding that the trial court judge did not err in refusing to recuse himself. However, the court reversed the second conspiracy conviction and vacated the corresponding thirty-year sentence because there was only a single express agreement to commit a criminal act.

State v. Townsend


No. 81,263


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


635 So. 2d 949; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 573; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 202



April 21, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fifth District - Case No. 91-1396 (Brevard County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The prosecution sought review of the decision the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida), which held that incompetency under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.603 did not render a witness unavailable for purposes of Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(23) and a child's statements regarding sexual abuse should not have been admitted.


OVERVIEW: Respondent father was convicted of sexual battery on his two-year old daughter. On appeal, the lower court held that incompetency was not the equivalent of unavailability for purposes of admitting the child's statements under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(23), and, as such, that the child's statements were improperly admitted, ordered a new trial and certified the following question as one of great public importance. The certified question was whether a finding of incompetency to testify because one was unable to recognize the duty to tell the truth satisfied the unavailable requirement of Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(23)(a)(2). The court held that an incompetent witness was unavailable within the meaning of Fla. Stat. ch. 90.804(1)(d)'s existing mental infirmity requirement. The court continued that a finding of incompetency to testify because the party was unable to recognize the duty and obligation to tell the truth satisfied the testify or be unavailable requirement of Fla. Stat. ch. 90.803(23).


OUTCOME: The court disagreed with the holding of the lower court and held that the child was unavailable for purposes of the introduction of her statements under the child hearsay exception. However, given the other errors in this case, the court approved of the lower court's decision to remand this cause for a new trial.


 

274 of 1586 DOCUMENTS



Feller v. State


No. 81,771


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


637 So. 2d 911; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 575; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 196



April 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1994. Released for Publication June 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance First District - Case No. 91-1062 (Duval County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal of the First District (Florida) certified questions for review relating to whether or not it was fundamental error for a trial court to fail to make the findings required by Fla. Stat. § 92.53(1) (1989), prior to allowing a child witness to testify by videotape and, if so, could the case be remanded for a determination of whether the record supported the required statutory findings. Petitioner raised other issues.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with three counts of sexual battery. The state filed a motion to allow videotaped testimony of the child victim. Appellant objected. The court allowed the testimony to be videotaped. Appellant raised the same confrontation-right objection when the testimony was videotaped, but failed to object at trial. Appellant was found guilty and moved for a new trial, claiming it was error for the victim to have been allowed to testify by videotape. The motion was denied. The appellate court affirmed but certified the question as to whether the trial court's failure to make the required findings under Fla. Stat. § 92.53(1) (1989), prior to allowing the child to testify by videotape, was fundamental error and, if so, could the case be remanded for a determination of whether the record supported the required statutory findings. The court found the trial court's failure to make the statutorily required findings was not fundamental error. The court did not answer the second question, but remanded on the basis that the trial court erred in allowing an expert witness to comment on the child's veracity and in allowing hearsay statements made by the child to investigators.


OUTCOME: The decision of the appellate court was quashed and the case remanded with directions to reverse the judgment of conviction and order a new trial. The failure to make the statutorily required findings did not constitute fundamental error. Reversal was warranted because the trial court admitted testimony of a child abuse expert witness that vouched for the child's truthfulness and also admitted statements made by the victim to investigators.

Jackson v. State


No. 79,509


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


648 So. 2d 85; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 576; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 215



April 21, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied October 13, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Fla. LEXIS 1546.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Donald R. Moran, Judge - Case No. 83-4600 CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner challenged her conviction of first-degree murder from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant prisoner was convicted of first-degree murder for the killing of a police officer and she was sentenced to death. Prisoner argued that the jury instruction on the cold, calculated, and premeditated (CCP) factor was unconstitutionally vague. The lower court instructed prisoner's jury that it could have considered, if established by the evidence, that the crime for which the prisoner was to have been sentenced was committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner without any pretense of moral or legal justification. The court noted that this standard instruction, which mirrored the language of Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(i), was previously upheld by this court. Upon reconsideration, the court held that in order to have found the CCP aggravating factor the jury must have determined that the killing was the product of cool and calm reflection and not an act prompted by emotional frenzy, panic, or a fit of rage and that the prisoner had a careful plan or prearranged design to commit murder before the fatal incident and that the prisoner exhibited heightened premeditation and that prisoner had no pretense of moral or legal justification. Sentence was vacated and remanded.


OUTCOME: Appellant prisoner's sentence for first-degree murder was vacated and remanded for a new sentencing proceeding. The court held that the jury instruction that the lower court had given on the cold, calculated, and premeditated was unconstitutionally vague.

County of Pasco v. Riehl


No. 82,098


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


635 So. 2d 17; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 489; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 183



April 14, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Second District - Case No. 92-02705.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county appealed a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida) declaring Fla. Stat. Ann. § 767.12 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant dog owners' dog bit a child who was visiting their home. The child's mother filed a dangerous dog affidavit, and animal control issued a notice of dangerous dog classification pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 767.12. Defendants sought an injunction preventing plaintiff county from issuing this classification, and the trial court affirmed. Plaintiff appealed, and the appellate court affirmed, holding that the statute allowed substantial restrictions and penalties to be placed upon defendants' use and enjoyment of their property without affording an opportunity to a prior hearing on the matter. The appellate court held that this failure to afford defendants an opportunity to be heard rendered the statute unconstitutional. The court agreed and affirmed the decision. The court held that defendants suffered a deprivation of property without benefit of a hearing and that such deprivation was a violation of their procedural due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision, holding that the dangerous dog classification statute was unconstitutional because it deprived defendant dog owners of their property without affording an opportunity to a prior hearing on the matter.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court, Duval County (Florida), convicting him of first-degree murder and imposing a sentence of death.

OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of first-degree murder and sentencing him to death, holding that the trial court erred in prohibiting defendant from waiving the statute of limitations defense when he requested instruction on the time-barred lesser-included offenses.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Circuit Court for Volusia County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed from his conviction for first-degree murder. The trial judge imposed the death penalty and defendant sought to have his pleas withdrawn for a new penalty phase proceeding or imposition of a life sentence. Defendant claimed that his guilty plea was illegally entered in order to stop the harassment of his family by the state. The court ruled that the record was devoid of proof of any good case for withdrawal. The court also held that the trial court erred in finding that the murder was committed to avoid arrest. The record contained no competent evidence showing the presence of this aggravating factor, but rather it contained evidence that the murder took place as the result of a spontaneous fight. Accordingly, the court affirmed defendant's convictions for solicitation and first-degree murder and the 30-year sentences on the solicitation counts. However, it vacated the death sentence and remanded for imposition of life imprisonment without parole for 25 years on the murder count.


OUTCOME: The trial court imposed the death sentence on defendant after his conviction for murder. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the death sentence because there were no aggravating factors.

Doe v. State


No. 79,508


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


634 So. 2d 613; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 457; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 149



March 31, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions Second District - Case No. 91-02739 (Polk County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court accepted an application for review of a decision from the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed a ruling that the state violated petitioner's U.S. Const. amend. IV rights by accosting petitioner for purposes of gaining her fingerprints.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was served with a subpoena in conjunction with an investigation conducted by the state attorney. The subpoena required petitioner to supply fingerprint samples and handwriting exemplars. The trial court concluded that the subpoena violated petitioner's U.S. Const. amend. IV right to privacy. The district court of appeal reversed the decision because it determined a subpoena for fingerprinting and voice exemplars violated no constitutional rights. The state supreme court approved the district court of appeal's decision and disapproved a conflicting decision. The court held that the state had a strong interest in gathering information relevant to an initial inquiry into suspected criminal activity, whether through use of the grand jury subpoena power or that of the statutorily empowered state attorney. Neither the directive compelling petitioner's attendance to obtain the exemplars nor the actual obtaining of the exemplars violated her privacy rights under U.S. Const. amend. IV.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court of appeal reversing the decision that the state's subpoena of petitioner for the purposes of acquiring her fingerprints was unconstitutional was approved. The state supreme court disapproved a conflicting case because petitioner did not have a privacy right in her fingerprints.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state department of revenue sought review of a decision from the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which declared Fla. Stat. ch. 212.0505 (Supp. 1988) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Fla. Stat. ch. 212.0505 (Supp. 1988) required those involved with marijuana transactions to report their income. Those engaged in legal sales were assessed a six percent tax and those engaged in illegal transactions were assessed a 50 percent tax. Respondent taxpayer was assessed a tax and penalty after he was discovered with 300 pounds of marijuana. Respondent sought review of the assessment. The trial court reversed petitioner state tax department of revenue's order and found that the statute violated the privilege against self-incrimination. Petitioner sought review, and the court affirmed, finding that the statute violated the U.S. Const. amend. V prohibition against self-incrimination because it caused the claimant to be confronted with a substantial hazard of incrimination even though there was a confidentiality provision. The court found that the confidentiality provision was undermined by Fla. Stat. ch. 213.053(8) and did not adequately protect the taxpayer from risk of self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision reversing petitioner state department of revenue's assessment against respondent taxpayer, and found that the statute that imposed a sales tax on marijuana transactions was unconstitutional because it did not protect the taxpayer from self-incrimination.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner psychologists sought review of an order from the First District Court of Appeal, Leon County (Florida), which found that respondent psychological association had no authority to waive the educational requirements for licensure in an effort to settle petitioners' lawsuit, which challenged the constitutionality of state licensing statutes.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner psychologists challenged an order, which found that respondent psychological association had no authority to waive the educational requirements for licensure in an effort to settle petitioners' lawsuit. Holland v. State


No. 78,660


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


636 So. 2d 1289; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 412; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 142



March 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 9, 1994. Released for Publication June 9, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, M. Daniel Futch, Jr., Judge - Case No. 90-15905CF10.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder of a law enforcement officer, armed robbery, sexual battery, and attempted first-degree murder and sentenced him to death. Appellant claimed that the trial court erred in overruling defense counsel's objections to the testimony of a state witness who testified at the competency hearing and at trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder of a law enforcement officer and several other offenses, and was sentenced to death. On appeal, appellant claimed that the trial court erred in overruling defense counsel's objections to the testimony of a state witness who testified at the competency hearing and at trial. The appellate court reversed and remanded appellant's convictions. The court ruled that appellant's evaluation by a psychiatrist at the county jail was acceptable to determine whether he needed further mental health evaluation or could be put into the general population. However, defense counsel was entitled to notice because the psychiatrist was the state's key witness at appellant's competency hearing. The court ruled that lack of notice would not have been a problem if the witness's testimony was confined to his observations of appellant, as opposed to his expert opinions about appellant's competency and sanity. Because it was not, the lack of notice violated Fla. Const. art. I, § 9 and appellant's U.S. Const. amend. VI right to consult with counsel. The witness's testimony as to appellant's sanity violated appellant's U.S. Const. amend. V right to remain silent.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed and remanded appellant's convictions and death sentence because the state violated appellant's constitutional rights by failing to give defense counsel notice of its intention to have a witness evaluate appellant and testify regarding issues of competency. The court noted that the witness was crucial because the court-appointed mental health experts testified that appellant was incompetent.

Allen v. State


No. 79,003


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


636 So. 2d 494; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 409; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 139



March 24, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 23, 1994. Released for Publication May 23, 1994.
Post-conviction proceeding at Allen v. State, 2014 Fla. App. LEXIS 18527 (Fla. Dist. Ct. App. 5th Dist., Nov. 14, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Martin Budnick, Judge - Case No. 91-72-CFC.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which imposed a death sentence on defendant after he was convicted of murder, armed robbery, possession of a short-barreled shotgun, and grand theft. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in admitting statements obtained from electronic eavesdropping of appellant and a co-defendant in their prison cells and in sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder, armed robbery, possession of a short-barreled shotgun, and grand theft of an automobile. The trial court sentenced appellant to death. On appeal, appellant contended the trial court erred in admitting evidence obtained from electronic eavesdropping of statements he and a co-defendant made in their prison cells and in sentencing him to death because he was 15 years old at the time of the crime. The appellate court ruled that the trial court did not err in admitting the jailhouse conversation because there was neither improper police involvement in inducing the conversation, nor any intrusion into a privileged or otherwise confidential or private communication. The court noted that voluntary jailhouse conversations between inmates were not entitled to the same degree of privacy afforded some other communications. However, the court ruled that the death penalty was either cruel or unusual if imposed upon one who was under the age of 16 when he committed the crime and, thus, was prohibited by Fla. Const. art. I, § 17. The court vacated the death sentence and reduced it to life imprisonment without possibility of parole for 25 years.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions for murder, armed robbery, possession of a short-barrel shotgun, and grand theft but vacated the death penalty and reduced it to life imprisonment without possibility of parole for 25 years. The court ruled that a jailhouse conversation was properly admitted but that the imposition of the death penalty was cruel or unusual because appellant was under the age of 16 when he committed the crime.

In re Advisory Opinion to the Atty. Gen.


No. 82,674


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


632 So. 2d 1018; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 314; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 109



March 3, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Attorney General petitioned for an advisory opinion regarding a proposed amendment to Fla. Const. art. I, § 10 pursuant to Fla. Const. art. IV, § 10 and Fla. Stat. ch. 16.061 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Fla. Const. art. IV, § 10 and Fla. Stat. ch. 16.061 (1993), the Attorney General petitioned the court for an advisory opinion on the validity of a proposed amendment to Fla. Const. art. I, § 10. The proposed amendment would prevent the state from passing any law regarding discrimination that would establish a right or privilege based upon a characteristic, trait, status, or condition other than race, color, religion, sex, national origin, handicap, ethnic background, marital status, or familial status. The supreme court declined to place the proposed amendment on the ballot because it embraced more than one subject and matter, in violation of Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3. The proposed amendment violated the single-subject requirement because it enumerated ten classifications of people that would be entitled to protection, and it covered both civil rights and the powers of the state and local governments. The court also held that the ballot summary regarding the proposed amendment failed to adequately describe the amendment and it was ambiguous in that it was confusing to voters, in violation of Fla. Stat. ch.101.161(1) (1993).


OUTCOME: The court struck the initiative petition and ballot summary because the proposed amendment violated the single-subject provision of the state constitution and the ballot summary failed to comply with constitutional and statutory legal requirements.
