State v. Stalder


No. 79,924, 80,126


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


630 So. 2d 1072; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 76; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 56



January 27, 1994, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Broward County, J. Leonard Fleet, Judge, Case Nos. 91-18929 CF10A & 90-25471 CF - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Case Nos. 92-01417 & 92-01432.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state appealed an order of the Trial Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which declared Florida's Hate Crimes Statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.085 (1989), unconstitutional and granted respondent's pretrial motion to dismiss the enhancement charge against him under the statute.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the order of the trial court and held that Florida's Hate Crimes Statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.085 (1989), was constitutional. The statute required a penalty enhancement when the commission of a crime evidenced prejudice based on certain enumerated characteristics of the victim. Respondent was charged with simple battery. Respondent's penalty was reclassified as a hate crime, thus, it went from a first-degree misdemeanor for simple battery to a third-degree felony. Petitioner argued that the enhancement was appropriate because respondent selected his victim based on ethnicity. The trial court granted respondent's motion to dismiss the enhancement and held that the hate crime statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that the statute was constitutional because it targeted criminal acts in which the selection of the victim was an integral part of the underlying crime. Therefore, the conduct was not speech but fell outside the protection of U.S. Const. amend. I and could be banned. The court quashed the trial court's order finding that the statute unconstitutional and remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the trial court's order that found that a state's hate crimes statute was unconstitutional and dismissed the charge against respondent. The court remanded the action for further proceedings with respect to respondent's sentencing enhancement under the statute.

 

288 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


No. 81,189, No. 81,724, No. 81,725


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


629 So. 2d 841; 1994 Fla. LEXIS 5; 19 Fla. L. Weekly S 22



January 6, 1994, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Three Cases Consolidated: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity First District - Case No. 91-2435 (Bay County) and two Appeals from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Second District - Case Nos. 91-03496, 91-03529, 91-03530, 91-03653, 91-03657, 91-03665, 91-03673, 91-03678, 91-03747, 91-03748, 91-03982, 91-04185, 92-01902.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First District Court of Appeal and the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) applied for review of three cases that involved the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13(1)(i), which imposed enhanced penalties for controlled substances violations within 200 feet of a public housing facility.


OVERVIEW: Three defendants were charged separately under Fla. Stat. ch. 893.13.(1)(i), which imposed enhanced penalties for controlled substances violations within 200 feet of a public housing facility. The statute was found unconstitutionally vague in the actions against two of the defendants and was found constitutional in the action against the third defendant. Two district courts of appeal applied for review of the decisions regarding the constitutionality of ch. 893.13(1)(i). The supreme court held that the statute was facially invalid under the void-for-vagueness doctrine. The supreme court determined that the phrase "public housing facility" was so imprecise that it was impossible to tell from the statute's plain language what conduct the legislature intended to target. Citizens did not have fair warning about what conduct was forbidden. As a result, arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement was likely. The supreme court affirmed the two court of appeal decisions which found the statute unconstitutional and quashed the decision which found the statute constitutional. The case in which the decision was quashed was remanded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed two decisions in which a statute that imposed enhanced penalties for controlled substances violations was found unconstitutional. The court quashed a third decision, which found the statute constitutional, and remanded. The court found the statute unconstitutional under the void-for-vagueness test where the phrase "public housing facility" was so imprecise that it was impossible to tell what the legislature intended to target.

Lopez v. Dugger

291 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Eller v. Shova


No. 80,776


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


630 So. 2d 537; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1933; 9 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 355; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 626



December 9, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied February 8, 1994. Released for Publication February 8, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity Second District - Case No. 91-02087.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the coworkers of the deceased, challenged the decision of the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida), which reversed the trial court's order that dismissed appellee executor's negligence action and found Fla. Stat. ch. 440.11(1) (Supp. 1988) unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. 1, § 21.


OVERVIEW: Appellee executor, the husband of an employee killed in the parking lot of the employer's store, sued appellants, the co-workers of deceased, for negligence for failing to take precautions to prevent his wife's death. The trial court dismissed appellee's complaint, finding that under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.11(1) (Supp. 1988), that appellee's exclusive remedy was workers' compensation benefits and that appellants were immune from liability absent allegations that appellants had committed a criminal offense identified in ch. 440.11(1). The district court reversed the trial court, ruling that the amendment to ch. 440.11(1) unconstitutionally limited access to the courts in violation of Fla. Const. art. 1, § 21. The court quashed the district court's decision and directed the trial court to dismiss appellee's complaint. The court found that ch. 440.11(1), as amended, was not unconstitutional because it merely limited the liability of coemployees to actions of gross negligence; it did not abolish a right to redress for an injury. The court further held that even if the amendment to ch. 440.11(1) had abolished a remedy, it provided a reasonable alternative.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the district court's decision because a law providing workers' compensation benefits as the exclusive remedy for the ordinary negligence of coemployees was constitutional in that it did not eliminate an existing remedy. The court remanded to the trial court with directions to dismiss appellee executor's complaint.

Ferguson v. Singletary


No. 80,549


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


632 So. 2d 53; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1934; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 630



December 9, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Revised February 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.
Ferguson v. State, 474 So. 2d 208, 1985 Fla. LEXIS 3387 (Fla., 1985)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After petitioner prisoner's convictions on eight counts of murder and the imposition of eight death sentences, in two cases petitioner filed a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In separate cases, petitioner prisoner was convicted and was sentenced to death on eight counts of murder. The convictions and sentences were affirmed. Petitioner's motion for relief, under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850, was denied. Subsequently, petitioner filed a writ of habeas corpus. Regarding petitioner's claim that he was entitled to a new sentencing hearing based on the fact that a substitute judge sentenced petitioner on remand, the court held that evolutionary developments in the law regarding the application of Florida's death penalty statute were not retroactively applied to final judgments. Furthermore, the court held that the claim was procedurally barred because petitioner failed to preserve the issue for review. Petitioner's claims regarding jury instructions on the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator were also procedurally barred based on petitioner's failure to raise the issue during the direct appeal. Finally, the court held that petitioner failed to establish ineffective assistance of the appellate counsel because petitioner failed to prove that there was either deficient performance or prejudice to petitioner. Therefore, the writ of habeas corpus was denied.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner prison's writ of habeas corpus because petitioner failed to establish ineffective assistance of his appellate counsel, and petitioner's other claims were procedurally barred because petitioner failed to preserve the issues for review.

 

293 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Rogers & Ford Constr. Corp. v. Carlandia Corp.


No. 80,788


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


626 So. 2d 1350; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1815; 62 U.S.L.W. 2348; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 592



November 10, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 91-2142 (Palm Beach County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Palm Beach County (Florida), which found that plaintiff had standing to sue defendants for damages arising from 33 alleged defects or deficiencies in various common areas or elements of the condominium.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff sued defendants, the developer and general contractor of a condominium unit that it had purchased, for damages arising from 33 alleged defects or deficiencies in various common areas or elements of the condominium, but did not allege any defects in the individual unit. Defendants argued that plaintiff had no standing to sue because Fla. Stat. § 718 (1991), gave only the condominium association the right to sue for damages to common elements of the condominium. The trial court held that plaintiff had standing to sue defendants. The Supreme Court held that a condominium owner has standing to maintain an action for construction defects in the common areas or common elements of the condominium. In addition, the interests of the other unit owners must be represented in the suit of the unit owner with standing to maintain the action.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was affirmed because plaintiff had standing to sue defendants for construction defects in the common areas or common elements of the condominium. The interests of the other unit owners were required to be represented in the suit of the unit owner with standing to sue.

 

294 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. Carmar Structural


No. 80,679


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


629 So. 2d 117; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1816; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 590



November 10, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 5, 1994. Released for Publication January 5, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 91-2649.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner worker sought review of a District Court of Appeal for the First District (Florida) judgment, upholding the calculation used by respondents companies pursuant to the Florida Workman's Compensation Law, Fla. Stat. ch. 440.15(3)(b) (1990), to determine wage-loss benefits, arguing the statute was inapplicable at the time of injury.


OVERVIEW: After petitioner worker suffered an industrial injury and performed an unsuccessful search for employment, respondents companies calculated his wage-loss benefits based on Florida Workmen's Compensation Law, Fla. Stat. ch. 440.15(3)(b) (1990). Petitioner filed suit based on the relevant statute's having been declared unconstitutional due to violation of the single-subject rule by addressing both workers' compensation and international trade, and on review the calculation was upheld. Petitioner appealed. Court held that the substantive rights of petitioner were fixed as of the time of injury. Further, court held that since the earlier statute had been declared unconstitutional because of the form of its enactment rather than because the legislature lacked power to enact it, and since the curative statutes in question had been expressly made applicable retroactively to the effective date of the statute, the statute in question was in effect at the time of petitioner's accident.


OUTCOME: Court affirmed lower court's judgment, holding that the statute in question had been declared unconstitutional because of its violation of the single-subject rule rather than because the legislature lacked power to enact it, and the legislature had cured this error, making the curative statute retroactive.

 

295 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


In re Dubreuil


No. 80,311


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


629 So. 2d 819; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1761; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 575



November 4, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied January 20, 1994. Released for Publication January 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Constitutional Construction Fourth District - Case No. 90-1295. (Broward County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, married, but separated, sought discretionary review from a decision of the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District, Broward County (Florida), arguing that a violation of state and federal constitutional rights of privacy, bodily self determination, and religious freedom occurred where she was compelled to receive medical treatment against her religious beliefs because her death would abandon four minor children.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing the lower court's mandate that appellant receive a blood transfusion to prevent the abandonment of her four minor children, the court quashed the order, finding that no abandonment was proven to override appellant's constitutional rights. It held that it was not appropriate for a hospital to assert state interests to defeat a patient's decision to forgo emergency medical treatment. Further, it found that appellant's rejection of a blood transfusion did not constitute abandonment of her minor children. The law presumed that had appellant died under these circumstances, her husband would have become the sole legal guardian of the couple's children. As there was no evidence presented that he was unable or unwilling to care for the children, the lower court erred in holding that sufficient evidence was presented to override appellant's constitutional right to refuse medical treatment. Moreover, it erred by suggesting that absent firsthand proof, the law should presume abandonment.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the lower court's order to transfuse the unwilling appellant, holding that the state's interest in maintaining a home for minor children was not compelling enough to override appellant's constitutional rights and that the state had mistakenly presumed that appellant's potential death would leave the children abandoned when in fact their father would become their guardian.

Operation Rescue v. Women's Health Ctr.


No. 81,905


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


626 So. 2d 664; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1739; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 559



October 28, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Seminole County, Robert B. McGregor, Judge, Case No. 91-2811-CA-16-K - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District, Case No. 93-969.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant anti-abortion group challenged and sought certification from the District Court of Appeal, Fifth District (Florida) of the judgment of a trial court that imposed an amended permanent injunction against appellant from engaging in certain obstructionist or abusive activities against appellees, a women's clinic, its patients, and its staff.


OVERVIEW: Appellant anti-abortion group sought relief from an amended permanent injunction awarded to appellees, a women's clinic, its patients, and its staff, enjoining appellant and its members from certain obstructionist, abusive, harassing, and picketing behaviors that affected appellees. Appellant argued that the injunction violated its constitutional rights to freedom of speech, freedom of association, equal protection, and the free exercise of religion. Focusing mainly on the freedom of speech issue, the court reviewed the injunction on certification. The court first determined that the area included was a public forum and then held that the restrictions were content-neutral and narrowly tailored to serve a significant government interest that left open alternative means of communication. The court also determined that the restrictions were not a prior restraint, were not vague or overbroad, and, because they affected the health, safety, and rights of Florida women, were the least intrusive means possible of protecting the public safety. The court therefore affirmed the amended permanent injunction.


OUTCOME: The amended permanent injunction that prevented appellant anti-abortion group from, among other things, picketing in front of appellee women's clinic. The court held that the injunction was content-neutral, narrowly tailored to serve a significant government interest of protecting the safety of women who sought the health procedure, and left alternative means of communication open to appellant.

 

297 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Munoz v. State


No. 78,900


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


629 So. 2d 90; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1663; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 537



October 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 17, 1993. Released for Publication December 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. First District - Case No. 91-8. (Bay County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner video store owner sought review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), that found that Fla. Stat. ch. 777.201 abolished the objective entrapment test and reversed the trial court's dismissal of criminal charges. Petitioner was charged with two counts of sale or distribution of harmful materials to a person under 18 years of age in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 847.012.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, the owner of a video rental store, was charged with two counts of sale or distribution of harmful materials to a person under 18 years of age in violation of Fla. Stat. ch. 847.012. Petitioner rented two X-rated videotapes to a minor informant as a result of a police operation. The court considered whether Fla. Stat. 777.201 abolished the objective entrapment test that was established through case law. The court found that the objective test was indeed abolished and replaced by a subjective test of whether a criminal defendant had been entrapped by law enforcement. The subjective test involved a shifting burden of proof. However, the court observed that the legislature could not prohibit the judiciary from analyzing whether a petitioner's due process rights under the Fla. Const. art. I, § 9, had been violated. The court concluded that it did not have to reach the due process question because petitioner had been entrapped under the subjective test of Fla. Stat. ch. 777.201 as a matter of law. There was no evidence that petitioner was predisposed to rent inappropriate materials to juveniles or that he would have done so without inducement.


OUTCOME: The court found the objective test for entrapment had been abolished by statute and that petitioner had been entrapped as a matter of law because no evidence of criminal predisposition was presented.

Fla. Bar v. Daniel


Nos. 78,063, 78,065


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


626 So. 2d 178; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1557; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 517



September 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 17, 1993. Released for Publication November 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Original Proceedings - The Florida Bar.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney sought review of complainant state bar association's disciplinary proceeding which, through a referee, found that he was guilty of misconduct with respect to his dealings with clients in two consolidated cases. The referee recommended concurrent 30-day suspensions.


OVERVIEW: Respondent attorney sought review of complainant state bar association's referee's reports in consolidated disciplinary proceedings, which found respondent guilty of misconduct and recommended concurrent 30-day suspensions. The court approved the referee's findings and recommended discipline. The subject proceedings involved respondent allegedly not obtaining court approval of a settlement that was reached with an insurance company for personal injuries sustained by a minor and respondent's failure to effect a public sale after obtaining a judgment in foreclosure for his clients. Respondent contended that there was no evidence to support the referee's findings of fact. However, the court held that when respondent failed to respond to complainant's requests for admissions, the requests were properly deemed admitted. Respondent further asserted that entry of summary judgment was not authorized in disciplinary proceedings. The court held that such a contention was without merit. Under Fla. Bar Rule 3-7.6(e)(1), once a formal complaint had been filed and forwarded to a referee for hearing, the Florida Rules of Civil Procedure applied except where otherwise provided in the rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment of complainant state bar association's referee finding respondent attorney guilty of misconduct and recommending concurrent 30-day suspensions was approved because substantial competent evidence to support the referee's findings in both cases was found, and respondent's contentions were without merit.

Jacobs Wind Elec. Co. v. Dep't of Transp.


No. 80,247


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


626 So. 2d 1333; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1556; 62 U.S.L.W. 2241; 29 U.S.P.Q.2D (BNA) 1763; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 513



September 30, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied December 14, 1993. Released for Publication December 14, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case No. 91-03845.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner patent holder filed an application with the Florida Supreme Court for review of Fla. Const. arts. I § 9 and X § 6(a) and U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV on his taking of property claim and conversion where the case was dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction by the Second District Court of Appeals (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Respondent state agency developed a tidal flow system based on petitioner's patented design. Petitioner designed a tidal flow system to prevent the stagnation of water and the accumulation of debris in waterways through the use of a one-way tidal gate. Petitioner's patent infringement claim in federal court was dismissed because suit against the state was barred by U.S. Const. amend. XI. The lower court found federal patent law preempted petitioner's claims, and the state therefore did not have subject matter jurisdiction. The state supreme court found that Congress did not intend to exclude a remedy simply because U.S. Const. amend. XI granted the state immunity from suit. Because a patent is property, it was protected under the state and federal constitutions, as was petitioner's state constitutional right of access to the state courts.


OUTCOME: The Florida Supreme Court quashed the dismissal by the lower court and remanded because Congress did not intend to preempt state protection of petitioner's state and federally protected property rights, and petitioner had a right of access to the state courts.

Later proceeding at Jackson v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 2776 (Fla., Nov. 14, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Cases Consolidated: An Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus, and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, L. Page Haddock, Judge - Case No. 85-12620-CF
Jackson v. Florida, 488 U.S. 1050, 109 S. Ct. 882, 102 L. Ed. 2d 1005, 1989 U.S. LEXIS 517, 57 U.S.L.W. 3487 (1989)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner under sentence of death, appealed from a decision of he Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which denied his motion under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Petitioner also filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus directly with the court.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was found guilty of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Petitioner was unsuccessful in previous appeals from his conviction and sentence, but he filed an appeal from the trial court's denial of his Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion to vacate the judgment and a petition for writ of habeas corpus. The court noted that it was prospectively allowing hearings on post-conviction motions in capital cases because of the severity of punishment in a death penalty case. However, the court noted that because the rule was prospective it did not apply to petitioner. The court found no other reversible errors that would change the finding of the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravating factor that supported petitioner's death sentence and stated that the evidence clearly established the aggravating factor. Petitioner's habeas corpus petition was found without merit and dismissed. The trial court denial of the Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 post-conviction motion was also affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petitioner's post-conviction relief motion and his request for state habeas corpus relief because, though capital defendants were entitled to hearing on initial post-conviction relief motions, that rule applied prospectively and not to petitioner. The court found that all of petitioner's habeas corpus claims were without merit.

Young v. Dep't of Cmty. Affairs


No. 76,911


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


625 So. 2d 831; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1450; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 476



September 9, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Third District - Case No. 89-661


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners applied for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida) and the issue of which party bears the burden of ultimate persuasion and the burden of going forward with the evidence in an "appeal" to the Florida Land and Water Adjudicatory Commission pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 380.07.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners applied for land clearing permits. The county issued the permits and transmitted copies to the Department of Community Affairs (Department) under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 380.072(1987). The Department appealed those orders to the Florida Land and Water Adjudicatory Commission (commission) and requested that the development orders be reversed as illegal and violative of the provisions of the county land development plan. At a hearing petitioners refused to participate and failed to present any evidence, and the commission denied the permits. On appeal, the order was affirmed. At issue was which party bears the burden of ultimate persuasion and the burden of going forward with the evidence in an "appeal" to the Florida Land and Water Adjudicatory Commission pursuant to § 380.07. The court determined that under the statute, the agency carried the ultimate burden of persuasion and the burden of going forward. The court reasoned that the statutory framework did not address which party carried the burden, and that the burden of proof rested on the party asserting the affirmative before an administrative tribunal. The decision denying the permits was quashed and remanded.


OUTCOME: The decision denying petitioners land clearing permits was quashed and the case was remanded for a new hearing because the agency carried the ultimate burden of persuasion and the burden of going forward.

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied November 17, 1993. Released for Publication November 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, death sentence prisoner, sought his second writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner claimed, inter alia, that his contemporaneous kidnapping conviction could not be considered as a prior violent felony aggravating circumstance, that the jury received a constitutionally inadequate instruction with regard to the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravating factor, and that the felony murder statute violated the U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first degree murder, kidnapping with intent to commit sexual battery, attempted burglary, and two counts of battery and sentenced to death. Finally, the court explained that both petitioner's U.S. Const. amend. VIII claim and pecuniary gain aggravating factor jury instruction claim were procedurally barred because they were not raised at trial or on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner prisoner's second request for a writ of habeas corpus, explaining that his claims were all procedurally barred because they were either previously disposed of by the court or were not preserved for appellate review because they were not raised at trial or on direct appeal.

 

303 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Lopez v. Singletary


Nos. 75,847, 78,228


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


634 So. 2d 1054; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1929; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 633



September 2, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised On Denial of Rehearing December 9, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1451.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and, An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, D. Bruce Levy, Judge - Case No. 83-11553.

Original Opinion of September 2, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1451.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prisoner appealed from the Circuit Court of Dade County (Florida), which denied his motion for post conviction relief. He also petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: A prisoner on death row petitioned the court for a writ of habeas corpus and appealed the trial court's denial of his motion for postconviction relief. The court affirmed the denial of relief. The court found claims of ineffective assistance of counsel had no merit or were procedurally barred. The court also disagreed with petitioner that the state had a duty to produce records of a polygraph examiner and a doctor. The court agreed with the state that access to the personal files that the examiner and the doctor might have had would not further petitioner's cause. The court also denied the petition for habeas corpus. The court remanded for the trial court to inspect in camera those portions of its records that the state attorney's office sealed, so that the court could determine if they were exempt from disclosure. The court ordered that if the documents were not exempt, they were to be disclosed to petitioner, who would be able to file an amended postconviction motion if the documents revealed any new claims.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for habeas corpus, and affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief, but remanded the case for the trial court to inspect in camera portions of its records that the state attorney's office sealed, finding that petitioner should be able to file an amended postconviction motion if the documents revealed any new claims.

 

304 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. State


No. 75,813


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


622 So. 2d 991; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1132; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 417



July 1, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 3, 1993. Released for Publication September 3, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Michael R. Weatherby, Judge - Case Nos. 89-7316-CF, 89-7317-CF, 89-7318-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict, of two counts of first-degree murder and one count of attempted murder and sentenced him to death and 30 years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted and sentenced to death for two counts of first-degree murder and attempted murder. Appellant argued for reversal on grounds of erroneous admission of a witness's prior statement and improper joinder. The court reversed and remanded the convictions and sentences and held that hearsay was a statement, other than one made by the declarant while testifying at the trial or hearing, offered in evidence to prove the truth of the matter asserted. The state used a witness's hearsay statement, not for impeachment purposes, but as substantive evidence. As such, it was inadmissible hearsay. Accordingly, because the improper evidence was such a prominent feature of the trial, the court held that it was unable to find that the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. Moreover, a joinder issue was remanded as being moot because reversal was warranted on the aforementioned grounds. The court also directed that the issue of age mitigation be evaluated upon remand and that a police officer's testimony, concerning appellant's popularity at school because of his hatred for blacks, was irrelevant, inflammatory, and an impermissible comment on character.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing appellant to death for murder and attempted murder was reversed and remanded because the prior inconsistent testimony of a witness, which was purportedly used for impeachment purposes, was, in reality, used substantively and violated the hearsay rule.

 

305 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Dep't of Prof'l Regulation v. Rampell


No. 79,371


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


621 So. 2d 426; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1138; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 374



July 1, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fourth District - Case No. 89-2668 (Palm Beach County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant/cross-appellee challenged a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal, Palm Beach County (Florida) that affirmed the trial court's ruling that held Fla. Stat. ch. 473.317 (1989) was unconstitutional but upheld that constitutionality of the solicitation statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 473.323(1)(l) (1989).


OVERVIEW: When appellee, a certified public accountant (CPA), called two businesses to offer his accounting services, a competing CPA firm filed a complaint against him with appellant board. Appellee then filed a declaratory judgment action, challenging the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 473.323(1)(l) (1989), which prohibited CPAs from engaging in personal solicitation. Appellee also challenged the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 473.317 (1989), which banned CPAs from making a competitive bid for a professional engagement. The trial court declared both statutes unconstitutional, and the lower court affirmed the ruling with respect to the competitive bidding statute but upheld the constitutionality of the solicitation statute. The supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision regarding the competitive bidding statute but quashed the decision with regard to the solicitation statute. The supreme court held that appellant board could regulate the profession of accountancy in an attempt to assure quality audits but that its regulations could not restrict economic expression protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. Both sections were unconstitutional as they restricted commercial speech.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision on the issue of competitive bidding but quashed the lower court's decision with respect to the use of solicitation. The supreme court held that both sections and the regulations enacted thereunder were invalid as unconstitutional restrictions of protected commercial speech in violation of the First Amendment.

 

306 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Perez v. State


No. 76,184


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


620 So. 2d 1256; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1104; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 361



June 24, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Third District - Case No. 89-2024 (Dade County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Third District Court of Appeal (Florida) applied for review of its decision to reverse the trial court's order suppressing evidence of a gun that had been discarded prior to an officer's seizure of petitioner. The district court requested review on the ground that its decision was in direct conflict with a decision decided by another court of appeal.


OVERVIEW: An officer approached petitioner because he believed petitioner was involved in a narcotics transaction. After petitioner ran, the officer caught him and gave him Miranda warnings. The officer recovered a firearm, which petitioner had discarded during the pursuit. Petitioner was charged with carrying a concealed firearm, Fla. Stat. ch. 790.01, and carrying a concealed firearm by a convicted felon, Fla. Stat. ch. 790.23. The trial court granted petitioner's motion to suppress the gun on the ground that it was seized as a direct result of an illegal stop. The court of appeal reversed, holding that the firearm was admissible because it had been abandoned prior to any search. The court of appeal applied for review of its decision on the basis of direct conflict with a Fourth District Court of Appeal decision. Based on a ruling by the United States Supreme Court, the state supreme court approved the court of appeal's reversal. Petitioner was not "seized" within the meaning of U.S. Const. amend. IV when he dropped the gun, and the recovery of the abandoned gun was not the fruit of an unlawful seizure.


OUTCOME: The court approved the court of appeal decision, which reversed the trial court's order suppressing evidence of a gun that had been discarded prior to an officer's seizure of petitioner. The abandoned gun was admissible in petitioner's trial on charges of carrying a concealed weapon because petitioner was not "seized" when he discarded the gun and, thus, the gun was not the fruit of the officer's unlawful investigatory stop.

Crump v. State


No. 74,230


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


622 So. 2d 963; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 974; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 331



June 10, 1993, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, M. Wm. Graybill, Judge - Case No. 88-4056-D.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Raising numerous issues in the guilt and penalty phase of the trial, appellant sought review from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida), which convicted him for murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Police found the nude and strangled bodies of two women. Appellant was identified as a suspect because a witness identified his truck and because plaster casts of the tire tracks found near one of the bodies were similar to those on appellant's truck. Police discovered a restraining device, a hair, and one of the victim's driver's license in appellant's truck. During the trial for the first murder, the state introduced evidence of appellant's murder of the other victim to establish his identity as the killer. The jury found him guilty of first-degree murder, and the trial judge followed the jury recommendation and imposed a death sentence. On appeal, appellant raised numerous issues in the guilt and penalty phase of the trial. The court rejected all of appellant's arguments concerning the guilt phase of the trial, but found that the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant killed with the necessary heightened premeditation. The court held that the case had to be remanded to reweigh the aggravating circumstance of cold, calculated, and premeditated, and the statutory and nonstatutory mitigating circumstances.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for first-degree murder was affirmed, however, the death sentence was vacated and remanded to reweigh the remaining aggravating circumstance and the statutory and nonstatutory mitigating circumstances established in the record.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions, but vacated the sentence and remanded for the imposition of a life sentence without possibility of parole for 25 years, because the trial court erred in the procedures it utilized in sentencing defendant.

Fla. Dep't of Educ. v. Glasser


No. 80,286


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


622 So. 2d 944; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 912; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 301



May 20, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Second District - Case No. 91-02336. (Sarasota County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant department of education sought review of an order from the Second District Court of Appeal, Sarasota County (Florida), which affirmed a declaratory judgment that found Fla. Stat. ch. 236.25(1) (1989) unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. VII, § 9.


OVERVIEW: Appellant department of education sought review of a declaratory judgment that found Fla. Stat. ch. 236.25(1) (1989) unconstitutional under Fla. Const. art. VII, § 9. Appellee school board members had filed the action to determine the constitutionality of the statute and to order appellant tax collector to collect and remit the nonvoted discretionary millage set by appellees. The court reversed the decision and remanded the matter for further proceedings not inconsistent with its opinion. The court found that the constitutional provision that authorized appellees to levy ad valorem taxes was not self-executing because it indicated such authority was limited to such taxes as authorized by law. The court determined that ch. 236.25(1) was the enabling legislation under the constitutional provision and limited the taxing authority of appellees. The court concluded that the constitutional provision and the statute could be harmonized and could co-exist. The court also found it was error not to join appellant board of education as a party to the original declaratory judgment action because appellant tax collector did not really have a vested interest in defending a state statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the declaratory judgment that found unconstitutional the statute pertaining to nonvoted discretionary millage that appellee school board members could levy for current operating expenses. The court determined that the constitutional provision that granted authority to appellees to levy taxes was not self-executing and the statute in question was the enabling legislation for that authority.

Univ. of Miami v. Echarte


No. 78,210


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


618 So. 2d 189; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 829; 26 A.L.R.5th 831; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 284



May 13, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Third District - Case No. 90-982. (Dade County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state university sought review of a decision from the Third District Court of Appeal (Florida), which affirmed the trial court's ruling that Fla. Stat. chs. 766.207 and 766.209 violated the Florida Constitution. Appellee parents sued appellant in a medical malpractice action in which they alleged their daughter was injured by negligent care provided by appellant's hospital's medical providers.


OVERVIEW: Appellee parents of an injured child sought to bring a medical malpractice action against appellant state university. Pursuant to Fla. Stat. chs. 766.207 and 766.209, appellant contended that appellees had to submit their claim to a medical negligence arbitration panel. Appellees filed a declaratory action questioning the constitutionality of the provisions. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellees because it determined the statutes were unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed. On appeal to the state supreme court, the appellate court's decision was reversed and remanded. The court held that the statutes which provided a monetary cap on noneconomic damages in medical malpractice claims when a party requested arbitration did not violate a claimant's right of access to the courts because they provided a commensurate benefit to plaintiffs in exchange for the monetary cap. Further, the legislature had reasonably concluded that the high cost of malpractice insurance made such measures necessary and unavoidable.


OUTCOME: The decision of the lower court finding medical malpractice arbitration statutes unconstitutional was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court held that the medical malpractice arbitration statutes did not deprive plaintiffs of their right to access to the courts.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which convicted him, upon a jury verdict, for the crimes of kidnapping and first-degree murder, and sentenced him to death.

313 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


B.J.Y. v. M.A.


No. 79,396


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


617 So. 2d 1061; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 711; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 265



April 29, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance and an Appeal from the District Court of Appeal. First District - Case No. 91-2901. (Duval County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed from order of District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), which denied petition for certiorari from decision granting defendant man's request for jury trial in paternity suit and declaring Fla. Stat. Ann. § 742.031 (1991) unconstitutional, and District Court of Appeal certified the question of statute's constitutionality.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff mother sued defendant man seeking a determination of paternity and an award of child support under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 742.031 (1991). Defendant requested a jury trial. The trial judge granted his request, finding § 742.031 unconstitutional because it denied defendant the right to jury trial as guaranteed by Fla. Const. art. I, § 22. The appellate court denied a petition for certiorari and certified to the court the question of the constitutionality of the statute. The court held that the Florida Constitution preserved the right to jury trial in paternity proceedings and declared unconstitutional that portion of § 742.031 that required paternity proceedings to be tried by the judge. The Florida Constitution guaranteed a right to jury trial in those cases where, at the time of the adoption of the constitution, the law gave that right. Before the Florida Constitution became effective, the Bastardy Act of 1828 permitted a woman to sue the alleged father of her illegitimate child and obtain child support. Under that act, the issue of paternity was to be tried before a jury. Accordingly, the Florida Constitution preserved the right to jury trial in paternity proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court held the Florida Constitution preserved the right to jury trial in paternity proceedings because, prior to adoption of the Constitution, there was a right to jury trial in paternity proceedings. It declared unconstitutional that portion of the statute that required paternity proceedings to be tried by a judge.

318 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Lite v. State


No. 79,636


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


617 So. 2d 1058; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 669; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 242



April 15, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. Fourth District - Case No. 91-0271. (Broward County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of the decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) that upheld the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 322.055(1) (Supp. 1990), a statute requiring the revocation of a driver's license upon conviction for possession of or trafficking in a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: The trial court refused to enforce Fla. Stat. ch. 322.055(1) (Supp. 1990), which required revocation of petitioner's driver's license after his conviction for cocaine possession, ruling that ch. 322.055(1) was unconstitutional under the substantive due process and equal protection clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The appellate court overruled the decision, and petitioner appealed. Approving the appellate court's decision and finding the statute constitutionally valid, the supreme court ruled that the penalty of license revocation was enacted to deter drug possession and reduce the mobility of those involved in drugs. Because ch. 322.055(1) was rationally related to the legislative goal, substantive due process was not violated. The court found that ch. 322.055(1) was constitutional even where no motor vehicle was used in the crime because Florida law did not require a direct relationship between punishment and offense, and driving was a privilege that could be taken away as a means of meeting a legitimate legislative goal. The court held that because people within the legally formed class were accorded equal treatment under ch. 322.055(1), equal protection was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court approved the appellate court's ruling that the statute requiring the revocation of a driver's license upon conviction of cocaine possession was constitutional, holding that the statute violated neither substantive due process nor equal protection. The case was remanded to the trial court for action consistent with its opinion.

 

319 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. 70,551


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


620 So. 2d 152; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 597; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 238



April 8, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised June 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County, Thomas E. Penick, Jr., Judge - Case No. 85-8933-D.
Davis v. Florida, 505 U.S. 1244, 113 S. Ct. 22, 120 L. Ed. 2d 948, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 4859, 61 U.S.L.W. 3204 (1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the Circuit Court in and for Pinellas County (Florida) convicting him of murder arguing that the jury instruction on the "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravating factor was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The instant action was remanded back the court by the United States Supreme Court because the court's former standard jury instruction on the "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" aggravating factor was held to be constitutionally inadequate. The court, nevertheless, affirmed appellant's death sentence on remand because appellant's argument regarding the vagueness of the jury instruction was barred because it was not raised before the trial judge. Moreover, had the vagueness issue been preserved, the court held that the error would have been harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court recognized that the particular facts of the case regarding the victim's multiple and horrific injuries were so indicative of the aggravating factor "heinous, atrocious, or cruel" that there was no reasonable possibility that the faulty instruction contributed to appellant's sentence. The court held that under any instruction, the jury would have recommended and the judge would have imposed the same sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and death sentence and held that appellant's argument regarding the vagueness of the jury instruction was barred because it was not raised before the trial judge. Moreover, had the argument been raised, the court would have held that the error in giving the instruction was harmless because there was no reasonable possibility that the faulty instruction contributed to appellant's sentence.

 

320 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Baxter v. State


No. 79,993


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


616 So. 2d 47; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 576; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 208



April 1, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions. Second District - Case No. 91-01311. (Hillsborough County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner convict challenged the order of the District Court of Appeal, Second District, Hillsborough County (Florida) sentencing petitioner as a habitual felony offender based upon a prior out-of-state felony conviction pursuant to the authority of Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 (1989), as amended by 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 280.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner convict was sentenced as a habitual felony offender based upon a prior out-of-state felony conviction pursuant to the authority of Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 (1989), as amended by 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 280. In a recent case, the court held that 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 280 was void as violating the single subject rule of the Florida Constitution. The court reversed the lower court's decision to the extent that it permitted petitioner to be sentenced as a habitual felony offender based upon an out-of state conviction because 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 280 was the only authority for considering prior out-of-state felony convictions as the basis for sentencing as a habitual felony offender. Because 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 280 had been declared unconstitutional and because the crime for which petitioner was being sentenced occurred before the effective date of the reenactment of the habitual felony statute, the court held that petitioner did not meet the requirements for being sentenced as a habitual felony offender and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded petitioner's sentence as a habitual felony offender because the statute which allowed petitioner's out-of-state conviction to serve as the basis for his habitual felony sentencing was declared unconstitutional for violating the state's single subject rule. Moreover, the crime for which petitioner was being sentenced occurred before the effective date of the reenactment of the habitual felony statute.

 

321 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Thompson v. State


No. 75,499


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


619 So. 2d 261; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 587; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 212



April 1, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 10, 1993. Released for Publication June 10, 1993.
Writ of certiorari denied Thompson v. Florida, 510 U.S. 966, 114 S. Ct. 445, 126 L. Ed. 2d 378, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 7020 (1993)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Thompson v. State, 759 So. 2d 650, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 742 (Fla., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, S. Peter Capua, Judge - Case No. 76-3350-B.

Original Opinion of June 4, 1992, Reported at 1992 Fla. LEXIS 997.
Thompson v. State, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 997 (Fla., June 4, 1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida) that sentenced him to death after he pled guilty to first-degree murder, kidnapping, and involuntary sexual battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder, kidnapping, and involuntary sexual battery. He was allowed to withdraw his guilty plea. He entered a second guilty plea, and a penalty phase jury recommended the death penalty. Defendant was denied a Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion and federal habeas corpus relief. After defendant's second Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 motion was denied, defendant appealed. The court reversed for a second sentencing proceeding, which resulted in the imposition of the death penalty. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed. Use of the prior testimony of a witness was allowed because the testimony was taken in the course of a judicial proceeding; the party against whom the evidence was offered was a party in the former proceeding; the issues were similar; and a substantial reason was shown why the original witness was not available. Defendant's right to confrontation was not violated by brief cross-examinations because it was only required that he have an opportunity to cross-examine witnesses. The court found it was error to admit autopsy photographs, but such error was harmless given the testimony of eyewitnesses and the medical examiner.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that imposed a death sentence was affirmed because the trial court properly admitted testimony of a witness from an earlier sentencing hearing because that witness was not available, and defendant had an opportunity to cross-examine witnesses.

 

322 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


White v. State


No. 75,571


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


616 So. 2d 21; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 515; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 184



March 25, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, M. Wm. Graybill, Judge - Case No. 89-11078


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his jury trial conviction for first degree murder and jury recommended death penalty sentence imposed by the Hillsborough County Circuit Court (Florida). Appellant alleged trial court errors in both the guilt and penalty phases of trial, with a main focus upon the proportionality of the sentence under these facts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for first degree murder and death penalty sentence imposed. The court considered and rejected as meritless appellant's claims of error in the guilt phase. The court reviewed appellant's claimed trial court errors in the penalty phase. The court agreed with appellant that the trial court erred in both instructing the jury that, and itself concluding that, the murder was committed in a premeditated manner. The court found that while premeditation existed, this aggravating circumstance was not established beyond a reasonable doubt. The court noted that the record showed the mitigating factor of appellant's controlled substance problem and that he murdered victim while intoxicated by cocaine. The court ruled the jury was improperly instructed to consider premeditation as an aggravating circumstance. Therefore, the court decided that the death sentence was disproportionate here because only one aggravating circumstance actually existed, while three mitigating factors applied. The court vacated the death penalty and imposed a life sentence without parole for twenty-five years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's jury trial conviction for first degree murder for appellee, but vacated the jury recommended and trial court imposed death penalty, because it was error to have found premeditation beyond a reasonable doubt and, thus, proportionality warranted the court's imposing a sentence of life without parole for twenty-five years.

Wyche v. State


No. 77,440


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


619 So. 2d 231; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 522; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 171



March 25, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1993. Released for Publication May 26, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Second District - Case No. 88-01141. (Hillsborough County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applied for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida), which affirmed petitioner's conviction for violating an ordinance regarding loitering for the purpose of prostitution.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was arrested after police observed her on a street corner in a skimpy outfit waving to passersby and entering a car that pulled to the curb. She was convicted of loitering for the purpose of prostitution. She appealed, and the court affirmed the conviction and certified the question of whether the ordinance she was convicted under was constitutional. The court found that the ordinance was unconstitutional because it unnecessarily infringed on constitutional rights. The court found it was too vague because a violation of the law is determined based on law enforcement officers' discretion, it violated substantive due process by punishing innocent activities, and it impermissibly provided a greater penalty than that imposed by state statutes for similar criminal conduct. Thus, the court answered the certified question in the negative, quashed that portion of the district's decision relating to the loitering ordinance, and remanded.


OUTCOME: The court found that the ordinance in question was unconstitutional, because it was vague, it violated substantive due process, and impermissibly provided a greater penalty than that imposed by state statutes for similar criminal conduct.

326 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Chiles v. United Faculty of Fla.


No. 81,252


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


615 So. 2d 671; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 328; 143 L.R.R.M. 2136; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 143



March 11, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, F. E. Steinmeyer, III, Judge, Case No. 92-696 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 92-3808


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, governor and state, sought review from the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Leon County (Florida), which issued a judgment for appellees, unions representing public employees, in their action against appellants after appellants eliminated pay raises agreed to in a collective bargaining agreement.


OVERVIEW: Appellees were unions representing public employees and were unable to resolve a collective bargaining process for pay and benefits. Appellants, governor and state, authorized a raise for the employees and the unions ratified the raise. Appellants eliminated the raises in order to meet a revenue shortfall. The court affirmed the circuit court's decision issuing judgment for appellees. Appellants' elimination of the raises was an impermissible impairment of contract and violated Fla. Const. art. I, §§ 6, 10. Appellants and appellees agreed on a fully enforceable contract because appellants accepted and funded the agreement. Appellants were parties to that contract. Appellants failed to show that they had no alternative means of preserving the contract with the public employees and, thus, had no authority to breach the contract. The savings clauses in the contract were not an escape hatch for appellants but were included only to preserve the contact in the event of partial invalidity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's decision for appellees, unions representing public employees, and found that appellants, governor and state, violated the Florida constitution when they eliminated raises for the public employees after appellants had agreed to and funded the raises because appellants failed to show they had no alternative means of funding the raises.

 

327 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Gayman v. State


Nos. 78,547, 79,602


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


616 So. 2d 17; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 163; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 109



February 11, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases Consolidated: Applications for Review of the Decisions of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 90-3635. Second District - Case No. 91-00507. (Duval and Polk Counties).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of their convictions from the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida) of felony petit theft, a violation of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 812.014(2)(d), and habitual felony offender sentences.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners were convicted of felony petit theft, a violation of Fla. Stat. Ann. § 812.014(2)(d), and sentenced as habitual felony offenders. The district court certified a question to determine whether double jeopardy clauses were violated by the reclassification of petitioners' offense as felony petit theft and then used to enhance their sentence pursuant to the habitual violent felony offender statute. The court held that each petitioner had at least two prior petit theft convictions, each were guilty of the substantive offense of felony petit theft as a separate felony, and the habitualization was independent of petitioners' prior petit thefts. The U.S. Const. and Fla. Const. principles that prohibited courts from imposing multiple punishments for the same offense were not an issue. In enacting § 812.014(2)(d), the legislature determined that a third or subsequent conviction for petit theft was the separate, substantive offense of felony petit theft and not an enhanced punishment. However, the record reflected that one petitioner was sentenced as a habitual violent felony offender under an amendment that violated the single subject provision of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court answered the certified question in the negative because the punishment imposed on petitioners did not violate double jeopardy principles. The court remanded one petitioner's case for resentencing because she was sentenced as a habitual violent felony offender under a statutory amendment that violated the single subject provision of the state constitution. The court approved the other petitioner's conviction and sentence.

 

328 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Capital City Country Club v. Tucker


No. 78,201


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


613 So. 2d 448; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 182; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 97



February 4, 1993, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 90-2551. (Leon County)



DISPOSITION:  The court approved the decision affirming the denial of a real estate tax exemption or reduction to petitioner because the state constitution did not give petitioner, a private lessee of city land on a lease entered into before 1976, an exemption, thus the statute could not give exemptions to pre-1976 lessees, and because the value of the lease did not affect the value of the real estate and could not be excluded for tax valuations.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The First District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirmed the judgment that Fla. Stat. Ann. § 196.199(4) (1991) did not exempt petitioner, a private lessee of city property on a lease entered into before 1976, from paying real estate taxes and that petitioner's payment of tangible tax on the lease did not cause the value of the lease to be excluded from the value of the property, and certified these questions to the court.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner entered into a 99-year lease in 1956 to lease city-owned land for the use as a private golf course. The lease required petitioner to pay all ad valorem taxes. Petitioner paid intangible tax on the lease, and sued for an exemption from real estate taxes under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 196.199(4) (1991), or to have the value of the lease excluded from the value of the land for real estate tax purposes. The trial court entered judgment against petitioner, and the appellate court affirmed the judgment and certified the question of the exemption and the exclusion. The court held that because § 196.199(4) (1991) did not expressly exempt leases entered into before 1976 from taxation, and because Fla. Const. art. VII, § 3(a) exempted city owned property from taxation only if it were being used for a public purpose, petitioner was not exempt from paying real estate taxes. Because the intangible tax on the lease and the real estate tax were two separate taxes on different types of property, there was no double taxation and the value of the lease could not be excluded from the value of the land for real estate for tax purposes. Therefore, the court affirmed the decision.


OUTCOME: The court approved the decision affirming the denial of a real estate tax exemption or reduction to petitioner because the state constitution did not give petitioner, a private lessee of city land on a lease entered into before 1976, an exemption, thus the statute could not give exemptions to pre-1976 lessees, and because the value of the lease did not affect the value of the real estate and could not be excluded for tax valuations.

Elledge v. State


No. 74,789


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


613 So. 2d 434; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 10; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 70



January 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 5, 1993. Released for Publication March 5, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, M. Daniel Futch, Jr., Judge - Case No. 75-87CF10A



DISPOSITION: We reverse and remand for resentencing consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County (Florida), which, on remand, resentenced appellant to the death penalty based on four aggravating and no mitigating circumstances. Appellant had previously pled guilty to rape and first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to rape and first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced appellant to death, but the sentence was reversed. The state supreme court also determined that the sentencing court erred in failing to consider evidence of an abuse childhood as a mitigating circumstance; that it erred in improperly admitting photos of a victim's corpse; and that it erred in giving jury instructions regarding contemporaneous rape as a prior violent felony.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court, which on remand resentenced appellant to the death penalty for rape and first-degree murder was reversed and remanded. The state supreme court held that a new sentencing hearing was required because the trial court erred in, inter alia, failing to grant a Richardson hearing and in failing to consider appellant's abused childhood as a non-statutory mitigating factor.

State v. Johnson


Nos. 79,150, 79,204


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


1993 Fla. LEXIS 252; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 234



January 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] An Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 91-742. (Duval County) and an Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory/Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case No. 91-00742. (Duval County)

Original Opinion of January 14, 1993, Reported at 1993 Fla. LEXIS 12.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged a decision from the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which certified a question for review regarding its holding that the habitual violent felony offender statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 contained in 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 89-280, violated Fla. Const. art. III, § 6.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was charged with the sale or delivery of cocaine. The prosecution filed a notice of intent to classify respondent as a habitual violent felony offender pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084 because of a prior felony conviction for aggravated battery. Respondent was convicted and sentenced to a prison term of 25 years with a 10-year mandatory minimum term. Respondent appealed, claiming that the amendments to the habitual offender statute contained in 1989 Fla. Laws ch. 89-280, violated the single subject rule of Fla. Const. art. III, § 6. The appellate court vacated respondent's sentence and certified the question of the statute's constitutionality for review. The court affirmed, stating that a facial challenge to a statute's constitutional validity could be raised on appeal if the error was fundamental. Because the statute affected fundamental liberty due process rights, it was a question of fundamental error. The court held that ch. 89-280 violated the single-subject rule because it contained two topics that had no cogent connection.


OUTCOME: The court approved the decision of the appellate court holding that the amendments to the habitual offender statute violated the single subject rule because they contained two topics that had no cogent connection.

Hall v. State


No. 77,563


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


614 So. 2d 473; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 14; 20 A.L.R.5th 923; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 63



January 14, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 22, 1993. Released for Publication March 22, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Sumter County, Richard Tombrink, Jr., Judge - Case No. 78-52-CF



DISPOSITION:  The court affirmed the death sentence that was imposed upon appellant, during resentencing, after appellant was convicted of first degree murder and second degree murder because the trial court properly considered the aggravating and mitigating factors, the sentence was not disproportionate, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion during resentencing.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Sumter County (Florida) that imposed a death sentence upon appellant after appellant was convicted of first degree murder and second degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of first degree murder for the murder of a pregnant woman and a deputy sheriff. Subsequently, the conviction for the deputy's murder was reduced to second degree murder. Appellant sought review of the death sentence that was imposed during resentencing. The court affirmed, holding that appellant failed to show that there was an abuse of discretion in the refusal to grant appellant more peremptory challenges during the trial, in the refusal to grant appellant's proposed jury instruction, and in excluding cumulative testimony. Furthermore, the court held that the proper standard was used in weighing the aggravating and mitigating factors and that the evidence supported the conclusion that the crime of the pregnant woman was committed in a cold, calculated, and premeditated manner with no pretense of moral or legal justification. In addition, the jury instruction on the heinous, atrocious, or cruel aggravator was not unconstitutionally vague because the terms were sufficiently defined. Finally, the court held that the sentence was not disproportionate because aggravators outweighed mitigating factors and the death penalty was properly imposed for the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the death sentence that was imposed upon appellant, during resentencing, after appellant was convicted of first degree murder and second degree murder because the trial court properly considered the aggravating and mitigating factors, the sentence was not disproportionate, and the trial court did not abuse its discretion during resentencing.

 

336 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Thomas v. State


No. 78,055


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


614 So. 2d 468; 1993 Fla. LEXIS 1; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 46



January 7, 1993, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 23, 1993. Released for Publication March 23, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fifth District - Case No. 89-2549. (Orange County)



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, we approve the decision below but disapprove the court's reasoning.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of a decision of the Fifth District Court of Appeal, Orange County (Florida), which affirmed the lower court's decision that convicted petitioner of carrying a concealed firearm and found that a municipal ordinance that required the existence of safety equipment on a bicycle ridden in the city limits was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was riding a bicycle that was not equipped with a bell or gong as required by a city ordinance. A police officer stopped petitioner and arrested him for violation of the ordinance. Incidental to the arrest, the officer searched petitioner and found a handgun in his pocket. Petitioner was charged with carrying a concealed firearm, and he filed a motion to suppress the seized evidence. The lower court denied the motion, and petitioner was convicted. The lower court further found that the ordinance was constitutional. The supreme court held that when a person was charged with violating a municipal ordinance regulating conduct that was noncriminal in nature, Fla. Stat. ch. 901.15(1) (1989) only permitted a person to be detained for the limited purpose of issuing a ticket, summons, or notice to appear. A full custodial arrest was unreasonable. However, the court affirmed the denial of petitioner's motion to suppress the evidence because the arrest was made in reliance on the city ordinance. Evidence obtained after a search incident to an arrest in reliance on a municipal ordinance was not to be suppressed even when the ordinance was subsequently declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: State supreme court affirmed the lower court's decision that convicted petitioner of carrying a concealed firearm and held that when a person was charged with violating a municipal ordinance that regulated conduct that was noncriminal in nature, the state statute only permitted the person to be detained for a limited purpose of issuing a ticket, summons, or notice to appear.

State v. Fla. Police Benevolent Ass'n


No. 77,842


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


613 So. 2d 415; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2144; 142 L.R.R.M. 2224; 18 Fla. L. Weekly S 1



December 24, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied March 4, 1993. Released for Publication March 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case No. 90-1236


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the judgment of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida) for appellees, declaring a proviso in a state appropriations bill unconstitutional after appellants enacted legislation altering the leave policy for appellees' career service employees.


OVERVIEW: Appellants enacted legislation that altered the leave policy for appellees' career service employees. Appellees claimed that appellants' actions abridged their right to collectively bargain, which was guaranteed by the state constitution. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees. The Supreme Court reversed the trial court's decision declaring Fla. Const. § 9.3 (A) 5 of the 1988 Appropriations Act unconstitutional. The court stated that where the legislature provides enough money to implement the benefit as negotiated, but attempts to unilaterally change the benefit, the changes will not be upheld, and the negotiated benefit will be enforced. Where the legislature does not appropriate enough money to fund a negotiated benefit, as it is free to do, then the conditions it imposes on the use of the funds will stand even if contradictory to the negotiated agreement.


OUTCOME: The court's decision declaring a proviso in the state appropriations bill unconstitutional was reversed because appellants had the right to impose conditions on the use of funds so long as they appropriated enough money, even if it was contradictory to the negotiated agreement with appellees.
