PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Mark E. Polen, Judge - Case No. 87-18628 CF 10

Original Opinion of August 29, 1991, Reported at 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1525.
Henry v. Florida, 505 U.S. 1216, 112 S. Ct. 3021, 120 L. Ed. 2d 893, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 4583 (1992)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appeal from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Broward County (Florida) for plaintiff, and convicting defendant of first-degree murder, sentencing him to death, and two concurrent terms of life imprisonment for armed robbery with a deadly weapon and arson.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a maintenance man, hit in the head with a hammer and set on fire two store employees. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, sentenced to death, and two concurrent terms of life imprisonment for armed robbery with a deadly weapon and arson. The Supreme Court held that defendant's statements were properly admitted into evidence because they were made knowingly and voluntarily. In addition, one of the victim's statements that identified defendant as the person who had set her on fire was properly admitted as a dying declaration. The trial court properly found that the aggravators outweighed the mitigators and imposed two death sentences. The court also affirmed the two life sentences for arson and robbery. The first-degree murder convictions were not scoreable under the guidelines and constituted valid reasons for departure from the recommended sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions of first-degree murder, death sentences, and two concurrent terms of life imprisonment for armed robbery and arson were affirmed, because the several allegations of procedural and evidentiary error did not merit reversal of his convictions or sentences on appeal.

Defendant's motion for postconviction relief was properly denied without an evidentiary hearing.

 

340 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Psychiatric Assoc. v. Siegel


Nos. 76,844, 76,917


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


610 So. 2d 419; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2012; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 726



December 3, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Cases Consolidate. An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. First District - Case Nos. 90-738 & 90-31. (Leon County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court reviewed two consolidated cases from the District Court of Appeal (Florida) in which the court invalidated as unconstitutional, Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 395.011(10)(b), 395.0115(5)(b), 766.101(6)(b), holding that plaintiff physicians were not required to post a bond to guarantee defendants' costs and attorney fees before bringing an action against defendant medical review boards.


OVERVIEW: The court consolidated appeals from two cases. In each case plaintiff physician filed suit against defendant hospital after it revoked or restricted plaintiff's hospital privileges, and the trial court required plaintiffs to post a bond. The court reversed because Fla. Stat. Ann. § 395.011(10)(b) (1987), Fla. Stat. Ann. § 395.0115(5)(b) (1987), and Fla. Stat. Ann. § 766.101(6)(b) (1988) shared language that required a plaintiff to post a bond to pay for costs and attorney's fees. The court found that the bond requirements were unconstitutional because requirements interfered with plaintiffs' right to access to the court, based on plaintiffs' inability to post bond. Access to the courts could be restricted if the plaintiff had an alternative reasonable remedy or commensurate benefit, or there was an overpowering public necessity for the abolishment of the right. Because the bond requirement was not the only method of reducing the number of frivolous suits filed by disgruntled physicians against medical review boards, the court found that the bond requirement arbitrarily cut off a plaintiff's right to be heard solely because of inability to post bond.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the lower court that required plaintiff physicians post a bond before they filed lawsuits against defendant hospital was reversed because the bond requirement arbitrarily cut off a plaintiff's right to be heard, and the bond requirement was not the only method of meeting the necessity of reducing the amount of frivolous lawsuits.

 

341 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Kush v. Lloyd


No. 76,476, No. 77,135, No. 77,192, No. 77,193


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


616 So. 2d 415; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2017; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 730



December 3, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Four Consolidated Notices for Review of the Decisions of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Direct Conflict of Decisions and Certified Great Public Importance. Third District - Case Nos. 87-2250 & 88-1419. (Dade County)



DISPOSITION: We answer the certified question in the affirmative. The opinion under review is quashed to the extent it conflicts with the views expressed above, but otherwise is approved. This cause is remanded for further proceedings consistent with the views expressed above.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal (Florida) requested the court to determine whether a wrongful birth action could be extinguished by the four-year statute of repose if the genetically impaired child was born more than four years after the negligent diagnosis.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs had a deformed son. They received genetic testing and were advised that their son's impairment was not a genetic defect. They had a second child with the same deformities. A test disclosed the condition was inherited. Plaintiffs filed suit for wrongful birth, wrongful life, and for the mental anguish suffered by the family. The lower court struck the wrongful life and mental anguish claims and found that the statute of repose barred most of the claims. The intermediate appellate court reversed in part. The question was certified for immediate review and the court affirmed in part. The court found the statute of repose in a medical malpractice case began to run at the time of the incident of malpractice regardless of whether it was fraudulently concealed. The court found that plaintiff parents were entitled to recover for mental anguish because the impact doctrine, which required them to be in the zone of danger, did not apply in the context of wrongful birth claims. Plaintiffs were entitled to recover for extraordinary costs after their deformed son reached majority because such costs were quantifiable with reasonable certainty.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the intermediate appellate court was affirmed because the statute of repose in a medical malpractice case began to run at the time of the incident, regardless of whether it was fraudulently concealed. The impact doctrine did not apply in the context of wrongful birth claims. Plaintiffs were entitled to recover for extraordinary costs because such costs were quantifiable.

Gordon v. State


No. 78,638


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


608 So. 2d 800; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1930; 16 A.L.R.5th 894; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 690



November 12, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Third District - Case No. 90-2497. (Dade County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff victim appealed a decision of the District Court of Appeal (Florida) affirming an award of 60 percent of defendant's damage award in a false imprisonment case to intervenor state under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.73(2)(b).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff victim sued defendant corporation, alleging he was falsely imprisoned and battered by employees of defendant in an incident in one of its stores. Plaintiff obtained a jury verdict against defendant and received compensatory and punitive damages. Intervenor state intervened, asserting that it had a 60 percent interest in the punitive damages award pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. § 768.73(2)(b). The trial court awarded intervenor the 60 percent share, and the appellate court affirmed. The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court, holding that the statute was constitutional. The court held that the right to have punitive damages assessed was not property and that until the judgment was rendered, there was no vested right in a claim for punitive damages. The court held, therefore, that the denial of punitive damages did not unconstitutionally impair any property rights of plaintiff. The court held further that no substantive due process violation occurred because the statute bore a rational relationship to legitimate legislative objectives.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the appellate court which affirmed the trial court's award to intervenor state of 60 percent of plaintiff victim's punitive damages award, holding that the statute authorizing such an award to intervenor was constitutional.

Fla. League of Cities v. Smith


No. 80,489


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


607 So. 2d 397; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1816; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 665



October 29, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Mandamus


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner cities sought a writ of mandamus to direct respondents secretary of state and chief elections officer to remove a proposed constitutional amendment from a ballot.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner league of cities sought to have a proposed constitutional amendment removed from the ballot, arguing that if the proposal were approved by the voters, Fla. Const. art. VII, § 6(d) would have the effect of repealing part of the homestead exemption in Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4. The court denied the writ of mandamus because the language of the ballot proposal was not clearly and conclusively defective; therefore, no relief sought by petitioners was available. Where constitutional language was precise, it had to be enforced, and no extrinsic guides to construction were allowed to defeat the plain language. The court also determined that the language of the proposed amendment would not trigger the repealer contained in Fla. Const. VII, § 6(d).


OUTCOME: The court denied the writ of mandamus because the clear and plain language of the proposed constitutional amendment would not trigger the repeal of the homestead exemption as argued by petitioners.

Firestone Tire & Rubber Co. v. Acosta


Nos. 78,255 & 78,506


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


612 So. 2d 1361; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1810; CCH Prod. Liab. Rep. P13,348; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 646



October 22, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied February 24, 1993. Released for Publication February 24, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: Two Consolidated Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Third District - Case No. 90-2024 and Fourth District - Case No. 90-1253. (Dade and Broward Counties)



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we answer both certified questions in the affirmative, quash the decision of the Third District in Acosta, approve the decision of the Fourth District in Walker, and remand Acosta with directions to affirm the decision of the circuit


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two cases were consolidated on appeal because two panels of the District Court of Appeals (Florida) reached conflicting conclusions as to the applicability of the statute of repose in Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2) (1975), which was repealed by the legislature in 1986.


OVERVIEW: Two wrongful death cases were consolidated for appeal. In one case, the decedent was killed when a multi-piece rim and wheel assembly exploded and struck him. In the second case, a machine accidentally caused a death. At the time that both products were manufactured, a statute of repose, Fla. Stat. ch. 95.031(2) (1975), was in effect. That statute was repealed before the deaths occurred and after the repose period had run. One appellate court panel ruled that a vested right existed which could not have been taken away by the repeal of the statute of repose. The other panel held that because of the repeal, the statute of repose was not applicable under any circumstances after its repeal, and the panel allowed the products liability claim to proceed. The court on appeal ruled that when the period of repose expired, any cause of action was extinguished by operation of law. The repeal of the statute of repose could not operate to revive a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The court adopted the view of the appellate court panel that held once the statute of repose extinguished a cause of action, nothing could revive the case, including the repeal of the statute of repose. The court reversed the other appellate decision that had held that the statute's repeal permitted a products liability action to proceed even though it had lapsed prior to the repeal of the statute.

Ragsdale v. State


Case No. 72,664.


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


609 So. 2d 10; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1799; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 620



October 15, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Wayne L. Cobb, Judge - Case No. 86-00091CFAES.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Vacated Opinion of March 12, 1992, Reported at 1992 Fla. LEXIS 498.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we affirm Ragsdale's convictions and sentences, including the imposition of the death penalty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and armed robbery and sentenced him to death. Defendant claimed that the trial court erred by not allowing him to question prospective jurors on voir dire as to their willingness to impose a similar penalty as that imposed upon a codefendant if they found defendant equally or less culpable.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and armed robbery. In accordance with the jury recommendation, the trial court sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court erred by not allowing him to question prospective jurors on voir dire as to their willingness to impose a similar penalty as that imposed upon a codefendant, if they found the defendant equally or less culpable. Defendant also contended that the trial court erred by imposing the death penalty where the jury indicated that defendant was less culpable than a codefendant who was sentenced to life imprisonment. The appeals court affirmed. The court ruled that the trial court did not commit error during voir dire because defendant's counsel had sufficient latitude to question the jurors to obtain fair and impartial jurors. Additionally, the court noted that the sentencing jury was fully aware of the sentence received by the codefendant, and defense counsel was not limited in the manner in which to assert that his client was less culpable in the commission of the murder. The court affirmed the sentences because deciding the verdict was exclusively the jury's job.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions for first-degree murder and armed robbery and defendant's death sentence because the trial court committed no reversible error. The appellate court ruled that the sentencing jury was fully aware of the sentence received by the codefendant and that deciding the verdict was exclusively within the jury's province.

Fotopoulos v. State


No. 77,016


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


1992 Fla. LEXIS 1800; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 643



October 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Revised Opinion of October 15, 1992, Reported at 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2142.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, S. James Foxman, Judge - Case Nos. 89-7632, 90-1995 and 90-6668



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, having found no reversible error, we affirm the convictions and sentences.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida) convicting him of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, solicitation, conspiracy, and burglary and sentencing him to death. Defendant claimed the court erred in excluding black jurors, in failing to sever the murder counts, which compounded errors in the penalty phase, and in improperly considering aggravating factors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions for first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, solicitation, conspiracy, and burglary and death sentences were upheld where the trial court properly considered aggravating factors and no severance of offenses was necessary. Defendant and his girlfriend shot a man to avoid revelation of defendant's counterfeiting. Defendant enlisted a man to kill his wife in a fake burglary. Defendant killed the hitman in order to make the burglary appear real. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed, claiming the trial court erred in excluding black jurors, in failing to sever the murder counts, in improperly considering the aggravating factors that the crimes were committed for pecuniary gain, and in improperly finding the murders were heinous. The court affirmed. The two black jurors were properly excluded for race-neutral reasons. Where the two murders were connected in an episodic sense, no severance was necessary. Because defendant killed the hitman in order to cover up a crime and the murders were premeditated and committed for pecuniary gain, these aggravators were properly considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, solicitation, conspiracy, and burglary, and sentencing him to death because the black jurors were excluded for race-neutral reasons and because the murders were premeditated, committed to avoid arrest, and committed for pecuniary gain.

Fotopoulos v. State


No. 77,016


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


608 So. 2d 784; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2142; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 643



October 15, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised. Rehearing Denied December 24, 1992. Released for Publication December 24, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County, S. James Foxman, Judge - Case Nos. 89-7632, 90-1995 and 90-6668

Original Opinion of October 15, 1992, Reported at 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1800.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, having found no reversible error, we affirm the convictions and sentences.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court in and for Volusia County (Florida), convicting and sentencing him for first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, solicitation to commit first-degree murder, conspiracy to commit first degree murder, and burglary of a dwelling while armed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder, attempted murder, solicitation, conspiracy, and burglary. Defendant alleged that the state used peremptory challenges to exclude black prospective jurors. He failed to meet the burden of demonstrating the likelihood that this was the case, and the state gave racially neutrally explanations for their challenges. The offenses with which defendant was charged were connected in an episodic and in a temporal sense, so defendant was not entitled to severance. Because defendant opened the door for further cross-examination regarding his prior convictions, there was no error in the state's questioning regarding this impeachment evidence. There was no error in failure to grant a hearing on the state's failure to provide defense counsel with a transcript copy because the trial court was not apprised of the alleged violation. The record contained substantial competent evidence to support defendant's convictions. Defendant failed to renew a severance motion at sentencing, there were no objections to the penalty phase instructions, nor were there requests for special jury instructions. Defendant's claims regarding his sentences were not preserved for appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences for murder, attempted murder, solicitation, conspiracy, and burglary were affirmed because there was no reversible error found in the court's decisions on peremptory challenges, denial of severance, impeachment of defendant, lack of hearing on an alleged discovery violation, aggravating circumstances, and the constitutionality of the death penalty.

Rodriguez v. State


No. 75,978


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


609 So. 2d 493; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1657; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 623



October 8, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1993. Released for Publication January 7, 1993.
Writ of certiorari denied Rodriguez v. Florida, 510 U.S. 830, 114 S. Ct. 99, 126 L. Ed. 2d 66, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 5172 (1993)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Writ of habeas corpus denied Rodriguez v. State, 919 So. 2d 1252, 2005 Fla. LEXIS 1169 (Fla., 2005)
Post-conviction proceeding at Rodriguez v. State, 968 So. 2d 557, 2007 Fla. LEXIS 1884 (Fla., 2007)
Post-conviction proceeding at Rodriguez v. State, 110 So. 3d 441, 2013 Fla. LEXIS 195 (Fla., 2013)
Post-conviction relief denied at Rodriguez v. State, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 891 (Fla., Apr. 20, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Thomas M. Carney, Judge - Case No. 88-18180-B



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, having found no reversible error, we affirm the convictions and sentences, including the sentence of death.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), which convicted him of first-degree murder, and related crimes arising from incidents of robbery and home invasion that occurred on two consecutive days which were tried together. Defendant appealed his death sentence and guilt based on various alleged evidentiary errors.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder, armed robbery, conspiracy to commit a felony, attempted armed robbery, armed burglary with an assault, aggravated assault, and attempted first-degree murder. The charges stemmed from two incidents that occurred on consecutive days. Defendant appealed his conviction and his death sentence and the court affirmed. It was not error to exclude deposition testimony of a defense witness who failed to appear for trial. Although Fla. Stat. ch. 90.804(2)(a) (1989) provided an exception to the hearsay rule for deposition testimony of an unavailable witness, Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.190(j) still applied, requiring notice to opposing counsel when a deposition was taken that may be used at trial. Although defendant moved for severance of his trial from the other defendants, he never moved for severance of the charges, so that claim was not preserved for appeal and it was not fundamental error that the trial court should have corrected sua sponte. Evidence that defendant pursued his victim and shot repeatedly while the victim begged for his life was evidence that the crime was heinous, atrocious, or cruel, justifying the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on murder and other charges and the death sentence holding that the trial court did not error in excluding deposition testimony from an unavailable witness because the deposition was not taken with notice to opposing counsel that it may be used at trial. Evidence that defendant enjoyed or was utterly indifferent to the suffering of his victim supported imposition of the death penalty.

Writ of mandamus denied, Stay denied by, Petition denied by Power v. White, 761 So. 2d 330, 1998 Fla. LEXIS 1144 (Fla., 1998)
Stay lifted by Power v. State, 770 So. 2d 160, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1852 (Fla., 2000)

DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we affirm Power's conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review and appellee state cross-appealed from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County (Florida), where appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and received the death penalty. Appellant claimed that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the jury verdict, that the prosecutor improperly commented on appellant's failure to testify, and that he was denied the right to a fair trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death in the killing and sexual assault of a young girl. The court rejected the contention that the prosecutor improperly commented on appellant's failure to testify in violation of his constitutional right against self-incrimination. The court also affirmed the sentence, holding that regardless of the existence of error as to mitigating circumstances, the trial court would have imposed the same sentence due to the evidence and aggravating circumstances.

State by Butterworth v. Republican Party of Fla.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida) certified the need for immediate resolution as to the constitutionality of Fla. OVERVIEW: Fla. Stat. chs. 106.29(1)(b), 106.07(3)(b), and 106.04(4)(b)(2) were declared unconstitutional by two trial courts after interested entities objected to financial assessments which funded causes and candidates they did not wish to support. The court determined that the laws infringed upon the U.S. Const. amend. I constitutional rights of those who did not support adversaries in government or elections. The court held that the means chosen to advance the state interest was unduly burdensome and was not tailored narrowly enough to withstand constitutional scrutiny. Therefore, the laws were declared unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The assessments imposed by statute impermissibly infringed upon the First Amendment constitutional rights of those who did not support adversaries in government or elections. The means chosen to advance the state interest was unduly burdensome and was not tailored narrowly enough to withstand constitutional scrutiny.

Gallagher v. Motors Ins. Corp.


No. 79,061


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


605 So. 2d 62; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1300; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 468



July 23, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, F. E. Steinmeyer, III, Judge, Case No. 90-2046 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 91-03704


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Florida challenged a judgment from the Trial Court, in and for Leon County (Florida), on Direct Appeal of Judgment to the Florida Supreme Court, in appellee's action for declaratory relief where the trial court declared unconstitutional Florida's insurance premium tax scheme, Fla. Stat. ch. 624.509, .512, .514, and where the trial court held appellant's proposed tax assessments invalid.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, insurance companies residing outside of the state of Florida, sought a declaratory judgment that the state's insurance premium tax scheme, Fla. Stat. ch. 624.509, .512, and .514, unconstitutionally discriminated against them under the equal protection and due process clauses of the U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and the due process clause of the Florida Constitution. After an evidentiary trial, the trial court found that the premium tax, on its face, discriminated against foreign insurance companies, and declared the scheme unconstitutional. The trial court found the state's proposed tax assessments invalid, but upheld Florida's retaliatory tax, Fla. Stat. ch. 624.429 (1983-1987). The supreme court reversed to the extent that the trial court found ch. 624.509, .512, and .514 invalid because the tax scheme was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose. Florida had more control and regulatory influence over a domestic insurer than over a foreign insurer, and Florida was in a better position to protect the interests of Florida policyholders. The supreme court affirmed that portion of the judgment upholding ch. 624.429.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the trial court ruling that Florida's insurance premium tax scheme was unconstitutional and that appellant State of Florida's tax assessments were invalid because the state's tax scheme was rationally related to a legitimate state purpose. The supreme court also reversed that portion of the trial court's opinion holding appellant's proposed tax assessments invalid.

Dep't of Revenue v. Magazine Publrs. of Am.


No. 75,201


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


604 So. 2d 459; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1304; 20 Media L. Rep. 1502; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 547



July 23, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 23, 1992. Released for Publication September 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, George S. Reynolds, III, Judge, Case No. 88-2442 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 89-3115


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a suit originally brought by appellee magazine publishers against the Florida Department of Revenue challenging the constitutionality of the imposition of sales tax on retail sales of secular magazines pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 212.05(1)(i) and 212.08(7)(w), the United States Supreme Court remanded the case for further consideration after vacating the court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: Appellees magazine publishers brought suit against appellant state department of revenue challenging the constitutionality of a sales tax on sales of secular magazines pursuant to Fla. Stat. Ann. §§ 212.05(1)(i) and 212.08(7)(w). After the state supreme court affirmed the trial court's order finding that the statutes unconstitutionally burdened interests protected by U.S. Const. amend. I but held that the proper remedy was the elimination of the exemption from sales taxes for newspapers, the United States Supreme Court granted certiorari, vacated the judgment and remanded the case. On remand, the court held that the tax did not discriminate either by singling out the press for a special tax or by targeting a small group within the press to bear the burden of the tax. However, the court held that the tax improperly discriminated on the basis of the content of the speech. The court held that, although the State had a legitimate interest in fostering literacy, the tax scheme was not narrowly tailored to achieve that end. The court therefore reversed the portion of the trial court's order regarding the proper remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's order holding that a sales tax imposed on sales of magazines violated First Amendment rights and did not serve a compelling state interest. However, the court reversed the portion of the trial court's order that concluded the appropriate remedy was to strike the tax imposed on magazines.

Marshall v. State


No. 75,406


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


604 So. 2d 799; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1274; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 459



July 16, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1992. Released for Publication September 28, 1992.
Writ of certiorari denied Marshall v. Florida, 508 U.S. 915, 113 S. Ct. 2355, 124 L. Ed. 2d 263, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 3319 (May 17, 1993)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Marshall v. Sec'y, Fla. Dep't of Corr., 610 F.3d 576, 2010 U.S. App. LEXIS 13206 (11th Cir. Fla., 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Marshall v. Jones, 2017 Fla. LEXIS 981 (Fla., May 4, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Martin County, Dwight L. Geiger, Judge - Case No. 89-174-CF



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we affirm Marshall's conviction for first-degree murder and the resulting death sentence.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From the Circuit Court in and for Martin County (Florida), defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder and the resulting death sentence after the judge rejected the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment. Defendant's appeal raised several issues regarding both the guilt phase and the penalty phase of the proceedings.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree murder and the resulting death sentence, despite the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment. The court rejected defendant's contentions and affirmed the conviction and sentence. The court held that defendant was not denied his right to cross-examination simply because the judge allowed a witness to testify anonymously. The court explained that because the defense always knew of the witness' identity, cross-examination was not hampered. The court further ruled that although the trial judge's jury instructions may have been error, the error was harmless and did not require reversal. Moreover, the court concluded that the trial court did not err in admitting a photograph taken of the victim during an autopsy because it assisted the medical examiner in explaining the nature of the victim's wounds. Finally, as to the penalty phase, the court held that the record contained insufficient evidence to reasonably support the jury's recommendation of life. Thus, the trial judge did not abuse his discretion in rejecting the life sentence and in imposing death, because the sentence was proportional to defendant's crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence. The court concluded that the trial court's evidentiary rulings were not an abuse of discretion and that although the trial judge's jury instructions may have been improper, any error was harmless. As to defendant's death sentence, the court held that the facts did not support a life sentence, thus the judge did not abuse his discretion in overriding the jury's recommendation.

608 So. 2d 1; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1240; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 443

Mandico v. Taos Constr.


No. 76,766


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


605 So. 2d 850; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1242; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 445



July 9, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected. Rehearing Denied October 8, 1992. Released for Publication October 8, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 89-2612. (Broward County)



DISPOSITION: However, because we approve the opinion below as it relates to the first question certified, we remand with directions that the suit be dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified for review the questions of whether immunity from a personal injury suit existed for a general contractor who provided workers' compensation coverage for an independent contract and whether orders denying immunity from civil suit under Fla. Stat. ch. 440 et seq. might be reviewed by a writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: In a personal injury action by petitioner independent contractor against respondents, a general contractor and an employee, the trial court denied respondents' summary judgment motion and respondents filed a petition for review. The district court treated the petition as a writ of prohibition, quashed the trial court's ruling, and certified for review the questions of whether a general contractor has immunity from personal injury where it provided workers' compensation coverage for an independent contractor and whether a writ of prohibition was the appropriate vehicle for review. The court approved the district court's decision as to the summary judgment motion, quashed the order granting prohibition, and remanded for dismissal. Under Fla. Stat. ch. 440.04, a general contractor was immune from civil liability where it obtained, by agreement, workers' compensation insurance for the independent contractor; despite the fact that independent contractors are generally excluded from coverage under Fla. Stat. ch. 440 et seq. The court ruled that a writ of prohibition could not be used to divest a court of jurisdiction, and the court revised Fla. R. App. P. 9.130(a)(3) to reflect this.


OUTCOME: The court approved the district court's reversal of summary judgment for respondents, quashed the order granting prohibition, and ordered that petitioner's personal injury suit be dismissed because respondent general contractor obtained workers' compensation coverage for petitioner independent contractor, giving respondents, the general contractor and its employee, immunity from suit.

 

359 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Garden v. Frier


No. 78,156


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


602 So. 2d 1273; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1215; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 381



July 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. First District - Case No. 90-2844. (Suwannee County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner land owners applied for review of the affirmative decision in favor of respondent land surveyor by the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which certified as a question of great public importance regarding whether a land surveyor was a professional for purposes of the professional malpractice statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(4).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner land owners sued respondent land surveyor for malpractice for a negligent land survey slightly more than two years after discovering the error. Respondent raised as an affirmative defense the two-year statute of limitations for professional malpractice, Fla. Stat. ch. 95.11(4). The sole issue presented to the court was whether land surveyors were "professionals" for purposes of the professional malpractice statute. The legislature had declined to define the term. The court's first-blush inclination was to strike the statute on the grounds of vagueness, but decided that an earlier opinion foreclosed that action. The court accepted jurisdiction to modify and clarify the earlier opinion. As now defined by the court, a "profession" in the context of the professional malpractice statute came into being when state licensing for all future admittees required a four-year undergraduate or graduate degree and not when any alternative method of admission was permitted. Because some land surveyors could be admitted to practice their occupation without a four-year degree, respondent was not a "professional" under the professional malpractice statute.


OUTCOME: Because some land surveyors could be admitted to practice their occupation without at least a four-year undergraduate degree, the court answered in the negative the certified question regarding whether a land surveyor was a professional for purposes of the professional malpractice statute. The opinion under review was quashed and the cause was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Turner v. Dugger


Nos. 75,848 & 77,062


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


1992 Fla. LEXIS 1128; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 391



June 25, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Withdrawn on Denial of Rehearing December 24, 1992, Reported at 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2160; Substituted Opinion of December 24, 1992. Reported at 1992 Fla. LEXIS 2164.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus and An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County. John D. Southwood, Judge, - Case No. 84-6504 Div. CR-D


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed a decision from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which denied petitioner's motion for postconviction relief filed pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 after he was convicted of first-degree murder. Petitioner also sought a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of two counts of first-degree murder. The trial court imposed sentences of death and life imprisonment. The convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Petitioner filed for a writ of habeas corpus and a motion to vacate conviction and sentence pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. The trial court denied the motion for postconviction relief. On appeal, the court barred petitioner's contentions that the murders were not cold, calculated, and premeditated, and that the trial court's instructions concerning aggravating factors conflicted with state law. For the same reason, the court barred petitioner's arguments concerning capital sentencing. The court also rejected petitioner's claims relating to ineffective assistance of counsel. In reviewing the habeas corpus petition, the court declined to retroactively apply case law concerning contemporaneous conviction. The court stated that the trial court was not required to use special jury forms for jury specification of the murder conviction, and the court again rejected petitioner's ineffective assistance of counsel claims. The trial court's decision was affirmed and the petition was denied.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision that denied petitioner's motion for postconviction relief was denied because some of petitioner's contentions were procedurally barred, and his claims relating to ineffective assistance of counsel were rejected. The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was also denied because there was no trial court error and the court declined to retroactively apply case law concerning contemporaneous conviction.

Ross v. State


No. 78,179


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


601 So. 2d 1190; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1113; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 367



June 18, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied July 28, 1992. Released for Publication July 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. First District - Case No. 90.563. (Duval County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed an application for review of a decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), which affirmed the trial court's decision that petitioner was a habitual felony offender and thus subject to enhanced sentencing, in connection to his conviction for "escaping" from prison while he was participating in a work-release program.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, a prisoner who participated in a work-release program, failed to report back to prison in the evening; petitioner was thus listed as "escaped." Petitioner was later apprehended and was found guilty. At his sentencing hearing, the state introduced evidence of petitioner's prior convictions for two counts of aggravated assault, among other convictions. The trial court found petitioner to be a violent habitual felony offender, and sentenced him as such. Petitioner filed for review, arguing that the violent habitual felony offender statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 775.084(1)(b), was unconstitutional as applied to him. The court held that it was plausible for the legislature to have included aggravated assault in its list of felonies considered as violent and thus warranting enhanced sentencing. Moreover, there was nothing irrational about the statute's focus on an offender's prior record because the state was justified in enhancing an offender's present penalty of a nonviolent crime based on an extensive or violent criminal history. The statute was also held as being specific as to the requirements necessary for habitual offender status. The decision below was approved.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's affirmance of the enhancement of petitioner's sentence under a habitual felony offender statute was approved, because the statute was held to be constitutional. The court found that it plausible for the legislature to have deemed aggravated assault as a violent felony, that petitioner was a habitual offender, and that the statute was specific as to the requirements for a trial court's finding of habitual offender status.

Goodman v. Brasseria La Capannina


No. 78,246


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


602 So. 2d 1245; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1028; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 353



June 11, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fourth District - Case No. 90-2042. (Palm Beach County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landlord sought review of a decision from the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which found that Fla. Stat. ch. 83.12 was unconstitutional on its face because it violated the U.S. Const. amend. XIV guarantee to due process of the law. Appellant had filed suit against appellee tenant, alleging breach of a lease agreement.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landlord leased a restaurant to appellee tenant. After appellee failed to pay timely rent, appellant filed a two count verified complaint, and the trial court issued a distress writ pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 83.11 and 83.12 (1989). The sheriff served the writ on appellee, and appellee moved to exclude food and alcohol from the writ so that the restaurant could continue operation. The court denied the motion. On appeal, the district court found that Fla. Stat. ch. 83.12 was unconstitutional because it failed to provide discretion to the presiding judge. Appellant sought review, and the court reversed, finding that the statute was constitutional because it provided sufficient procedural safeguards to protect a debtor's interest. The statute provided for judicial authorization of the writ, for issuance of the writ only after the allegation of specific facts, for a bond to be posted, for an opportunity for the debtor to dissolve the writ, and for a prompt hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment holding that the statutory provision for a distress writ was unconstitutional, holding that the prejudgment seizure provided for by statute was constitutional because it complied with due process requirements.

 

363 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Maison Grande Condominium Ass'n v. Dorten


No. 78,197


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


600 So. 2d 463; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 981; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 325



June 4, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Third District - Case No. 90-529. (Dade County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Appeal, Third District, Dade County (Florida), certified a question following its judgment in favor of appellant lessor declaring Fla. Stat. ch. 718.4015 unconstitutional: Was an escalation clause in a condominium recreation lease that was entered into before 1975 enforceable after October 1, 1988, for the entire term of a 99-year lease, where the lessor had not agreed to be bound by future changes in the Condominium Act?


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the decision in which the lower court granted judgment to appellee lessor by expressly declaring Fla. Stat. ch. 718.4015 unconstitutional. The lower court certified the following question: Was an escalation clause in a condominium recreation lease that was entered into before 1975 enforceable after October 1, 1988, for the entire term of the 99-year lease, where the lessor had not agreed to be bound by future changes in the Condominium Act? The court answered in the affirmative. The retroactive application of the predecessor to § 718.4015 violated the contract clauses of the state and federal constitutions. A law was presumed valid until it was declared unconstitutional. Until ch. 718.4015 was declared unconstitutional, it was valid, and the escalation clause was void for public policy. Therefore, appellant condominium association's nonperformance of the escalation clause was excused. The award of attorney fees to appellee lessee was reversed because they resulted from an effort to have a law declared unconstitutional, and the parties' contractual provisions for payment of litigation costs did not include such costs or appeal costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part and observed that a law was presumed to be valid until it was declared unconstitutional. Therefore, appellant lessor's nonperformance of the escalation clause until a statute was declared unconstitutional was excused, and appellant was not liable for appellee lessee's costs and attorney fees associated with the action to have the statute declared unconstitutional.

Thompson v. State


No. 75,499


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


1992 Fla. LEXIS 997; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 342



June 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Vacated on Denial of Rehearing April 1, 1993, Reported at 1993 Fla. LEXIS 587. Substituted Opinion of April 1, 1993, Reported at 1993 Fla. LEXIS 587.
Vacated by, Substituted opinion at, Rehearing denied by Thompson v. State, 619 So. 2d 261, 1993 Fla. LEXIS 587 (Fla., 1993)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, S. Peter Capua, Judge - Case No. 76-3350-B
Thompson v. Dugger, 515 So. 2d 173, 1987 Fla. LEXIS 2296 (Fla., 1987)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), entering defendant's resentence of death following his convictions for first-degree murder, kidnapping, and involuntary sexual battery. Defendant claimed, inter alia, the trial court erred in admitting a witness's prior testimony, denying a motion to strike the jury panel, admitting defendant's prior inconsistent testimony, and in imposing the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions for first-degree murder, kidnapping, and involuntary sexual battery were upheld because a witness's prior testimony and defendant's prior inconsistent testimony were properly admitted, the jury panel was properly retained, the admission of victim photographs was harmless error, and the death penalty was properly imposed. Defendant pled to first-degree murder. The death penalty was imposed. Defendant appealed and argued that the trial court improperly rejected mitigating circumstances. The appellate court reversed and remanded for a resentencing. Defendant was resentenced to death. Defendant appealed. The state supreme court affirmed. The supreme court held that because plaintiff, the state, showed that the witness was unavailable, and defendant cross-examined her at a prior trial, the testimony was admissible. Because the state was rebutting a defense, use of defendant's prior inconsistent testimony was proper. The use of victim autopsy photographs was harmless error because other photographs supported the finding that the murder was committed in a cruel manner. Because evidence of a heinous murder existed, the death penalty was upheld.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed defendant's death sentence following his convictions for first-degree murder, kidnapping, and involuntary sexual battery. The admission of victim autopsy photos and the finding of premeditation were harmless errors because the evidence showed the murder was heinous. The use of prior testimony at a second trial was upheld because the witness was unavailable, and defendant cross-examined the witness at the prior trial.

R.J.A. v. Foster


No. 79,296


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


603 So. 2d 1167; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 999; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 327



June 4, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied September 23, 1992. Released for Publication September 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Certified Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Hillsborough County, Edgar Hinson, Vincent E. Giglio and Florence Foster, Circuit Court Judges, Case Nos. 91-4267 Div. C; 91-5620 & 91-5621 Div. B; 91-5383 Div. B; 91-4769, 91-4954, & 91-4955 Div. B; 91-6204 Div. B; 91-6080 Div. B; 91-4968 Div. B; 91-5609 Div. B; 91-2515 Div. C; 91-5504 Div. B; 91-6006 Div. B; 91-6002 Div. B; 91-5962 Div. B; 91-6481 Div. B; 91-4999 Div. B; 91-4812 Div. B; 91-5846 Div. B; 91-4417A Div. B; 91-8809 A-I Div. B; and 91-7991 A-D & 91-7992 AB Div. B - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Second District, Case Nos. 91-03810 thru 91-03826; 91-03848 92-00184 & 92-00185


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner juveniles brought a writ of prohibition in the Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) claiming that Fla. Stat. ch. 39.048 (1991) granted them an absolute substantive right to be tried within 90 days. Petitioners alleged that Fla. R. Juv. P. 8.090, which allowed the state an extra 10 days to bring petitioners to trial, did not apply. Petitioners sought dismissal of their cases because they were not tried within the statutory period.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner juveniles' cases were not dismissed because Fla. R. Juv. P. 8.090 took precedence over the speedy trial statute, Fla. Stat. ch. 39.048 (1991), and no speedy trial violations occurred. Petitioner juveniles' delinquency cases were scheduled for adjudicatory hearings beyond the statutory speedy trial period. Petitioners brought motions to dismiss. The trial court denied the motions. Petitioners brought a writ of prohibition, alleging that the statute created a substantive right and that the procedural rule violated the state constitution's separation of powers clause. The district court certified the cases to the supreme court. The supreme court denied the writ, holding that the speedy trial statute was merely a triggering mechanism that created a presumption of prejudice. Violation of the statute alone did not per se prejudice a juvenile's ability to defend himself or herself. Because the legislature did not intend to expand a juvenile's speedy trial right, the supreme court concluded that the procedural rule took precedence over the statute. Thus, dismissal was inappropriate where the savings clause of Fla. R. Juv. P. 8.090 applied.


OUTCOME: The supreme court denied petitioner juveniles' petition for a writ of prohibition and upheld the trial court's denial of their motions to dismiss their juvenile delinquency petitions with prejudice. A procedural savings rule applied and no speedy trial violations occurred. A violation of the statute alone did not per se violate a juvenile's rights. The right was a procedural one that did not enjoy a higher level of constitutional protection.

In re Forfeiture of 1985 Ford Ranger Pickup Truck


No. 78,456


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


598 So. 2d 1070; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 879; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 290



May 14, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. First District - Case No. 89-03063. (Bay County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District (Florida), which reversed the trial court's decision holding Fla. Stat. ch. 932.703(2) (1989) to be unconstitutional and found that, although the state could proceed against the forfeited truck, it was not entitled to take the property of one who did no wrong and knew no wrong.


OVERVIEW: The co-owner of a truck that was seized by the police challenged the seizure, claiming to be an innocent owner pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 932.703(2) (1989). The trial court declared the statute unconstitutional. The district court reversed but held that, although the state could proceed against the truck, it was not entitled to take the property against the truck, it was not entitled to take the property of one who did no wrong and knew no wrong. On application for review of the decision of the district court, because of direct conflict of decisions, the court concluded that the district court had correctly applied the principle of statutory construction. The state could secure forfeiture of the interest of the person involved in criminal activity, but ch. 932.703(2) was to be interpreted to protect the interest of innocent co-owners from forfeiture. The court approved the decision under review and disapproved the holding in that an innocent co-owner's interest in property was forfeited along with the guilty co-owner's interest.


OUTCOME: The court approved the district court's decision that, although the state could proceed against the forfeited truck, it was not entitled to take the property of one who did no wrong and knew no wrong.

Ragsdale v. State


No. 72,664


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


1992 Fla. LEXIS 498; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 174



March 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Vacated on Denial of Rehearing October 15, 1992; Substituted Opinion of October 15, 1992, Reported at 1992 Fla. LEXIS 1799.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Wayne L. Cobb, Judge - Case No. 86-00091CFAES


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of his convictions of first-degree murder and armed robbery and the imposition of the death penalty in the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate sought review of his convictions of first-degree murder and armed robbery and the imposition of the death penalty. In affirming, the court determined that the trial court did not err in limiting appellant's voir dire by prohibiting him from questioning potential jurors as to their willingness to sentence appellant differently than a codefendant found to be equally or less culpable, since appellant's counsel had sufficient latitude to question the jurors to obtain fair and impartial jurors. Likewise, the court found the trial judge did not err in imposing the death sentence when the sentencing jury indicated that appellant was less culpable than codefendant sentenced to life imprisonment. The court held that the trial court's responses to jury questions did not result in the jury's not knowing it could consider the codefendant's sentence as nonstatutory mitigating evidence during the penalty phase. The jury instructions, coupled with the closing arguments by both parties and the nature of the questions asked by the jury, indicated that the relative culpability of the codefendant was in the minds of the jurors and properly considered in recommending the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions and sentences, including the imposition of the death penalty, holding that the limitations on appellant's voir dire and comments by the trial judge in response to the sentencing jury's questions did not constitute error since the record reflected that the jury appropriately considered the relative culpability of appellant's codefendant in making its sentencing determination.

Nelms v. State


No. 77,602


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


596 So. 2d 441; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 500; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 164



March 12, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. Fourth District - Case No. 90-1312. (Palm Beach County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an appeal from the decision of the Fourth District Court, Palm Beach County (Florida), which denied the petitioner's postconviction relief, found that the petitioner did not raise the issue at trial or on direct appeal, and that petitioner's defense counsel could not be held responsible for subsequent changes in the law.


OVERVIEW: The petitioner was charged with first-degree murder. A county administrative order divided the county into two separate districts for the purpose of drawing petit juries. The petitioner filed a pretrial motion to dismiss the indictment because the grand jury had not been summoned from the same geographical area as the petit jury. Several years later, the court determined that the county administrative order was unconstitutional because it systematically excluded a significant portion of the black population. The petitioner sought postconviction relief but the trial court denied relief. The petitioner filed an appeal. The court held that had the petitioner failed to raise the issue of the constitutionality of the jury pool at trial and on direct appeal, he would not be entitled to relief. The petitioner's statutory challenge to the grand jury could not be equated to the constitutional claim regarding petit jury selection upon which relief was previously granted. The court approved the decision of the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court approved the decision of the lower court denying the petitioner's postconviction relief because defense counsel could not be held ineffective for failing to anticipate a change in the law.

Patten v. State


No. 74,318


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


598 So. 2d 60; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 505; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 172



March 12, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 10, 1992. Released for Publication June 10, 1992.
Writ of certiorari denied Patten v. Florida, 507 U.S. 1019, 123 L. Ed. 2d 448, 113 S. Ct. 1818, 1993 U.S. LEXIS 2605 (1993)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Patton v. State, 784 So. 2d 380, 2000 Fla. LEXIS 1895 (Fla., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Frederico A. Moreno, Judge - Case No. 81-19702



DISPOSITION: For the reasons expressed, we affirm the trial court's imposition of the death penalty.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, death-row inmate, challenged the imposition of the death penalty in a second sentencing hearing before the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, death-row inmate, challenged his sentence of death imposed in a second sentencing proceeding. In affirming, the court rejected appellant's contention that Florida's death penalty procedure was unconstitutional because it did not require the sentencing jury to report in detail what decisions it reached with respect to each of the aggravating and mitigating circumstances. The court determined that no constitutional or statutory requirement mandated the use of a special verdict form in death penalty cases. The court also held that the prosecutor's references to the victim as a police officer were not improper and did not deny appellant due process in his sentencing proceeding, since this information was a part of the factual situation and was critical for the state to establish the aggravating circumstance of hindering the enforcement of laws under Fla. Stat. ch. 921.141(5)(g)(1981). The court found appellant's claim of prejudice in the instruction of the jury with regard to similar aggravating factors was without merit because the instruction did not have a doubling effect. The court summarily rejected appellant's remaining claims as without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's imposition of the death penalty against appellant, holding that appellant was not deprived of a fair sentencing hearing and that appellant's claims of error were without merit.

 

370 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Fla. Ass'n of Counties v. Dep't of Admin., Div. of Ret.


No. 77,850


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


595 So. 2d 42; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 276; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 154



March 5, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions. First District - Case No. 90-2071. (Leon County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners filed an application for review of the decision of the District Court of Appeal, First District, Leon County (Florida), wherein the district court upheld the constitutionality of 1988 Fla. Laws ch. 88-238, which provided increased retirement benefits for special risk members of the Florida Retirement System. In upholding the statute, the district court construed Fla. Const. art. X, § 14.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed 1988 Fla. Laws ch. 88-238, which funded increases in the retirement benefits of special risk members of the Florida Retirement System. It provided for the increased benefits in five steps and required that public employers make increased contributions for each of the corresponding increases in benefits. Petitioners sought a declaration that chapter 88-238 was unconstitutional as an improper exercise of the taxing and spending power of the state under Fla. Const. art. X, § 14. The district court upheld the constitutionality of chapter 88-238. It also construed Fla. Const. art. X, § 14. Petitioners filed an application for review. The issue was whether the legislature was able to constitutionally enact a law providing for five consecutive annual retirement benefit increases and require the governmental unit responsible to fund each increase in the year in which it was implemented. The supreme court adopted the opinion of the district court. "Sound actuarial basis," as contained in art. X, § 14, meant that a retirement program was to be funded in such a way that the retirement fund was able to meet its continuing obligations as and when they matured.


OUTCOME: The supreme court approved the decision of the district court that upheld the constitutionality of the session law that provided increased retirement benefits for special risk members of the Florida Retirement System. It found that the district court made a proper and thorough analysis of the issues and reached a proper resolution of the issues. The supreme court adopted the opinion as its own.

Amendments to Rules Regulating the Fla. Bar-1-3.1(a) Etc


No. 74,538


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


598 So. 2d 41; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 209; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 121



February 20, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied June 1, 1992. Released for Publication June 1, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding - Rules Regulating The Florida Bar and Rules of Judicial Administration


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Report of the Florida Bar/Florida Bar Foundation Joint Commission on the Delivery of Legal Services to the Indigent in Florida was before the court for consideration of recommendation number 24, which involved pro bono legal services.


OVERVIEW: The Florida Bar/Florida Bar Foundation Joint Commission on the Delivery of Legal Services to the Indigent in Florida (Commission) submitted a report on the legal needs of the poor for the court's consideration. In recommendation number 24, the Commission recommended that attorneys be required to participate in 20 hours of voluntary pro bono legal services annually or make a monetary contribution. The recommendation also suggested reporting requirements to ensure lawyers' compliance. The court initially noted that one purpose of courts was the protection of individual rights. The court reasoned that the availability of lawyers was essential to ensure the protection of constitutional rights. Next, the court thought that the government should pay for some indigent representation, and some representation should be pro bono. The court adopted recommendation number 24 with some modifications.


OUTCOME: The court concluded that recommendation number 24 on the subject of pro bono legal services in the Report of the Florida Bar/Florida Bar Foundation Joint Commission on the Delivery of Legal Services to the Indigent in Florida was a beginning step in meeting the legal needs of the poor, and approved it with some modifications.

 

372 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dixon


No. 78,563


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


594 So. 2d 295; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 233; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 102



February 13, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Polk County, Susan Wadsworth Roberts, Judge, Case No. GCG1988-2410 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Second District, Case Nos. 90-01618 & 90-01619


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Second District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified a trial court's opinion that Fla. Stat. ch. 61.181(5) violated Fla. Const. art. VII, § 10.


OVERVIEW: Appellee clerk of court filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment that Fla. Stat. ch. 61.181(5) violated Fla. Const. art. VII, § 10. Appellee argued that the statute required his office to disburse funds representing payments made to a domestic relations depository account before the account received payment of those funds. The trial court entered judgment for appellee, stating that the statute pledged public credit without a definitive public purpose. Appellant state government challenged the decision. The court found that the statute was not a pledge of public credit because there was no public liability incurred when appellee disbursed support payment checks before receiving payment on those funds. The depository account contained sufficient funds to disburse support payments paid by personal check. The legislature established a trust fund that could reimburse returned checks paid for child support. The court further found that the legislature acted pursuant to the strong public purpose of providing spouses and children with prompt support payments. The court held that the statute was valid and constitutional. The case was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: A state statute outlining the disbursement of support payments was constitutional because it was not a pledge of public credit without a definitive purpose where the legislature acted pursuant to strong public purpose in providing spouses and children with support payments.

 

373 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Coy v. Fla. Birth-Related Neurological Injury Comp. Plan


No. 76,565


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


595 So. 2d 943; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 210; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 104



February 13, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 22, 1992. Released for Publication April 22, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity. First District - Case Nos. 89-2569 & 89-2593. (Leon County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner physicians challenged a decision from the First District Court of Appeal (Florida), which held that Fla. Stat. ch. 766.314 did not violate due process or equal protection, was not an impermissible delegation of legislative authority, and met the standards for tax statutes.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner physicians, practicing in areas other the obstetrics, filed an action against respondent, an entity created as part of medical malpractice reform legislation. Respondent administered a no-fault system to insure against certain types of neurological injuries suffered by infants at birth. To fund respondent, all physicians were required to pay a mandatory annual assessment. Petitioners argued that the assessments against them were unconstitutional because they derived no benefit from it greater than did the general public. A trial court and an appellate court rejected petitioners' claims. On appeal, the court found that the assessment under Fla. Stat. ch. 766.314 was a tax because the assessment was levied upon physicians to support a governmental enterprise. The court concluded that there was a rational basis for the statutory assessment of all physicians, even though they did not practice obstetrics. Ensuring the availability of obstetrical services benefited all physicians, including petitioners, to a greater degree than the general public benefited. The court held that Fla. Stat. ch. 766.314 was constitutionally valid, and approved the lower court's decision.


OUTCOME: The lower court's decision that upheld the constitutionality of the statute which created respondent compensation plan was approved because there was a rational basis for assessing fees from petitioner physicians to ensure the availability of obstetric services.

376 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Herrera v. State


No. 78,290


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


594 So. 2d 275; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 183; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 84



February 6, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 90-00583. (Palm Beach County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida) certified the question of whether Fla. Std. Jury Instructions 3.04(c)(2) (Crim.) and Fla. Stat. ch. 777.201(2) (1989) unconstitutionally shifted the burden to the defense to prove entrapment. The district court affirmed petitioner's convictions for trafficking in cocaine and obstructing an officer on the ground that the current standard instruction on entrapment was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: After a sting operation, petitioner was charged with trafficking in cocaine, conspiracy to traffic in cocaine, and obstructing an officer. Petitioner raised entrapment as an affirmative defense and asked the trial court to give the former standard instruction on entrapment, which stated that respondent state had the burden of showing beyond a reasonable doubt that a defendant was not entrapped. Instead, the trial court gave the current instruction, which stated that a defendant had the burden of showing by a preponderance of the evidence that he was entrapped. Petitioner was convicted of the trafficking and obstruction charges. The lower court affirmed and certified the question of whether Fla. Std. Jury Instructions 3.04(c)(2) (Crim.) and Fla. Stat. ch. 777.201(2) (1989), both applicable to offenses after 1987, unconstitutionally shifted the burden to the defense to prove entrapment. The supreme court answered the certified question in the negative and approved the lower court's decision. The supreme court held that the allocation of the burden to petitioner was not unconstitutional because it did not lessen the respondent's burden of proving every element of the offense charged.


OUTCOME: The supreme court answered the certified question in the negative and approved the district court's decision. The supreme court ruled that petitioner's constitutional rights were not violated because the jury instruction's new method of allocating the burden of proof did not lessen respondent state's burden to prove every element of the charged offenses.

 

377 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Leapai v. Milton


No. 76,241


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


595 So. 2d 12; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 104; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 61



January 23, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 27, 1992. Rehearing Denied March 27, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fifth District - Case No. 89-415


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant seller appealed from the judgment of the Fifth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which (a) reversed an award of attorney's fees made under Fla. Stat. ch. 45.061 (1987), after summary judgment was entered against plaintiff motorist, following his rejection of defendant's settlement offer in an insurance subrogation action, and (b) ruled that § 45.061 violated the judiciary's rule-making authority under Fla. Const. art. V, § 2(a).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff motorist's insurer paid his claim for damage to his vehicle resulting from an accident with another car. Thereafter, on behalf of his insurer, plaintiff brought a subrogation action against the other driver and defendant seller, whom he thought was the owner of the other car. Defendant was granted summary judgment on evidence that she had sold the car to the other driver two months before the accident. Defendant was also awarded attorney's fees, pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 45.061 (1987), because plaintiff had rejected defendant's earlier offer to settle for one dollar. The appellate court reversed, upon ruling that § 45.061 violated separation-of-powers principles in that its procedural provisions encroached upon the judiciary's rule-making authority under Fla. Const. art. V, § 2(a). Defendant appealed. In reversing, the court ruled that § 45.061 was constitutional because the objectionable procedural provisions were superseded by Fla. R. Civ. P. 1.442. In addition, the procedural aspects of § 45.061 were severable from the substantive right under the statute to recover attorney's fees and costs.


OUTCOME: The judgment denying attorney's fees was reversed because the statute under which the award was made was not an unconstitutional encroachment by the legislature upon judicial authority, even though it had procedural aspects, since those procedural aspects were superseded by judicial rule and were otherwise severable from language creating a substantive right to recover attorney's fees and costs.

Hodges v. State


No. 74,671


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


595 So. 2d 929; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 105; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 74



January 23, 1992, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Rehearing Denied April 20, 1992. Released for Publication April 20, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County, John P. Griffin, Judge - Case No. 89-2165 Trial Div. II


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court in and for Hillsborough County (Florida) that convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his first-degree murder and sentence of death on many grounds. In the guilt phase the court allowed two detectives to testify, over objection, that the victim was adamant about prosecuting appellant for indecent exposure. Appellant argued that what the victim thought and said about prosecuting him was inadmissible hearsay. Appellee State of Florida argued that the statements were used to prove that appellant had a motive to kill the victim. The court agreed that the statements were hearsay but found the admission to be harmless error. The court found the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction and affirmed the conviction. Appellant argued that during the penalty phase, the court should have halted the proceedings and conducted a competency hearing rather than ruling that appellant had absented himself voluntarily and continuing. The court found that prior to the suicide attempt, appellant's conduct gave no indication that his competency might be of concern, and his attempted suicide surprised everyone connected with the case. Thus, there were no reasonable grounds to question his competency. The court affirmed the sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence for first-degree murder because the evidence was sufficient to support appellant's conviction and it was not error to continue in the penalty phase without appellant present.

In re Forfeiture of 1969 Piper Navajo


No. 77,076


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


592 So. 2d 233; 1992 Fla. LEXIS 6; 17 Fla. L. Weekly S 9



January 2, 1992, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] An Appeal from the District Court of Appeal - Statutory or Constitutional Invalidity. Fourth District - Case No. 89-1282. (Broward County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the judgment of the Fourth District Court of Appeal (Florida), which dismissed appellant's petition for forfeiture of appellee's aircraft, found to contain equipment that violated Fla. Stat. ch. 330.40 (1989).


OVERVIEW: Appellee's aircraft was seized by authorities pursuant to appellant state's law prohibiting possession of extra fuel tanks that did not comply with federal aircraft regulations. However, appellee argued that appellant's law mandating forfeiture of such a non-complying aircraft was unconstitutional. Examining the statute at issue, the court first held that the statute's prohibition of additional fuel tanks that did not comply with federal regulations was a constitutional exercise of appellant's police power in preserving public safety. However, the court held that requiring the forfeiture of such noncomplying planes exceeded appellant's police power because the punishment was not sufficiently narrowly tailored to the objective of flight safety. The court reasoned that, in light of the state constitution's protection of property rights, the statute at issue was unreasonable. As a result, the court upheld the trial court's decision dismissing appellant's petition for forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The judgment dismissing appellant state's petition for forfeiture of appellee's aircraft was affirmed because the statute allowing forfeiture was unconstitutional.
