Advisory Opinion to Atty. Gen.-Ltd. Political Terms Etc


No. 78,647


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


592 So. 2d 225; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 2159; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 779



December 19, 1991, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Advisory Opinion to the Attorney General


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Attorney General petitioned for an advisory opinion on the validity of an initiative petition providing for limited political terms for certain elective offices. The court permitted interested parties to file briefs on the validity of the proposed amendment.


OVERVIEW: A constitutional amendment was proposed regarding term limits for certain elective offices and the Attorney General petitioned for an advisory opinion on the validity of the initiative petition. The court permitted interested parties to file briefs on the validity of the proposed amendment. Petitioner concluded that the proposed amendment met the single-subject requirement of Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3, and the ballot title and summary requirements of Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161. On review, the court held that the proposed amendment met the single-subject requirement because it had a logical and natural oneness of purpose. The sole subject of the proposed amendment was limiting the number of consecutive terms that certain elected public officers could serve. The court held that although the proposed amendment affected officeholders in three branches of government, that fact alone was not sufficient to invalidate the proposed amendment. Further, there was no existing constitutional provision that imposed a different limitation on terms of office.


OUTCOME: The court held that the proposed amendment was valid because it met the single-subject requirement and had a logical and natural oneness of purpose in that the sole subject of the proposed amendment was limiting of the number of consecutive terms that certain elected public officers could serve. Although the proposed amendment affected three branches of government, that was not sufficient to invalidate the proposed amendment.

 

381 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Weir v. State


No. 77,091


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


591 So. 2d 593; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 2127; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 749



November 27, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Rehearing Denied January 28, 1992. Released for Publication January 28, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance. Fourth District - Case No. 90-2680. (Broward County)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a case concerning the admissibility of a dying declaration against petitioner, the District Court of Appeal, Fourth District (Florida), certified the question of whether a district court of appeal had certiorari jurisdiction to review an order granting a defendant's motion in limine filed prior to trial but not actually ruled on until trial commenced, where such order posed potentially irreparable harm to the state.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed a pretrial motion in limine to prohibit introducing and referring to a declaration, claiming that the victim's statement did not qualify as a dying declaration. At trial, the judge excluded the declaration because he found the statute authorizing admission of dying declarations unconstitutional. During a temporary recess, respondent state filed its petition for certiorari to the district court and obtained a stay of the trial. On remand from the district court the trial resumed, using the dying declaration, and petitioner was acquitted. Hence, petitioner had no personal interest in the review. The court found that the district court did not have jurisdiction to take the action that it did, and the court declined to extend the right of certiorari to rulings in criminal cases made after jeopardy had attached even though such rulings were predicated on motions filed prior to trial, thus answering the certified question in the negative. The court found that the trial judge wrongly excluded the dying declaration, and wrongly found the law allowing such evidence unconstitutional, and adopted the district court's discussion on the law of dying declarations.


OUTCOME: The court quashed the decision under review but approved of its holding on the merits. The court answered the certified question in the negative and declined to extend the right of certiorari to rulings in criminal cases made after jeopardy had attached even though such rulings were predicated on motions filed prior to trial.

 

382 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Schmitt v. State


No. 76,317


Supreme Court of Florida


590 So. 2d 404; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1990; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 731



November 14, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Statutory Validity; Fourth District - Case No. 89-0187; (Martin County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal to affirm his conviction for possession of depictions known to include sexual conduct by a child under Fla. Stat. Ann. § 827.071(5) (1987) after a search revealed nude photos and videos of defendant's daughter. Defendant claimed that the search warrant was invalid because the affidavit that supported it was facially insufficient to support a finding of probable cause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled no contest to a charge that he violated Fla. Stat. Ann. § 827.071(5) (1987), which prohibited possession of any depiction known to include sexual conduct by a child, after police officers who executed a search warrant found nude photos and videos of defendant's daughter. Defendant then appealed his conviction, claiming that the search warrant was invalid because the affidavit that supported it was facially insufficient to support a finding of probable cause. The district appellate court and the state supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction. The supreme court held that the affidavit created a substantial basis for the magistrate who issued the search warrant to conclude that probable cause existed for a belief that defendant violated § 827.071(5). The affidavit indicated that defendant did not treat the nudity of himself or his daughter in the offhand, natural manner that might be expected if his conduct were innocent, but that defendant's conduct tended to show a lewd intent, which was prohibited under the statute. As a result, the affidavit created a substantial basis for believing that the search would yield evidence of a violation of § 827.071(5).


OUTCOME: The state supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of depictions known to include sexual conduct by a child after a search revealed nude photos and videos of his daughter. The court held that the search warrant was valid because the affidavit, which showed that defendant's conduct tended to show a lewd intent, created a substantial basis for believing that a search would yield evidence that defendant violated the law.

Davis v. State


No. 76,640


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


589 So. 2d 896; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1900; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 713



October 31, 1991 


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication January 23, 1992.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 23, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County, Major B. Harding, Judge - Case No. 82-4752-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant death row prisoner sought review of a decision from the Circuit Court in and for Duval County (Florida), which, without an evidentiary hearing, denied appellant's second motion for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellant death row prisoner killed a woman and her two young daughters in their home. He was convicted of first-degree murder, and the lower court imposed three death sentences. After the governor signed appellant's death warrant, appellant filed his first postconviction motion. The lower court denied the motion and the state supreme court affirmed the denial. Appellant's petition for writ of habeas corpus was also denied because it contained unexhausted claims and constituted an abuse of the writ, but the appellate court reversed for consideration on the merits. On remand the petition was dismissed and appellant was directed to exhaust his Hitchcock claim or to refile the petition without that claim. Appellant then filed his second petition for postconviction relief, which was denied by the lower court. On appeal, the state supreme court affirmed, holding that the lower court properly found that appellant's Hitchcock claim had no merit and that the other issues raised by appellant, concerning ineffective assistance of counsel and the impropriety of sentencing instructions, were procedurally barred because they had been previously raised.


OUTCOME: The decision from the lower court, which denied appellant death row prisoner's second motion for postconviction relief, was affirmed. The state supreme court held that appellant's Hitchcock claim had no merit and that the other issues he raised were procedurally barred because they had been previously raised.

Chiles v. Children a


No. 78,792


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


589 So. 2d 260; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1902; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 708



October 29, 1991 


NOTICE:

 [**1]


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Dade County, Henry G. Ferro, Judge, Case No. 91-46672 CA (13) - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, Third District, Case No. 91-2530.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant administration commission members brought a direct appeal from the decision of the Dade County Court (Florida) that granted declaratory and injunctive relief holding Fla. Stat. ch. 216.011(1)(ll) and 216.221 to be unconstitutional. Appellants were enjoined from attempting to restructure 1991 Fla. Laws ch. 91-193, § 1, pursuant to the budget reduction procedure established in Fla. Stat. ch. 216.


OVERVIEW: Appellee foster children sought declaratory and injunctive relief against appellant administration commission members. The action stemmed from the state's determination of a general revenue shortfall in the budget requiring state agencies to prepare revised financial plans reducing their current operating budgets. The trial court granted appellees' request, held Fla. Stat. ch. 216.011(1)(ll) and 216.221 to be unconstitutional, and enjoined appellants from attempting to restructure an appropriations act, 1991 Fla. Laws ch. 91-193, § 1, pursuant to the budget reduction procedure established in Fla. Stat. ch. 216. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that the statutes, Fla. Stat. ch. 216.011(1)(ll) and 216.221, were unconstitutional as a violation of the doctrine of separation of powers because the statutes were an impermissible attempt by the legislature to abdicate a portion of its lawmaking responsibility and to vest it in an executive entity, resulting in the powers of both the legislative and executive branches lodged in one body. This concentration of power was prohibited by the tripartite system of constitutional democracy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of declaratory and injunctive relief and the trial court's order holding that the budget reduction procedure statutes were unconstitutional as a violation of the doctrine of separation of powers based on the delegation of the legislative function to the executive branch because the state constitution specifically provided for the state legislature alone to establish fiscal priorities.

Cruse v. State


No. 74,656


Supreme Court of Florida


588 So. 2d 983; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1864; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 701



October 24, 1991 


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication January 13, 1992.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 13, 1992.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, John Antoon, II, Chief Judge - Case No. 87-1763-CF-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which convicted appellant of first-degree murder and numerous lesser offenses arising from the killing of six people and the injuring of 10 others. Sentences of death were imposed on appellant for two of the murders.


OVERVIEW: Criminal appellant procured an assault rifle, shotgun, pistol, and ammunition. He then went on a shooting rampage, killing six people, including two police officers, and injuring 10 others. Appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and numerous lesser offenses. He was sentenced to death for killing the two police officers. Appellant claimed that a new trial was necessary based on trial errors. The court affirmed the convictions because the state's failure to disclose psychiatric evidence did not violate appellant's due process rights because the experts had not interviewed appellant or formed an opinion about his sanity. Also, the trial court did not err by refusing to allow cross-examination of a state expert based on immateriality, and the insanity jury instruction was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for murder and lesser offenses because the trial court did not err by failing to allow cross-examination of the state's expert witness or surrebuttal evidence based on relevancy. The state's psychiatric evidence was properly not disclosed because it was immaterial. Therefore, the trial court did not abuse its discretion and a new trial was unnecessary.

Williams v. Campagnulo


No. 76,593


Supreme Court of Florida


588 So. 2d 982; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1714; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 663



October 10, 1991 


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication December 6, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 6, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Application for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Direct Conflict of Decisions; Fourth District - Case No. 89-1467; (Broward County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner dentist sought review of the decision of the Fourth District Court of Appeal, Broward County (Florida), which reversed summary judgment in favor of petitioner in a medical malpractice action and remanded the case to the trial court with instructions that respondent patient was allowed to amend his complaint to allege that notice was filed pursuant to Fla. Stat. ch. 768.57(3)(a) (1985).


OVERVIEW: The court quashed the appellate court's decision and remanded the action with directions to reinstate the trial court's judgment. Respondent patient filed suit against petitioner dentist alleging medical malpractice, but respondent failed to file the notice required by Fla. Stat. ch. 768.57(3)(a) (1985). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of petitioner. The appellate court reversed and remanded with instructions to allow respondent to amend his complaint to allege compliance with the notice requirement. On review based on a conflict of decisions, the court found that compliance with the pre-filing notice of ch. 768.57 was a condition precedent to maintaining an action for malpractice and, while it may be complied with after the filing of the complaint, the notice must be given within the statute of limitations. The court rejected respondent's argument that the notice requirement was procedural and, as such, was an unconstitutional invasion of the court's exclusive rule-making authority. The statute was intended to address a legitimate legislative policy decision related to medical malpractice actions and to promote settlement of meritorious claims at an early stage.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's order reversing the grant of summary judgment to petitioner dentist in a medical malpractice action was quashed, and the cause was remanded for reinstatement of summary judgment to petitioner because the pre-filing notice requirement was a condition precedent to maintaining a medical malpractice action. The court rejected respondent patient's argument that the notice requirement was procedural and unconstitutional.

 

387 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Bedford v. State


No. 73,703


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


589 So. 2d 245; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1743; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 665



October 10, 1991 


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication December 9, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied December 9, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Broward County, Mel Grossman, Judge - Case No. 88-424-CF-10-B.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Broward County Circuit Court (Florida), convicting him of kidnapping and first-degree murder and sentencing him to consecutive life and death sentences, respectively, upon the finding of three aggravating factors and no mitigating factors, even though the jury recommended a life sentence only.


OVERVIEW: A dead woman was found nude with her hands bound by duct tape, which also covered her mouth and neck. When defendant was questioned by police, he initially denied any involvement, but later said the woman was killed accidentally when he tried to loosen tape that her boyfriend and his employer had put around her neck during sex. At trial, he claimed the woman accidentally died because of erotic sexual asphyxia during consensual sex with defendant. A pathologist testified that the victim's injuries were consistent with both erotic sexual asphyxia and strangulation. Defendant was convicted of kidnapping and first-degree murder. Despite the jury recommending life imprisonment, he was sentenced to death for the murder, upon a finding of three aggravators with no mitigators, with a consecutive life sentence for the kidnapping. Defendant appealed. In affirming the convictions and the kidnapping sentence, the court ruled, inter alia, that they were supported by substantial credible evidence. In vacating the death sentence, the court ruled that it was improper to override the jury's recommendation because it had a reasonable basis, given mitigating evidence that was presented.


OUTCOME: Both convictions and sentence for the kidnapping were affirmed because, inter alia, they were supported by competent substantial evidence, to the exclusion of defendant's claim of accidental death, and the life sentence was not improper. The death sentence was reversed because the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment had a reasonable basis in the record, which the trial court could not properly override.

Ponticelli v. State


No. 73,064


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


593 So. 2d 483; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1742; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 669



October 10, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 9, 1992.
Released for Publication March 9, 1992. Rehearing Denied March 9, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Fla. LEXIS 470.
Rehearing denied by Ponticelli v. State, 1992 Fla. LEXIS 470 (Fla., Mar. 9, 1992)
Vacated by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Ponticelli v. Florida, 506 U.S. 802, 113 S. Ct. 32, 121 L. Ed. 2d 5, 1992 U.S. LEXIS 4948 (1992)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ponticelli v. State, 2006 Fla. LEXIS 1855 (Fla., Aug. 31, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Marion County, Raymond T. McNeal, Judge - Case No. 87-2719-A-W.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the convictions of first-degree murder and sentences of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court in and for Marion County (Florida) that convicted appellant of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant shot two people in the head. One of the victims was struck several times in the head with the butt of the gun and driven around with his head pushed down on the hot floorboard. Appellant was convicted for first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Appellant sought review of the judgment on twelve grounds. The court found that several of the grounds lacked merit or had already been rejected by the court. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in finding him competent to stand trial because one of the three experts appointed to examine him testified that in his opinion appellant was incompetent. Although this doctor testified that appellant was not competent to stand trial because he suffered from delusional thought processes, two other doctors testified that appellant was competent. The court concluded that it was the trial court's responsibility to resolve disputed factual issues. The record contained sufficient evidence to show that appellant understood the charges against him and could assist in his defense. The court affirmed appellant's convictions and sentence. The court did not abuse its discretion when it ruled on the issue of competency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellant's conviction for first-degree murder and sentence of death because the record contained sufficient evidence that appellant understood the charges against him and appellant's other contentions were without merit.

Sireci v. State


No. 76,087


Supreme Court of Florida


587 So. 2d 450; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1626; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 623



September 19, 1991 


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication November 4, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 4, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Orange County, Gary L. Formet, Sr., Judge -- Case No. CR76-532.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Orange County (Florida), which imposed the death penalty upon defendant in a resentencing hearing subsequent to convicting defendant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant was originally sentenced to death for a murder he committed, a new sentencing hearing was ordered. However, defendant received the death penalty in the second sentencing hearing as well. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in refusing to waive the jury sentencing recommendation. The court noted that the trial court implied it would lessen its reliance on the jury's recommendation if it found the recommendation was improperly influenced by knowledge of defendant's prior death sentence. As a result, the court upheld the refusal to waive the recommendation. The court then held the prosecution's reference to defendant's prior death sentence was improper, but was inadvertent and its impact was negligible, because the jury likely knew of the earlier sentence. Thus, the court held the trial court did not err in refusing to grant a mistrial for the statement. Reviewing the record, the court also held that the trial court acted within its discretion in refusing to apply the mitigating factors argued by defendant because the evidence did not clearly support the application of the factors. Thus, the court upheld imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: The imposition of the death penalty in defendant's resentencing hearing was affirmed because the trial court's refusal to apply statutory mitigating factors argued by defendant was not erroneous.

Klokoc v. State


No. 74,146


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


1991 Fla. LEXIS 1520



September 5, 1991 


NOTICE:  [*1] Released for Publication November 27, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 27, 1991. Revised Opinion Reported at 1991 Fla. LEXIS 2130.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Edward M. Jackson, Judge - Case No. 88-4009-CF-A.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida) convicting him of first degree murder and imposing the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant killed his nineteen-year-old daughter while she slept, in order to spite his estranged wife. Appellant pleaded guilty to the first degree murder of his daughter and waived his right to a jury for the penalty phase. Moreover, appellant refused to allow his counsel active participation on his behalf in the penalty phase and refused to cooperate or allow counsel to present evidence by family members in mitigation. In imposing the death sentence, the trial judge concluded that the one aggravating circumstance outweighed the mitigating circumstances. On appeal, the court vacated appellant's death sentence because it was disproportionate to other sentences imposed where the murders resulted from domestic disputes. The court concluded that the mitigating factors in the record were not outweighed by the one statutory aggravating factor and that proportionality required the court to reduce appellant's sentence to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for twenty-five years.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's sentence of death, holding that the mitigating factors were not outweighed by the one statutory aggravating factor and that proportionality required appellant's sentence be reduced to life imprisonment.

Klokoc v. State


No. 74,146


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


589 So. 2d 219; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 2130; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 603



September 5, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised September 5, 1991


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Edward M. Jackson, Judge - Case No. 88-4009-CF-A

Original Opinion of September 5, 1991, Reported at 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1520.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court, Brevard County (Florida) convicting him of first degree murder and imposing the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant killed his nineteen-year-old daughter while she slept, in order to spite his estranged wife. Appellant pleaded guilty to first degree murder and waived his right to a jury for the penalty phase. Moreover, appellant refused to allow his counsel active participation on his behalf in the penalty phase and refused to cooperate or allow counsel to present evidence by family members in mitigation. In imposing the death sentence, the trial judge concluded that the one aggravating circumstance outweighed the mitigating circumstances and imposed the death penalty. On appeal, the court vacated appellant's death sentence because of the mitigating circumstances. Applying the principle that the reasons present in one case will reach a similar result to that reached under similar circumstances in another case, the court determined that the one statutory aggravating factor did not outweigh the unrefuted mitigating factors. Thus, the court reduced appellant's sentence to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for twenty-five years.


OUTCOME: The court vacated appellant's sentence of death, holding that the one statutory aggravating factor did not outweigh the unrefuted mitigating factors when compared to other death penalty decisions.

Wright v. State


No. 71,534


Supreme Court of Florida


586 So. 2d 1024; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1528; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 595



August 29, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 30, 1991. Rehearing Denied October 30, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for St. Lucie County, Dwight L. Geiger, Judge - Case No. 86-1546-CF.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court, St. Lucie County (Florida), which convicted appellant of first degree murder, burglary, and battery on a police officer and sentenced appellant to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, convicted of first degree murder, burglary, and battery on a police officer, argued that appellee state, during jury selection, unconstitutionally exercised a peremptory challenge for racial reasons. The court agreed, ruling that appellee's challenge of a venire member who was black, because he might identify with a black defendant, was unjustifiable. The challenge's alternative basis, that the venire member shared no eye contact with appellant, was pretextual. Moreover, it was reversible error for the trial court to deny appellant's motion to sever the murder and burglary charges from the battery charge because the latter was not episodically connected to the former and involved different victims, offenses, dates, places, and circumstances. Also, the consciousness-of-guilt from flight instruction given to the jury during the trial's guilt phase was improper in the absence of supporting evidence. Finally, the court's override of the jury's recommendation of life imprisonment was error, for reasonable mitigating factors--alcohol abuse and remorse--supported this recommendation, and the court ruled that double jeopardy barred imposition of the death penalty on retrial.


OUTCOME: Judgment convicting appellant of murder, burglary, and battery on a police officer, and sentencing him to death, was reversed and remanded because peremptory challenge of venire member was racially based, because severance of murder and burglary charges, from the battery charge, was required for episodically unconnected charges, and because override of recommended life sentence was improper given the reasonable basis for jury's recommendation.

Dep't of Law Enforcement v. Real Property


Nos. 77,308, 77,309, 77,310, 77,311, 77,312


Supreme Court of Florida


588 So. 2d 957; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1256; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 497



August 15, 1991 


NOTICE:  [**1] Released for Publication December 2, 1991.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Dismissed Voluntarily December 2, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Five Cases Consolidated - Direct Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Levy County, Benjamin M. Tench, Judge, Case Nos. 90-383-CA, 90-253-CA, 90-252-CA, 90-251-CA, and 90-250-CA - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case Nos. 90-3811, 90-3812, 90-3813, 90-3814, and 91-23.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law enforcement challenged an order from the Trial Court in and for Levy County (Florida) in which the court declared that the Fla. Contraband Forfeiture Act, Fla. Stat. §§ 932.701-.704 (1989), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A man was arrested on drug trafficking charges stemming from a reverse sting operation conducted by appellant law enforcement. The state immediately initiated forfeiture proceedings in circuit court against certain properties including a 60-acre tract of land, an R/V mobile home subdivision of more than 40 acres, an entire 280-acre subdivision, an entire 100-acre platted subdivision, and a personal residence and property including garages, sheds, and other improvements. Claimants sought to dismiss the forfeiture petitions on constitutional grounds, and the lower court held that the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act (the Act), Fla. Stat. §§ 932.701-.704 (1989), was unconstitutional. The supreme court reversed and held that the Act was constitutional provided it was applied consistent with the minimal due process requirements of the Fla. Const. The court explained the procedures needed to satisfy due process, which were also consistent with the language and intent of the Act. As for the merits of the case, the state had not complied with due process. It seized real property, including residential property prior to giving the claimants any notice or opportunity to be heard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order declaring the Florida Contraband Forfeiture Act (Act) unconstitutional and held that the Act was constitutional, provided it was applied consistent with the minimal due process requirements of the Fla. Const.

Espinosa v. State


No. 73,436


SUPREME COURT OF FLORIDA


589 So. 2d 887; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1062; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 489



July 11, 1991, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Revised.
Rehearing Denied November 27, 1991, Reported at: 1991 Fla. LEXIS 2105.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Dade County, Arthur I. Snyder, Judge - Case No. 86-19790-A


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court in and for Dade County (Florida), convicting and sentencing defendant for first-degree murder, second-degree murder, attempted murder, grand theft, and burglary. The trial court denied defendant's motion to sever trial from that of his codefendant and denied his motion for witnesses' expenses.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant was convicted of first-degree and second-degree murder, attempted murder, grand theft, and burglary. He was tried together with his codefendant. The state introduced evidence concerning the commission of the murders in the victims' home. Victims' daughters testified that they recognized defendant's voice because he had been their neighbor. Both defendants were found guilty and sentenced. The appellate court affirmed the judgment, holding that defendant was not entitled to severance from codefendant because he was not prejudiced by any testimony admitted. The state did not enter codefendant's confession, and evidence of codefendant's history of violent behavior was inadmissible. Also, defendant's motion for witnesses' expenses was properly denied because he did not prove experts would be of assistance.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's murder, theft and burglary convictions, along with his sentences. The motion to sever his trial from that of codefendant was properly denied because no evidence was introduced that could not have been introduced against defendant and his codefendant if either had been tried alone.

In re Advisory Opinion to Atty. Gen.-Homestead Valuation Limitation


No. 77,506


Supreme Court of Florida


581 So. 2d 586; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1015; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 472



July 3, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Proceeding - Advisory Opinion to the Attorney General - Homestead Valuation Limitation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court issued an advisory opinion to the attorney general regarding the validity of an initiative petition, circulated by a corporation, for a constitutional amendment regarding homestead valuation.


OVERVIEW: A court issued an advisory opinion to the attorney general regarding the validity of an initiative petition circulated by a corporation. The court permitted briefs to be filed by interested parties and heard oral arguments on the subject. The initiative petition sought to add a homestead valuation limitation to Fla. Const. art. VII, § 4. The court found that the provision complied with the single-subject requirement under Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3, which provided that a proposed amendment had to have a logical and natural oneness of purpose. The court next had to determine whether the proposed ballot title and substance complied with Fla. Stat. ch. 101.161, which required that the ballot and title had to be fair and advise the voter sufficiently to enable him to intelligently cast his ballot. Although the court stated the ballot summary could have been drafted more broadly to explain the increase in homestead property valuation, overall the summary fairly reflected the chief purpose of the proposed amendment. Therefore, the court found the initiative petition and proposed ballot summary met the requirements of Fla. Const. art. XI, § 3 and Fla. Stat. ch. 101.16.


OUTCOME: The court found that the initiative petition and proposed ballot summary met the state statutory requirements. The initiative petition for a constitutional amendment regarding homestead valuation complied with the single-subject requirement and the proposed ballot title and substance was fair and enabled a voter to intelligently cast a ballot.

 

397 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Abdala v. World Omni Leasing


Nos. 75,966, 75,968


Supreme Court of Florida


583 So. 2d 330; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 1049; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 464



June 27, 1991 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Two Consolidated Applications for Review of the Decision of the District Court of Appeal - Certified Great Public Importance; Third District - Case No. 89-1769 & 89-2803; (Dade County).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases petitioner lessees sought review of the decisions of the Third District Court of Appeal, Dade County (Florida) that granted summary judgment to respondent lessors and held that Fla. Stat. ch. 324.021(9)(b) (1987), which concerned a long-term motor vehicle lessor's financial responsibility for the operation of that vehicle, was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: In consolidated appeals, the supreme court upheld the constitutionality of Fla. Stat. ch. 324.021(9)(b) (1987). Chapter 324.021(9)(b) provided that the lessor of a motor vehicle for a period in excess of one year was not liable under the dangerous instrumentality doctrine for damages resulting from the operation of that vehicle provided that the lessee maintained the requisite minimum insurance coverage. The court rejected petitioner lessees' contention that ch. 324.021(9)(b) was unconstitutional based on access to courts, equal protection, and due process violations. The statute did not irrationally distinguish between lessees injured by vehicles leased for a period in excess of one year and lessees injured by vehicles leased for a period of less than one year. The court found that there was a rational basis for ch. 324.021(9)(b), which simply redefined "owner" of a motor vehicle so as to exclude a long-term lessor upon satisfaction of the statutory preconditions. The statute did not discriminate against lessees suffering the worst injuries by eliminating possible recovery from the lessor in view of the unlimited ability to recover from the lessee.


OUTCOME: Summary judgments in favor of respondent lessors of motor vehicles were approved. Respondents were not liable under the dangerous instrumentality doctrine for damages resulting from the operation of leased vehicles because the lessees maintained the requisite minimum insurance coverage and had leased the cars for more than one year. The court found that the controlling legislation was constitutional.

Capehart v. State


No. 74,231


Supreme Court of Florida


583 So. 2d 1009; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 923; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 447



June 13, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication September 3, 1991. Rehearing Denied September 3, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal and Cross-Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County, Maynard F. Swanson, Jr., Judge - Case No. 88-394CFAES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment rendered by the Circuit Court in and for Pasco County (Florida) that convicted him of burglary and first-degree murder and the resulting sentences, including a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for burglary and first-degree murder and was sentenced to fifteen years for burglary and a death sentence was imposed for first-degree murder. Appellant sought review of the judgment on many grounds. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in permitting the Chief Medical Examiner to testify regarding the cause of death and the condition of the victim's body because she did not perform the autopsy, nor was the autopsy report admitted into evidence. Appellant contended that Appellee State of Florida failed to lay a proper foundation for her testimony. The court was satisfied that a proper predicate for her testimony was established because an expert, under Fla. Stat. ch. 90.704, could rely on facts or data not in evidence in forming an opinion if those facts were of a type reasonably relied upon by experts. The expert relied on several reports and photographs of the body. The court affirmed the convictions and sentence of death. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in sentencing him for burglary without regard to a sentencing guidelines scoresheet. The court agreed and vacated the sentence for burglary and remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for burglary and first-degree murder because expert testimony was properly admitted and defendant's other contentions regarding guilt were without merit. The court vacated the sentence for burglary and remanded because the sentence was not imposed based on a sentencing guidelines scoresheet.

Jennings v. State


Nos. 75,689 74,926


Supreme Court of Florida


583 So. 2d 316; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 932; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 452



June 13, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 20, 1991. Rehearing Denied August 20, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: An Appeal from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County, Charles Harris, Judge - Case No. 79-773-CF-A; and an Original Proceeding - Habeas Corpus.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court in and for Brevard County (Florida), which denied his motion for postconviction relief under Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850. Defendant also petitioned the court for habeas corpus relief based on failure to disclose exculpatory material and based on a claim on ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, kidnapping, sexual battery, aggravated battery, and burglary. His convictions and death sentence were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant filed a motion for postconviction relief pursuant to Fla. R. Crim. P. 3.850 which the trial court denied. Defendant appealed that order and also sought habeas corpus relief. The court affirmed the denial of postconviction relief and denied the petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant claimed that the prosecution failed to disclose a taped witness statement that supported defendant's claim of intoxication. The court said that defendant was aware of his own intoxication and was aware of evidence to support it. However, intoxication would not have been defense in the guilt phase of the trial and it was not a theory pursued by the defense. Furthermore, the withheld evidence was merely duplicative of other evidence of which defendant was aware. Counsel was not ineffective for choosing another theory of defense, identity, where the rejected theory would only have been relevant in the penalty phase of the trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion for postconviction relief and denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus because the exculpatory material that the prosecution withheld did not relate to the theory of defense pursued at trial and was duplicative of other evidence known to defendant. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to call all potential witnesses who would have duplicated other testimony given.

 

400 of 1586 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. Scanlan


No. 77,179


Supreme Court of Florida


582 So. 2d 1167; 1991 Fla. LEXIS 905; 16 Fla. L. Weekly S 427



June 6, 1991 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 13, 1991. As Corrected. Rehearing Denied August 13, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Direct Appeal and Cross-Appeal of Judgment of Trial Court, in and for Leon County, J. Lewis Hall, Judge, Case No. 90-3137 - Certified by the District Court of Appeal, First District, Case No. 90-3677.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The district court certified a case of great public importance seeking review of a case whereby the trial court held that amendments to the Comprehensive Economic Development Act of 1990 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee taxpayers and others and appellant various corporations and others disputed the constitutionality of amendments to the workers' compensation law. Appellees claimed that, because the cumulative effect of chapter 90-201 was to substantially reduce preexisting benefits to employees without providing any countervailing advantages, the workers compensation statute was no longer a reasonable alternative to common-law remedies and, therefore, violated the access to courts provision of the Florida constitution. The court rejected this claim. Although chapter 90-201 reduced benefits, the workers' compensation law remained a reasonable alternative to tort litigation. Appellees claimed that chapter 90-201 was facially unconstitutional because it violated the single subject requirement. Appellants contended that the workers' compensation and international trade subjects were logically related to the topic of comprehensive economic development. The court disagreed. The subjects were too dissimilar and lacked the necessary logical and rational relationship to the legislature's stated purpose of comprehensive economic development to pass constitutional muster.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that portion of the trial court's decision that declared chapter 90-201 facially unconstitutional for the single subject violation and that portion of the decision that rejected the contention that chapter 90-201 unconstitutionally denied access to courts. The court reversed the remainder of its decision.
